O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	You, three sons, I have fulfilled this book that is behind the science of medicine, the fulfillment of it, and made the end through its exposures and by its declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to my vision that I have fulfilled this book with this surgery, which is part of the work of hands, it is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is forbidden in our region and is rejected in every way, if it is perceived by science and knowledge, and there is nothing more to do than the small descriptions in books that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And this has led to the error and vanities, and the intentions are closed and science is alienated.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	I seem to think that I will revive this by assembling the order of this cauterization according to the way of exposure and declaration and abbreviation; and I will assemble the forms of the sharpeners of the cautery, and other instruments of the work with the alignment of the declaration and preparation of it, as it is their craft.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And because no one of the hands masters is found in our hands, the art of medicine is extended.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And it is necessary for him who enters the science of anatomy, as Galen says, to know the judgment of the members, and their forms and conjunctions and separations of the parts, and to have knowledge of the bones, the nerves, the muscles and the number of joints, and the movement and rest of the limbs, and the issue of the same.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	1. For this reason, Iophras says that the non-with-the-non is not with the will, and with the body it is rare; and at the same time in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	1. In the introduction of this book, we say that those who are not acquainted with things as they should be, if they do not want to make mistakes and do not disturb men, have often more times lost this science and abandoned it for lack of knowledge and experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	1. For I see a foolish man who cuts off the crown of an abscess or the neck of a woman, and cuts the arteries of the neck; because so much blood is lost that the woman dies in her hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And see I another case where a wound of an old man was infected, and the wound was large; if it was removed with a piece of the bladder, and he died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	I had not yet been called to treat this wound, and I saw the position of the patient and the size of the wound, and if it was not cut well, he died.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And see I another case where the Duke of our land had a broken leg, and with the splint it was plated; the patients were ignorant and forced the break on the plate as soon as possible, and did not leave any part of the bone uncovered, and they finished it; the command was that he should not remove it; but it took a long time until the leg was completely healed and the bone was lost.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I am called to come to him, and I hurried to come remove the leg; and when I dislocated it if it was not in pain and did not feel any pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the way to the corruption of the member was confirmed or the member, and could not be healed; and the corruption did not cease by the member as long as the member was completely lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And see another reason why it will fall and be enchanted, and then burned by the malice of his lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For chancre, when it is free of melancholic matter, only one thing can be done if it is not in its entirety the part that can be completely cured of what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And for this reason, thrice-woven threads, you should know that handwork is divided into two divisions: it is knowledge, whether or not there is risk in other dispositions; and I will show you in each chapter of this book where there is danger and risk.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	If you do not keep them in order, so that the folk may not speak ill of you. Take your weapons in hand, and use your remedies lightly but firmly, and choose the best way if by God's grace you come to salvation and become wise; and leave behind the unwholesome diseases of grief; and keep your arms from what makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you may come from this world to another with glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen's admonishes in none of his prescriptions: "Do not take medicine for the treatment of sick people, lest you be called foolish.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have heard this treatise is discussed in three chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapter is about fire cauteries and medicinal cauterizations, and it is ordered from the head down to the feet; as well as forms of strangulations and incisions, and all that is necessary in the work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter is about cutting and piercing, and ventouses and wounds, and the extraction of arrows, and similar things; and it is ordered and the forms of strangulations.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter is about restoring dislocations and twists, and similar things; and it is ordered by the surgeon's hands, and the forms of the instruments.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	However, if we remember our work, it is necessary that I give the quality of the aid and no less for each complexity.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of the aid and no less is the longest word and subtlest science and the secret reposition; and for this they speak more of the wounds, and agree to this; and they are not much in their words, because I repeat the length.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that cauterization is useful for all complexions, where it has matter, and that is to know the hot complexion with matter, and the dry complexion with matter.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions, some say that cauterization is of no use at all and that it is great help; while others say the opposite: that cauterization is only useful for diseases that come from chlorine and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be curative for hot diseases caused by chlorine, nor for dryness; and that is what those who say the opposite mean, that cauterization is great help for hot and dry diseases that come from the courage of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you perceive the chest of the patient and its moisture on the complexion of fire, you must quickly close the chest.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it once by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all ways, it does not mix with anything but those who have experienced it and know by long use the chapter of cauterizations, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of their diseases, and their symptoms and spasms; other complexions do not have our fear, in fact in cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And then they are supposed to fit together and agree with the cauterization.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	Understand, children, that cauterization is a fire if it contains secrets of healing, and even more beneficial than fire medicine.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For the fire is simple, and only comes to harm to the member it is cooked in, and does not hurt other members.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	Fire medicines come from one part of the body to another, and bring diseases of grief to health; and by chance the patient often has fire because of its high quality and the goodness of its substance, if it does not cause harm, if there is no excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	1. And I found this in my research through experiment and the length of service and study I have given to the art, and it is true; and for this I excuse the length of the word, as I only wish to reveal the secret which is hidden or fire, and the quality of the work, as it treats the diseases of the body, just as the philosopher says in demonstrating; and you should receive it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	1. Know, son, that the burns should be made in certain ways and not too tightly.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	1. I say that cauterization is allowable in all tightnesses, because the wounds are not always misplaced by the aid of cauterization; and moreover, if the cauterization is for necessary pains and hurts that cannot wait for the tightness that greatest malice comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	For do not think that the cautery is a remedy for all diseases; for the disease that is healed by cautery has no return; and he says so; but it is not easy if one does not know how, because cauterization is only a medicine that dries up the complexion, and dries up the humors that cause pain, and is worthy of medicine for its courage, and for its virtue in its work and its chivalry.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	And there is something that the disease does not return any time according to the complexion of the patient and the lesion of the disease and its virtue; and they are assembled in him the superfluities by the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cauterization is administered to him or he has little superfluity and moisture, as cauterization does for pain, and the similar things, and part of the pain does not return; but this is rare.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And many people do not understand that cauterization is a part of medicine, and this is seen; but they only believe that cauterization is after medicine, but we understand it is false, and cauterization is part of medicine because when we know ways to cure in any disease and they are not effective, then we administer our cauterization and it is effective.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	However, it is well understood that cauterization is part of medicine, even if some do not agree with this.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancients said that gold-tipped cauterization was as harmful as iron, and they said this was due to the quality of the gold and its high substance. They said that gold cauterization does not cause any poisoning, but it is not true, and I have experienced it, and I found that it is true in some men; and gold cauterization is as good as iron, as they say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	When you hold the gold instrument, you do not know how much it is heated by the color of gold, and when it has cooled down; if it is heated too much, it will burn; and then it is enough to prevent it.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And that's why we use fire cauterization in our work because we have already used it.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or if you have ordered this chapter of the small joints, because it is easier to find.
dou cautere olivaire	oil cauterization
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	oil cauterization is useful for moisture and cold in the eye socket, and when it is caused by a disease called "soda", and by many humors that descend to the small joints as the ears, and the ears, and by numerous sleeps and tooth pain and throat pain, and even by all diseases that come from cold, such as paralysis, apoplexy, and semblances of diseases.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cauterization is as follows: if the patient is purged by solvent medicine modifying the head III or IV, according to which virtues and age and customs of the patient he can bear; then I make another head for the patient.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the palm tree root between the other's palm roots between its II fingers; and if you come to your two hands, bleed a little and wash the cauterization called "olive" which is formed like this:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And place the sign of ink on the leg, and make it descend and pull your hand back a little by a little; then relax your hand, and if you see the bone I said is small; and if you don't see it, the cauterization resumes as long as you see the bone as I told you; then take the pouch of silk, and soft cotton, and place on the leg, and let it stay for three days; then put a moist cloth on it until the burn is healed; then cure the wound with the ointment called "tetrafarmaçon" as long as it is healthy.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And they would say to the ancient one, that as the wound becomes more sunken, it purges more; and this is why it helps to relieve the pain.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And none of these say that too much fatigue is needed for the cauterization, but rather part of the bone should be burned, and then what is burned is removed, and it is treated.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And they say that the cauterization should be done with too much fatigue, and it must be driven in so hard that it penetrates as far as the vertebrae that women put in their hoofs because the humors flow out; and then it must be relieved for a long time over the wound; after that, it must be treated and dressed.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	1. These two methods of cauterization do not seem less effective in total, whether for any man or woman who fears pain; and I think it is better to leave them, as the head of the shoulder is often injured by continuous natural solutions, as we have experienced in other parts; and even when the head of the shoulder is weak by nature, the first appearance of cauterization seems more safe and gentle to me, and I use it accordingly.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	1. of the ancient pain of the head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	1. When the entire head is afflicted with chronic pain that lasts long, and it must use the drugs called "cochie" and pills, as well as purging of the head and oils and plasters; and if the cauterization is done as we have described before, and it does not work.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	The patient's head is severely injured, and it cannot be moved; therefore, the cauterization of that part is done as we have described earlier.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After cauterizing each eye of the patient's head as we have described, and then cauterizing the legs called "vassels"; and they are the ones where ventouses are placed; and hold your hand so that you do not see the bone: the patient feels much more pain in this cauterization than in others, and I will explain further; and it is necessary that the cauterizations of the eyes be more subtle than those of the chief's foot, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	For in one part of the pain, it is extended to the entire body, and the head is expelled due to the oil, and the patient is purged with medicines that are changed, and the other cures I mentioned in the division of diseases are not effective: therefore, I made the cauterizations according to two methods, which is to say, with hot medicine and iron.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	If you apply a dose of ointment containing alum, and scrape and sew the wound, and then make the temple where the pain holds in such a way that you can replace the dose of ointment; and when it is replaced, if the lie and the eye are well held and left for 12 hours; and then the dose of alum is removed and the plaque is left for 2 or 3 days; then pour cold water on it as much as possible until the wound is healed.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the healing of the wound as soon as it is healthy; and if you see that there are no such medicines as I have written or treated of cureless medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The iron burn is according to this method.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the iron burner in this way:

Se tu viens au comencement dou cautere jusc’a l’os, si serait bien.	If you come to the beginning of the fire cautery on the bone, it would be good.
Se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere encor une fois, et autre se tu en as mestier, et le laisse III jors; aprés i met sus coton moilliet en burre, et lou cure de l’oignement desiccatif tant qu’il soit sanez, et se XL jors passent qu’il ne soit sanez, si met sus medicine ague corrosive tant que li os soit descovers; et lou reis selonc ceu que il venrait en son chapistre.	If not, then resume the fire cautery again and as many times as you can, and let it lie for three days; then put cotton wool on it, and the ointment desiccating as long as it is dry, and when 40 days have passed and it is dry, if put an acrid medicine on the bone until it is exposed; and follow according to what comes in your chapter.
Et i a une maniere de cautere de fistule que aucun des anciens dirent.	And there is a way of cauterization of fistulas that no of the ancients said.
Entens a fistule, et fens le leu; aprés met en la fendure I camahan subtil de coi ci est li forme:	Understand the fistula, and then put in the forceps the small piece of copper; after that make a subtle cut of it so that its form is.
et i font a la quantiteit d’une .З. de plonc; et tien ta main ou camahan fermement, et ne se mueve li malaides nes point, que li plons fondus ne corre a son oil; et covient c’on mette sus l’oil a malaide coton moilliet en abin d’uefz ou en awe: li plonc si art lou leu de fistule, et lou saine per mervillouse saniteit.	And they make it to the size of a zinc piece; and hold your hand on the forceps firmly, and do not move the patient at all until the ploncs melt and stick to the oil; and it is necessary to put the oil on clean cotton wool in the abscess or in the wound: the ploncs if they are good for the fistula, and the patient will be healthy.
Et se li fistule est sanee per le cautere que nos avons dit, c’est boin.	If the fistula is healed by the fire cautery we have described, that is good.
Se ce non, si covient aministrer pertus au neif, et ramener la fistule au cors dou neif selonc ceu qu’il covient en som propre leu.	If not, then it is necessary to administer physick to the umbilicus, and to bring the fistula back to its proper place according to what is appropriate for the patient's own belly.
des crevaices en levres	cracks in the lips
Mout de fois avienent crevaices en levres que sont apelees «poil», et meismement en levres des enfans.	Many times cracks in the lips are called "cracks" and also in the lips of children.
Quant tu cures ces crevaices de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et li cure ne profite, adonques eschaufe I petit cautere cultellaire selonc ceste forme:	When you treat these cracks as we have described in divisions, and the cure does not help, then use a small fire cautery according to this form:
Et le met hastanment en celles crevaices tant qu’il viegne jusc’a font; aprés cure le leu de cerote tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is placed in those cracks as much as possible, after healing the limb with a splint until it is healthy.
de l’aposteme de la goule	Of the abscess of the groin
Quant apostume vient en la racine de la goule ou en l’uve, ou ou palais, ou as racines des dens, aprés fait porriture et ront et est enveillis et devient fistule; et tu le cures si com nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne profite mie: adonques covient il que tu aies I cautere selonc la quantiteit de la fistule; aprés le bote ou pertus de la fistule, et tien ta main tant que li fer chaus viegne au font de li, et ou derrien leu; et fai ensi une fois ou II, aprés le cure de ce que nos avons dit en cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il est curez ensi, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si covient descovrir le leu et oster l’os corrumput, selonc ceu que vos le troverez en son chapistre.	When an abscess in the groin comes out through the root or the urethra, or the teeth, or the roots of the teeth, and it becomes ulcerated and forms a fistule; and you treat it as we have said in divisions, and it does not profit: therefore, it is necessary that you cauterize according to the size of the fistule; after the bite or rupture of the fistule, and hold your hand as long as the fire stays at the edge of the wound, and if it goes into the limb; and then make once or twice, after the cure of what we have said in the cures, as soon as it is healthy; and if it is cured once or twice, it is good; and if not, it is necessary to uncover the limb and open the corrupted bone, according to what you will find in your work.
dou movement des dens	The first line of the translated text is "For the fire
Quant les gencives sont mollifies par moistor et les dens muevent, et tu le cures per medicines et ceu ne vaut, adonc met le chief dou malaide en ton sain; aprés eschaufe le cautere dont li forme venra ci aprés en teil maniere que tu mettes une cainne sor le dent; et met dedens le cautere chaut hastanment, et tien tant ta main que li malaides sente la chalor venant a la racine dou dent; aprés lieve ta main et rencomence le cautere selonc ta volenteit; aprés emplisse li malaides sa bouche d’awe salee, et la teigne une houre et raiche fuers.	For the gums are softened by moisture and the teeth move, and you treat them with medicines if necessary, and then place the heated iron in your mouth; afterwards wash the cauterization that was formed in this way after it comes out in a manner similar to putting a nail in a hole; and pull out the teeth with the iron hot, and hold your hand tightly so that the patient feels the pain coming from the root of the tooth; afterwards gently release your hand and continue the cauterization according to your will; afterwards fill the patient's mouth with bitter-tasting stuff, and paint it once an hour and rinse it thoroughly.
Et en teil maniere li dens qui estoit movans si est confermez, et li gencive mollifie restrainte, et li moistors corrumpue sechie.	And in part, if the teeth that were moving are confirmed, and the gum becomes soft and restrained, and the moisture is dried out.
de la dolor des dens	of the pain of the teeth
Quant dolor de dens vient por froidor, ou il i a froidor ou veir, et les cures de medicine ne valent, adonc i ait mestier de cautere selonc II manieres: et cautere de burre et cautere de feu.	When pain in the teeth comes from coldness, or if it is cold or visible, and the remedies of medicine are ineffective, then it has a duty to cauterize according to two ways: cauterization with brimstone and cauterization with fire.
Cautere de burre si est telz que tu preignes burre de vaiche, et le bout en une cuillier de fer ou d’arain; aprés pren coton et envolope sus la pointe d’une tente, et la moille en burre bulit, et met sus le dent dolant hastanment et tien tant qu’il soit refroidiez; et ensi fai sovent tant que sa vertus viegne a la racine de la dent, et se tu vues si moille laine et coton en burre froit, et met sus le dent doillant, et met sus I fer chaut tant que li feus viegne au chevement dou dent.	Cauterization with brimstone if it is such that you burn brimstone of wool, and the end in a iron or steel pincer; then take cotton and wrap it around the point of a toothpick, and melt the brimstone, and place it on the painful tooth and hold as long as it is cold; and often I do this until the virtue reaches the root of the tooth, and if you see that the wool and cotton are burning in brimstone, and place it on the painful tooth and put a piece of iron charred as much as the fire reaches to the end of the tooth.
Li cauteres ensamble feu si est telz que tu preignes uns cainne de fer ou d’arain, et soit grosse si que li feus ne viegne a la bouche dou malaide; aprés chaufe le cautere, de coi li forme venra ci aprés, et le met sus le dent et tien ta main tant que li cauteres soit refroidiez; fai ceu sovent, car li dolor sera ostee celui jor meisme ou l’endemain.	When the fire cautery is very hot, such that you can burn a piece of iron or lead, and it is large so that the flame does not reach the patient's mouth; then heat the cauterization tool, and form it as follows, and place it on the tooth and hold your hand until the cautery is cool; do this often, because the pain will be tolerable for you or the next day.
Et covient que li malaides emplisse sa bouche de boin burre en l’empressement de cel cautere, et puis le raiche fuer; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	It is necessary that the patient fills their mouth with hot water in the pressure of this cauterization tool, and then it heats up; and this is the form of the cauterization tool:
Et fai cautere dou queil chief que tu voudras, et selonc ceu que tu as pooir; et c’est li forme de la caine:	I make a cut of the part you want, according to what you can bear; and this is the form of the scalpel:
des scrophules	of scrofulous lumps
Quant les scrophules sont de fleume et de moistors froides, et ne sont obeissans a digestion par medicines, adonques eschaufe le cautere cheveit de coi ci aprés vient li forme, et ait II aovertures por les fumees a issir au cautere de l’autre partie; et met le cautere chaut sus l’apostume une fois, ou II se mestier est, tant qu’il viegne au font de l’apostume; et se li apostume est petis si met cautere selonc la quantiteit de l’apostume, et le laisse ensi III jors; et met sus coton moilliet em burre tant que li arsure soit ostee; aprés cure le leu d’oignemens et de tentes tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the scrofulous lumps are soft and cold, and do not respond to digestion with medicines, then shave the scalpel blade as soon as the form appears, and make two openings for the fumes to escape from the other part; and place the scalpel on the abscess once, or as it may be, until it reaches the end of the abscess; and if the abscess is small, then cut according to the amount of pus, and leave it for three days; and press with cotton wool in a burette as soon as the wound is clean; after that, cure the wound with ointments and poultices as soon as it is healthy.
Li forme de la cainne:	The form of the collar:
Quant les moistors vainquent sus les chenals dou pormon, et meismement quant ce vient de froide complexion, adonc covient que li malaides soit voidiez premiers par medicines solutives; aprés li fai cautere a la racine de la gorge, et te garde que tu ne venir mie jusc’a la gorge, et n’ardre dou keur mais c’un poc.	When moisture reaches the ear holes, and even when it comes from cold complexion, it is necessary that the patient be treated with soluble medicines first; then I make a fire cautery at the root of the neck, and keep you from coming too close to the head, and do not burn the ear but only a little.
Aprés li fai I autre cautere a la jointure dou col au chief de l’espinee, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» de coi nos avons la forme devant; et cure le leu si com nos avons devant dit tant qu’il soit sanez.	After that, I make another fire cautery at the joint of the neck and head of the spine, and it is called "clavicle"; and treat the limb as we have said, as soon as it is healthy.
de la toust	Of the whole
Quant tous et maladie de pormon sont de moistors froides, et li malaides nen ait fievre ne sechor, et est li maladie anciaine, se li fai ij cauteres sus la forcele en leus vuis; et I autre cautere emmi le pis entre II mameles; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «clavile» selonc la forme qui est devant dite.	When all the symptoms of the disease are cold and moist, and the patient has no fever or thirst, it is an ancient disease, and I made two cauterizations on the sides; then the cauterization called "clavicle" according to the form mentioned earlier.
Et se tu vues, fai cautere en poignant a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins» de coi li forme est ci devant en la maladie des oreilles; et soient li poins jusc’a XXX, ou enqui entor.	And if you see, make cauterization by pricking all the cauterization called "points" in the form mentioned earlier in the disease of the ears; and let the points be as far apart as possible, or as close together.
Aprés cure le leu selonc ceu qui est devant dit, et soit li cauteres a III rains selonc ceste forme:	After treating the limb according to what is mentioned earlier, and let the cauterization be at three points according to this form.
Et por ceu sont li cautere plus legier, por ceu que tu en fais III a cop.	And for this reason, the fire cautery is lighter, because you make it three times a day.
de la dislocation de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Quant li chiés de l’ajutoire est desaloiez par cause de moistor, et on le remet a leu, et il n’i puet demorer ains revient adés et desalue par petit movement qui avient, si com nos avons esproveit, adonques covient il que tu ramoinnes la dislocation premierement.	When the head of the shoulder is dislocated due to moisture, and it is reset but cannot stay in place, repeatedly dislocating with slight movement as we have experienced, then you must first reset the dislocation.
Aprés soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos et sus son costeit; aprés lieve le keur qui est dedens le titillite as dois de ta main senestre; et se li jointure est desaluee dedens, si eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners douqueil ci est li forme:	After soaking the patient's back and chest; after easing the pressure on the titillate, use your left hand; and if the joint is dislocated, you must first loosen the cautery that has two strings like this:
et cauterize lou keur tant qu’il le perce jusc’a costeit, et venrait li fugure dou cautere ensamble IIII cauteres; et por ceu est faite cautere avec le cautere qui a III ners, por coi li figure de cauterization sunt sis cauteres; et sont li nerf selonc la subtiliteit d’une tente et c’est li forme dou cautere qui a III ners:	1. And cauterize the skin as much as it can be pierced, and it will come out with four burns; and this is done with a cauterization iron that has three points, because the figure of cauterization is six points; and these points are according to the fineness of a tent and are the form of the cauterization iron that has three points.
Et aucune fois est ajostez sus ce I nerf por coi il i a VIII cauteres.	2. And never has it been adjusted to this point because it has eight burns.
Aprés met sus le cautere porrelz broiez avec seil; aprés fai reposer le malaide, et ne soit meus li membres par lonc tens tant qu’il soit bien confortez.	3. After applying the cauterization iron with a hot iron, and after letting the patient rest, do not pull on the limbs as long as they are well comforted.
Et s’il est desaloiez desus, liquelz chose avient poc, adonques fait cautere sus l’epaisse dou cautere clavile, ou mout de cauteres en poignant.	And if it is dislocated, something comes out quickly, therefore a cautery is made on the thick part of the cautery clamp, or rather, the point where cauterization is pricked.
Car li jointure est refermee, et est ostee li moistor et est sanez li malaides.	For the joint is closed, and the moisture is removed, and the pain is eased.
Quant en l’estomac vienent froidures et mout de moistors tant qu’il l’estraient a sa complexion, et sont multipliet li catharre a lui, et es manieres de cures acostumees et il ne profite mie, adonc covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son dos, et estende ses jambes et ses mains.	When coldness and moisture come to the stomach, and they are drawn out of it as soon as possible, and the purges are given to it, and according to customary cures, but it does not improve, then it is necessary that the patient's back be soaked with water, and his legs and hands are extended.
De ceu en aprés li fai III cauteres I desoz la cuillier dou pis per la quantiteit d’un doi, a tout le cautere clavile, et II cauteres defuers les II costez tant que li figure des cauteres soit a III angles, et ait teil espaice entre l’une et l’autre qu’elles ne soient jointes ensamble quant elles giteront porriture; et soient li cautere si parfont qu’il porpreignent les II pars dou keur, et soit li figure des cauteres selonc ceste forme sens ajostement:	1. For this reason, I made three cauterizations on the thigh of the foot due to the quantity of a dose, at all cauterization points, and two cauterizations on the costals as much as the cauterizations look at three angles, and they should be spaced apart between one and another so that they are not joined together when they excrete feces; and they should be the cauterizations if they bent as much as the two parts of the knee, and the figure of the cauterizations should be according to this form without any change.
Et se tu vues cauterize d’un grant cautere enmi l’estomac selonc ceste forme; et celui qui avra paour de cest cautere, cauterize en poignant et seigne sus l’estomac i. point selonc la quantiteit que tu vues d’enche; puis le cauterize a tot le cautere qui est apelez «poins».	2. And if you see cauterization of a large cauterization in the stomach according to this form; and the one who suffers from this cauterization, should cauterize by touching and holding by the stomach at any point according to what you see of the quantity; then the cauterization is entirely over the cauterization called "points".
Aprés le cure de la cure que nos avons eut devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After the cure we had before, as long as it is healthy.
Quant au foie vient dolor de froit et de moistor et de grosse ventositeit, tant qu’il est fuer mis de sa complexion natureil per les superfluitez; et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en divisions, et il ne li profite mie, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus son haitereil; et signe d’enche III cauteres selonc ceste forme et ceste figure et ceste quantiteit sus lou foie, defuer les ypocondres, lai ou li coutes de l’ome vient; et ait d’espaice entre chaicun cautere la groissece d’un doi; et soient li cautere dou lonc dou cors, et ne presser mie mout ta main a tot le cautere; et soit arse tant soulement li moitiez dou keur, et soit li malaides drois sus ses piez; et s’il ne peut, si soit gisans, et estende ses jambes, et lieve ses brais; et c’est li forme:	When the liver has pain from frost and moisture and large vents, as long as it is healthy; and the patient is treated as we have said in divisions, and if he does not benefit, then the patient should be sewn up on his own will; and sign of encision III cauterizes according to this form and figure and quantity on the liver, defend the hypocandres, whether the cost of the stomach comes; and there should be space between each cauterization of a grower of one do; and they should be long and thin cauters, and not press too hard with your hand on the cauterization; and it should only be the half of the knee, and the patient should be laid on his side; and if he cannot, then it is better to be crooked, and extend his legs, and lower his head; and this is the form:
Et se ta volentez est, si cauterize ces cauteres dou cutellaire, se tu es subtilz et saiges en l’art, et te warde que tu n’ardes mie tout le keur, car tu feroies sechier tout le cors; et qu’il ne viegne jusc’a boueil, car li keurs est mout subtilz lai endroit, et lou saiches por voir.	If your desire is to cauterize these sharp cautery devices, if you are subtle and gentle in the art, and you wear a warrior's shield that does not burn the entire body, because you will dry all the flesh; and so it does not become muddy, because the hair is very delicate in every place, and you see to it.
Quant il a apostume au foie, et tu vues savoir s’il est en la char dou foie ou en la toile: s’il est en la char, se sent li malaides dolor ne mie trop fort; et s’il est en la toile, si sent dolor forsenee.	When it has become infected in the liver, and you see whether it is in the liver or on the cloth: if it is in the liver, it feels the pain of the physician too much; and if it is on the cloth, it feels pain suddenly.
Et lors quant ceste cure desoit les mires, si covient que li malaides soit sovinez sus sa teste; et puis seigne d’enche le leu ou li apostumes est, et puis chaufe le cautere qui est semblans au rais, de coi ci est li forme:	When this remedy is applied to the eyes, if the patient's head becomes dizzy; and then apply pressure to the eye or where it is swollen, and then heat the cautery that is similar to the raisin, depending on which part it is:
Et cauterize I cautere tant que li keurs soit ars, et viegne jusc’a syphac, tant que li porreture soit toute fuers; aprés la cure selonc la cure des essues tant qu’il soit sanez; et ne covient mie que de cest cautere use nuls fuers que cil qui ait estudieit longement en l’art de medicine, et par cui mains cestes maladies ont corrut aucune fois.	And cauterize the cauterization as much as the eye is burned, and it becomes softer, as long as the corner is all firm; after the treatment according to the treatment of the fluids as soon as it is healthy; and it is only necessary to use this cauterization with no other tools than those who have studied for a long time in the art of medicine, and by their hands these diseases have never been corrupted once.
Adonques puet il hardiement ovrer, et toutevoies il me semble que mues vaut li laissier.	Therefore, it is not possible to overcome it, and I believe it is better to leave it alone.
dou cautere de pleuresin	Therefore, it is not possible to overcome it, and I believe it is better
Li ancien dirent que on doit faire a pleuresin cauteres de racines d’aristologe, et en teil maniere: pren une racine d’aristologe longe, la plus grant que tu poras troveir, et soit seche, et soit ausi grosse et ausi longe comme tes dois; et la moille en oile, et l’emprens au feu, et cauterize I cautere entre la forcele et lou col, et II petis cauteres un poc en dessendant en la partie qui est desoz la barbe; et II cauteres entre la quinte coste et la sisime, en declinant derrier un poc; et I cautere emmi le pis, et I autre sus l’estomac, et I entre II espaules, et II as II costez dou pis defuers le cautere qui est entre II espaules; et ne presser mie ta main, ains fai apertement ausi com en odorant.	Therefore, it is not possible to overcome it, and I believe it is better to leave it alone. The ancients said that one must make cauteries with aristolochia roots, and in this manner: take a long aristolochia root, the longest you can find, and let it be dry and as large and long as your fingers; then grind it into oil, and heat it, and make a cauterization between the forceps and the collar, and two cauterizations in descending order in the part that is rough around the beard; and two cauterizations between the fifth ribs and the sixth, declining downwards on one pouch; and the cauterization at the pis, and the other at the stomach, and at the esparces, and the costals on both sides, deflecting the cautery that is between the esparces; and do not press too hard with your hand, but open it as you smell.
Et dirent aucun ancien que aucun home usent de cautere de feir semblant a I raseur, et l’eschaufent et le mettent entre les costes, tant qu’il vient a cel aposteme; et saut fuers li dolor, si com nos avons dit en l’aposteme dou foie.	And no ancient one has ever heard of anyone using a fire cautery like this, and they thrust it between the ribs, as soon as it reaches the abscess; and then there is great pain, as we have said in the abscess of the liver.
Mais en cestui ovraige est paour ou li malaides muert maintenant, ou fistule i vient qui ne puet estre sanee.	However, in this case, there is no pain or death for the patient, or fistula that cannot be cured.
de la mice	of the mouse.
Quant tu cures la maladie de la mice de ceu que nos avons dit as divisions des cures, et il ne profite mie, adonques i afierent III manieres de cautere que tuit sont boin.	When you treat the disease of the mouse as we have described, and it does not help, then there are three ways of cauterization that you should know.
Desquelz li une maniere si est que tu faices III cauteres, ou IIII, en lignant selonc la longor de la mice, selonc la figure dou cautere dou foie que nos avons dit devant; et n’apresser mie ta main a tout le cautere, et soit li malaides sovins sor son dos; et une autre maniere de cautere si est que tu eschaufe le cautere qui a II ners, si com nos l’avons mostreit en la dislocation de l’espaule; et lieve le keur qui est endroit la mice, ou li coutes dou malaide vient devers senestre, et soit li elevations dont tu lieves le keur selonc la keur, selonc la longesce dou cors, et li cautere soient selonc la largesce dou cors.	1. If you are doing three cauterizations or four, align them according to the length of the hairs, following the cauterization figure we mentioned before; do not press your hand on all the cauterization, and let the patient's arm rest on his back; another way of cauterization is if you scrape the cauterization that has two needles, as we showed in the shoulder dislocation; gently lift the hair that is where the hairs are, or the pain of the patient comes from the opposite side, and make the elevations according to the hair, according to the length of the chest, and the cauterization should be according to the width of the chest.
Aprés i boute les II ners enflamez tant que li keurs soit perciez de l’autre part, et puis trai fuers le cautere, et ensi en i avra IIII Et se tu vues, si cauterize a tot le cautere a III ners.	After the two nerves are inflamed as much as the knees can be felt from the other side, then perform the cauterization, and then insert it into the wound. And if you see, cauterize the entire cauterization with three needles.
Aprés le cure quant il a geteit porriture par lonc tens, et ce vaut mues que li autre des cures devant dites.	After the treatment when the patient has developed phlegm due to long tension, and it is necessary that the other treatments beforehand be said.
de ydropisie	of dropsy.
Cautere ne vaut a ydropique, fors c’a la maniere qui est apelee «asclytes».	Cauterization is not for dropsy, but in the way that is called "ascites.
Quant tu la cures selonc les manieres que nos avons dit en divisions, et ta cure ne profite mie, adonques covient il que tu li faices IIII cauteres entor la boude, et I sus l’estomac, et un sus le foie, et I sus la mice, et II derrier le dos sus l’espinee, et I endroit le pis; et soit li cauteres bien pres de l’espés dou keur.	When you treat according to the methods we have said in divisions, and your treatment does not profit, then it is necessary that you make four cauterizations entering the belly, and one through the stomach, and one through the liver, and one through the bladder, and two through the back near the spine, and one at the anus; and let the cauterization be well close to the spine of the knee.
Aprés laisse le cautere aovert por giter porriture lonc tens, et ne lassier mie la cure dou malaide aprés le cautere; et sanation se hasterait, et seront ensamble les II ententions avec l’aide de Deu.	After the fire cautery, let the patient drink long and thin broth, and do not neglect the care of the wounded patient after the fire cautery; then the healing will be swift, and the two instructions will be combined with the help of God.
Li forme dou cautere por le ventre soit li clavile que nos avons devant mostreit; et cil por le dos soit olivaire, selonc ceu qu’il est ci devant mis.	The form of the fire cautery for the belly is the clavicle that we have shown before; and for the back, it is olive-shaped, according to which it is placed before.
de l’enfleure des piez	of the wrapping of the arrows
Quant li piez sont enflez a celui qui est ydropique, et sont plain d’awe citrine, il covient que tu cauterizes sus le dos dou piet entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire; et lieve ta main avec le cautere sens torner.	When the arrows are wrapped with the hydropathic one, and are made of clear citrine, it is necessary to cauterize on the back of the arrow between the auricular and the urethral; and gently hold the cauterizing iron with the cautery so as not to turn.
Et n’entrer mie trop em parfont, ensi sarrait fuers li awe citrine, et soit li cauteres selonc cest forme:	And do not enter too much in front, otherwise it may be too rough for the awl, and let the fire cautery be according to this form:
Aprés fai sus II jambes II cauteres en chescune jambe a la pointe dou cutellaire; et soit li cauteres dou lonc, l’un desoz le genoil devant et l’autre defuers, enmi la jambe; et laisse les cauteres aovers longement sens curer, que li awe en isse; aprés le cure des autres cures que nos avons dit.	After making two cauteries on each leg at the pointed end, let them be long and one cut through the thigh in front and the other curves towards the leg. Leave the cauteries to heal for a long time before the awl can enter; after the cure of the other cures we have mentioned.
de la menoison	of the menstruation

de la cure des emorroydes	of the cure of the hemorrhages

de plaie mal curee	A wound that has not been properly treated
Quant li malaides ne puet soffrir tailleure ne overture, que nos raconterons en son leu, si vient teil maladie que ne puet estre sanee fuer que par cautere.	When the patient cannot endure tightness or opening, we will tell you about it in their own words, if they come to a serious illness that cannot be cured by cauterization.
Quant a aucun vient fistule, et est enveillie et giete porriture et moistors corrumpues, si la doies prover a tot une tente subtil, et garde que tu saiches a tot la tente combien elle a de parfont.	When there is no fistula, and it is awake and gushes pus and corrupt moisture, if you provide total care to the wound, and keep the patient aware of the entire wound as much as possible.

The first sentence to translate: "If the fistula would reach the course of the vein and the intestine, if it were found in these parts, and one were to do this only in the belly, and think that it is not a serious matter; after curing the belly so it is healthy, and if the fistula is seen, and the matters are long bones, then one should know that the belly is completely healthy; and if the matters are long bones, one should know that the belly is healthy entirely; and if the matters are not long bones, one should know that the belly is damaged, and corrupted the bones at their root.
de la maladie des reins	Of the disease of the kidneys

de la vessie	Of the bladder

de la marris	Of the marsh

de la hainche	Of the hedgehog
Quant les moistors viscouses dessendent a la boiste de la hainche, et por ceste cause si se muet de son leu, et li signes est que li cuisse est plus longe que li autre quant on le mesure ensamble; et est trovez li leus dou departement vuis, si covient que tu cauterizes le malaide sus la boiste de la hainche a I cautere semblant au cercle, et seigne devant le leu entor la boiste si com elle torne, si que li boiste soit dedens le cercle; et si soit li cauteres telz com cil dont on a cauterizeit le stomac.	When the viscous moisture descends to the hedgehog's chest, and for this reason if it is motionless from its shoulder, and the sign is that the breast is longer than the other when measured together; and it is found that the shoulders are in different departments wanted, then it comes that you cauterize the patient on the hedgehog's chest at the cauterization like a circle, and sign before the shoulder around the chest if the chest turns the circle; and if it is the cauterizations such as those that have been cauterized on the stomach.

de la dolor de la hainche	for the pain of the shoulder
Quant dolor vient en la boiste de la hainche, et c’est de froidor et de moistor, et li malaides est curez de ceu que nos avons dit en la division et li cure ne vaut, et li maladie est anciene: adonc covient il que tu purges le malaide des grosses humors de pilules fetides, ou autres pilules bones semblans.	When pain comes in the shoulder joint, and it is cold and moist, and the patient is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not work, and the disease is old: then it is necessary that you purge the patient of large humors of fetid pills or other bone-like pills.

Et se tu vues, si le cauterize au cautere dou cercle que nos avons devant dit en la dislocation de la hainche; mais fai en teil maniere que li cercles conteigne toute la hainche, et tous li espés dou keur soit ars. And when the pain comes to the thigh and the knee, the patient is to have the sciatic nerve cauterized at the ankle, four times, on the side where there is less flesh; and if it is the cutaneous nerve, and if it is near the end of the toe or finger, then the nerve should be cauterized at the point where the patient feels the pain three points or four at the cautery which is called "points".
Et se mestiers est, se li en fai plus; et se il seit que li dolor soit desoz le genoil vers la cuisse, se li fais cautere au cautere cutellaire ou circulaire, et te done bien garde en tous tes cauteres que tu n’i lassier mie tant le cautere que tu brules les ners et les grans arteres, et que tu ne faices au malaide plus grant nuisance et contraction.	And if it is necessary, I will do more; and if the pain is from the groin to the thigh, I will make a fire cautery at the cutting or circular cautery, and you should keep well in all your cauterizations that you do not burn the nerves and the large arteries, and that you do not cause more harm and contraction to the patient.

And I myself have seen more cases where cautery was done on the ankle, and they hurt so much that the entire leg became inflamed, and the toe as well, and it was noticed and corrupted in all the toes.

And let it be washed as much as it is all red and wet, then put it on the handle of the hot iron, and make it bend once on the cauterization; and leave it three hours; then apply ointment, and leave the wound open long until cured.

Et Galiens nos raconte une cure dont uns hons fut curez de la dolor de la hainche et de la voine sciatique, et lou loe mout, et dit que on n’i fist autre cure, et qu’il en fut sanez a une soule fois quant on ot fait ceste cure, et il se fut baigniez si com il l’enseigne ci aprés. Et Dyascorides dist que quant li voine sciatique est cauterizee de fiens de chievre, si i aide mout; et doit estre fais li cauteres en teil maniere.	When the science of the vein is cauterized with the horn of a goat, if it helps the pain; and it must be made in a certain way.

Aprés pren fiens de chievre sec, et l’empren a feu tant qu’il soit charbons, et lou met sus la laine, et le laisse tant qu’il soit estains; et refai encor ensi, et ne cesser de faire ensi tant que tu penses par sens qu’il viegne jusc’a la hainche, et que li dolor soit cessee; et cist manieres de cautere est apelez «cautere de chievre». de la dolor dou dos	Of the pain in the back of the neck
Quant dolor vient au dos, ou par cheoir ou de percussion ou par trop grant evacuation, ou par semblans de matiere espandue froide, a nule de ces semblances ne vaut cauteres, fuer que a celi qui vient de infusion de froide matiere.	When pain comes to the back of the neck, whether from scratching or percussion or from too much evacuation, or from the appearance of expanded cold matter, none of these appearances is worth cauterization, rather it is for that which comes from the infusion of cold matter.
Il covient c’aprés ceu que li malaides est voidiez de pilules fetides ou d’autres semblans, que on li faice sus lou dos, lai ou li dolor tient, trois lignes signies d’enche, et en chescune ligne V cauteres ou plus selonc la vertut et la quantiteit que li malaides puet soffrir; et soit fait li cauteres selonc le cautere qui est apelez «poins»; et se tu vues, fai III cauteres ou IIII au cautere clavile moien selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary after the patient has been made clean by removing fetid pills or other substances, to make a line on the back of the neck where the pain remains, with three lines marked with a scalpel, and in each line V cauterization or more according to skill and the amount that the patient can bear; and this cauterization should be made according to the cautery called "points"; and if you see, make III cauterizations or IIII on the scalpel clavicle according to this form:
