de la dolor des jointes	of the pain of the joints
Quant dolor de jointes sunt de moistors que sont espandues a chaicun membre dou cors, et quant dolor vient em piez, que li mire apelent «podagre» proprement, et quant elle est de froide cause et cures de medicines ne la puent curer, si est curez par cauteres en teil maniere: fai li mout de cauteres entor la jointure dou piet, et soit li cauteres olivaire selonc ceste forme:	When pain in the joints comes from moisture that is expanded to every part of the body, and when pain comes by cramps, which they call "gout" properly, and when it is of a cold cause and medicines do not cure it, then it can be cured by fire cauterization in this way: make the cut on either side of the joint, and the cauterization should be olive-shaped according to this form:
Et s’il i a besoigne que tu poignes sus la faice dou piet, se li fai cautere a tot le cautere c’on claime «point».	If he thinks that you prick at the cheek, then he orders a burn to be performed on the entire area claimed as "point".
Et se les dolors viegnent jusc’a genous et as autres jointures, et ceu avient maintes fois, se li fai cautere sus chaicun genoil III cauteres ou IIII de chescunne partie, a tout le cautere olivaire; et se tu as mestier de plus, si en fai plus, mais n’i tenir mie ta main fuers que tant que li espés dou keur soit ars.	If the pain comes to the jaw and other joints, and this happens repeatedly, then he orders a burn to be performed on each jaw three times or four times at the olive oil cauterization; and if you have skill for more, but do not hold your hand as long as the pain is tolerable.
Et se les dolors dessendent jusc’a genoil et au dos, se li aministre le cautere que nos avons dit en son chapistre.	If the pain descends to the jaw and back, then he administers the cauterization we have mentioned in this chapter.
Et se les dolors sunt as mains, si fai poins entor le foscile II lignes; et s’il remaint point de dolor as dois, si fai poins sus chescune jointe et sus lou poil de la main; et se les dolors vienent jusc’as coutes ou jusc’as espaules, si cauterize chescune partie, et fai boin governement au malaide et penre medicines.	And if the pain is in the hands, then I make points every second line; and if there is no more pain, then I make points on each joint and on the hair of the hand; and if the pain comes from the elbows or shoulders, then cauterize each part, and govern the patient with medicines.
Car se tu li fais boin governement et tu purges fleume, si sera saneis a l’aide de Deu.	For if you make the patient govern with medicines and purge the blood, then they will be cured by God.
de la routure dou syfac	from the rupture of the face
Quant routure vient en angres, et li bouelz dessendent as coions et c’est novelement, si covient que quant tu lou vues curer, qu’il ne menjuce mie celui jor; et qu’il use choses qui laichent lou ventre, si que li fiens dessende de son ventre; aprés le fai seoir sus son dos entre tes mains, et li comande qu’il teigne son alaine tant que li boueil soient repairiet, et les ramoinne a tes dois, et seigne d’enche desoz la routure sus l’os dou poignil, et a tout un signe que soit semblans a la moitiet d’un cercle a desus dou cors; puis eschaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	When the rupture comes in gushes, and the blood flows downwards, and it is newly born, then if you cure it as soon as you see it, do not let it mix with your belly; and use things that relieve your stomach, so that it does not descend from your stomach; after which you make him lie on his back between your hands, and command that he lick his nails until they are repaired, and pluck them out at your sides, and sign with your thumb that the rupture is on the bone of the wrist, and in a sign that is like half of a circle around the two corners of the wrist; then wash the cauterization with this form:
tant qu’il soit blans et qu’il giete senteles.	As long as it is white and has a glistening feel.
Puis ramoine les bouels a lor leu; et li ministres teigne sa main sus qu’il ne retornent arrier; et oevre bien les cuisses au malaide, et met desoz lui I cussin et I serjant sus les cuisses, et I autre sus lou pis qui li teigne les mains; puis met le cautere sus lou signe a tout ta main, et lou tien droit et lou tien tant que tu ateignes l’os, et se tu ne l’ateins la premiere fois, si le rencomence encor une autre tant que tu viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde subtilment que li boueil ne saille quant tu fais lou cautere; que tu ne le brulasses; et que par ceu li malaides ne muere, ou autre malz.	Then remove the dirt from your body; and the physician teaches you how to hold it so that it does not return; and well work on the thighs with the patient, and put the cautery at the sign of all your hand, and hold it right and as far as you can reach the bone, and if you do not reach the first time, then it will recur again as soon as you get near the bone; and warn subtly that the dirt does not come out when you make the cautery, that you do not burn it; and so that the patient does not die, or other harm.
Et saiches que quant tu ne viens jusc’a l’os au cautere, tes ovraiges ne vaut rien.	And you should know when you come to the bone at the cauterization, your efforts are worthless.
Et covient que li cauteres des enfans soit subtilz selonc la mesure d’ous, et des grans gens aussi grans selonc lor mesure; aprés III jors cure lou leu dou cautere de burre tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés le cure d’autres oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez, et gise li malaides XL jors sus son dos tant que li plaie soit bien soudee; et covient que ses norrissemens soit lassatis longement, si que li boueil ne saillent quant il se preigdra d’aler en chambres.	And it is necessary that the cauterization of children be done subtly according to the size of the bone, and the same for adults; after three days, cure the wound of the cauterization as much as possible until the burn is healed; after the treatment of other wounds as long as it is healthy, and gently press on his back for as long as the wound is well sweating; and it is necessary that his nails be kept long, so that the dressing does not fall off when he wants to take a bath.
Et aprés XL jors, quant il se voudra lever, se li amenistre une faixe bien faite, et la porse XL autres jors; et ait boin repos, qu’il se travaille poc et se warde de trop grant repletion de boivre et de mengier, et de trop haut braire; et quant il fait cest enseignement si est sanez entierement.	After forty days, when he wishes to rise, he should pull on a well-made belt, and every other day; and he should rest for a while, so that he works quickly and does not have too much overflow of drink and dregs, and does not bark too loudly; and when he teaches this lesson, it is completely healthy.
Et je dirai ci aprés la cure de taillier en son chapistre.	And I will say this after the cutting in his chapter.
de la routure dou ventre	of the rupture of the abdomen
Quant routures vienent en autres ventres et sont connisans, et tu vues qu’elles ne croissent plus, se li fai I cautere dou cautere reont selonc sa quantiteit, et soit ars li tiers dou keur; aprés le cure selonc ceu que nos avons dit; et aucun des anciens ont dit c’on le doit cauterizer au cautere a III angles selonc ceste forme:	When ruptures occur in other abdomens and are known, and you see that they are not increasing, one should re-cauterize according to the quantity, and so it is for the third degree; after the treatment as we have said; and no of the ancients have said that it should be cauterized at three angles according to this form:
mais signe premier le leu d’enche et fai une ligne per la largesce desus la routure, et une autre defuers, et main ta main emmi a tout le cautere clavile.	1. The shoulder rises and I make a line for the width of the fracture, and another for the defense, and hold the patient's hand at all the cauterization point.
Mais li premiers cauteres est plus legiers et muedres.	2. But the first cauterizations are more gentle and milder.
de dolor anciene en aucun membre	3. there is no pain in any limb.
Quant dolor vient en aucun membre, ou de cheoir ou de ferir, et cele dolor tient lonc tens, et li cure de medicine n’i vaut, adonc covient qu’il soit cauterizeis au cautere qui est apelez «poins», et soit li cauteres selonc la longesce dou membre et la petitece et sa foibleteit et sa vertut et sa location de torcions et de sa dolor.	4. When pain comes in any limb, whether from cold or injury, and this pain persists for a long time, and medicine does not help, then it is necessary to cauterize at the point called "points", and to cauterize according to the length of the limb, its thickness, its weakness, its location of torsions and its pain.
s’il est sanez dou premier cautere, c’est bien; se ceu nom, recomence I autre cautere sus celui, car teilz costume est qu’il se doit muer au membre que li est prochiens, por coi il covient que tu faices les cauteres tant que li malaides soit saneis.	If the first fire cautery is healthy, it's well; if not, continue with another one, as custom dictates that one must die at the member that is proximal, because you must perform the cauteries as long as the shoulder is healthy.
de meselerie	of medicine
Li meseil sont aidiet aucune fois par cautere par grant aide, et meismement li maladie que vient de la putrefaction de fleume et de melancolie.	The remedies are never helpful once through cauterization, and at the same time, the disease that comes from the putrefaction of flesh and melancholy.
Cant tu la vues cauterizer, pren warde se li maladie est au comencement, et s’ele est curee selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et ne dessent ne ne demoure, et tu doutes que li corruption ne porpreigne tout le malaide, adonques li fai V cauteres sus lou chief: I emmi le chief a nouf, et l’autre vers lou front a la fin des chevous; et II sus les II cornes, et I derrierre sus le haiterel; et i laise tant ta main que li cauteres viegne jusc’a l’os, et tant que les escorces en issent fors si que les vapors des grosses humors s’en puissent issir; et le cauterize sus la mice selonc ce qu’il est devant.	Can you see the cauterization, when the disease is at its beginning, and if it is cured according to what we said in the division, and not hesitate or tire, and you doubt that corruption will spoil all the shoulder, therefore I make the following cauterizations on the head: I emasculated the head, and the other on the front near the end of the cheeks; then they touch the corners, and the buttocks at the hind part of the thigh; and it lasts as long as the hand holds the cauterization, and as long as the discharges issue forth so that the vapors of the large humors may issue forth; and the cauterization is made on the mouth according to what is before.
Et se li meselerie est partout esparse; et elle pert manifestement, si covient que tu lou cauterizes de ces cauteres que nos avons dit ou chief, et I cautere en som lou neis, et II cauteres sus l’espinee dou col, et VI cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos, et I grant sus la crupie et I autre delez, et II sus les II espaules; et II sus les coutes, et II sus les tendrons dou pis, et I sus chascune jointe des mains et des piez, et sus les fosses des mains; et te warde des ners que sunt sus lou derrien calcant, que tu ne les bruler; et aucune fois fait om cautere sus l’os dou poignil, et I autre sus l’os de l’estomac, et I autre sus lou foie.	1. If the scar is widespread; it is evident, if you cauterize it with these cauteries that we have mentioned or chief, and one cauterization is enough, and two cauterizations are on the shoulder bone, and six cauterizations are on the backbone, and one on the hip and the other on the knee, and two on the elbows and the wrists, and two on the ankles and the feet, and all joints of the hands and feet, and all fissures of the hands; and you will find nerves that are located below the skin, which you should not burn, and no time has been made for a cauterization on the bone of the thumb, and the other on the bone of the stomach, and the other on the liver.
Et saiches que quant plus i fais de cautere, plus li fais d’aide, et mues li profite; et saiches que li malaides ne sent point de dolor au cautere si com li sain le sentent, por ce que li cors est ja toz corrumpus.	And you advise that the more fire cauteries you perform, the more help you will receive from them; and you advise that the patient does not feel pain in the cauterization if it is not as painful as they think, because the body is already corrupted to some extent.
Et covient ke li cautere soient grant et petit selonc les membres et les jointures, selonc ceu que vos lou troverez en manieres des fers.	And it is necessary that the cauterization be both large and small according to the parts and joints of the body, according to what you will find in the ways of iron.
Aprés cure lou leu de farine de veces avec miel et autres cures tant qu’il soit saneis.	After curing the dough with flour several times with honey and other remedies until it is safe.
Quant enfleure vient en aucun membre et est curee par medicines et oiles et emplastres, et il n’est mie sanez, adonques li fai cauteres sus le membre selonc la grandour et la petitece dou membre; et soit li cauteres un poc entrans en l’espés dou keur; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound comes to any part and is treated with medicines and oils and plasters, and it is not yet healed, then perform cauterization on the part according to its size and smallness; and if the cauterization is entered into the edges of the skin; then treat for sores as long as they are not healed.
Et aucune fois fait on cautere et a la main et au piet et au dos, a l’issue dou nerf que muet le membre, et ensi si est ostee li enfleure; et toutevoie ne s’en entremette nuls s’il n’est conoissans des membres et des issues des ners movans lou cors.	And never has it been done to burn and the hand, the arm, and the back, at the end of the nerve that is silent, and then if it is not inflamed; and all this does not come into question if one does not know the members and the ends of the moving parts of the body.
de albaras	of scars
Quant li maladie qui est apelee «albaras» est enveillie, et li engien de medicine n’i valent rien, adonques le cauterize d’un cautere un poc parfont, selonc la quantiteit de l’espés dou keur, tant que li blenchour soit ostee, et soit muee sa color; puis le cure de farine de veces et de lentilles avec oile roset et foilles de plantain, et sanc de colon et sanc d’alondre, de chescun une partie; et soit mellez tout ensamble, et soit liiez d’un drapel, et soit aers au leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the disease called "scars" is awakened, and the art of medicine does not do anything, therefore it is cauterized with a cautery once or twice, according to the amount of the heat, as long as the wound is ostee and colorless; then the care of flour and lentils with rose oil and plantain leaves, and salt of colic and alendron, of each part; and mix all together, and wrap it with a bandage, and apply it to the body as long as it is healthy.
li cure de chancre par cautere	The treatment of syphilis by burning
Quant chancre vient au comencement, et tu lou vues arrester, si le cauterize au cautere qui semble I cercle, tout entor au tour dou chancre.	When syphilis appears at the beginning, and you see it stop, if the burning is done with a fire cautery that seems to form a circle, it should go around the entire syphilis.
Et toutevoie li saige dirent que on faice cautere ausi au mileu dou chancre; et toutevoie ceu ne me semble mie boin, car je redous que il ne soit ulcerez et corrumpus, et je l’ai ja veut avenir aucune fois; et plus droituriere chose est qu’il soit cauteriés entor, au cautere qui est apelez «circule», si com nos avons dit en mout de cauteres.	And all agree that it is done with fire cautery in the environment of the syphilis; and I do not think it is a bad thing, because I doubt that it will become ulcerated and corrupted, and I have always wanted this to happen once; and the most appropriate thing is that it be burned all around, with the cautery called "circular," as we have said at the mouth of cauterization.
de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer	The first sentence to translate is "de l’enfleure qui ne puet meurer". The translation of this line into English is
Quant aucuns ait une maladie qui est apelee «adubelati», et elle tarde de meurer ou por la superfluiteit qu’ele fait ou por l’eaige dou malaide quant il est decrepites (c’est a dire trop vielz) et il a poc de sanc, ou por lou tens; et tu la vues haster de meurer: adonques le cauterize entor de mout de petis cauteres en poignant; aprés le laisse ensi.	When someone has a disease called "adubelati", and it delays in dying either due to excessive production or lack of blood when it becomes old (too many) and has little sang, or for lousy; and you see it struggling to die: therefore, the cauterization is done by putting small cauters on the mouth; afterwards, it is left alone.
Car elle se hastera de meureir.	For it will struggle to die.
Et se tu la vues percier a tout le cautere, si chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	And if you see it perishing at all the cauterization, if you heat the cauterization of this form:
Et met ta main en mileu de cele maladie qui est apellee «adubelati» tant que li cauteres ait perciet lou keur, et soit telz li cauteres que li malaides lou sente defuers en teil maniere que li cours de la porriture soit alegis.	And put your hand in the environment of this disease called "adubelati" as long as the cauterization has perceived the heat, and such are the cauterizations that the patient feels deflated in a certain way that the course of the pulse is alleviated.
Aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	After the treatment, if it is perfectly healthy.
li cure dou feu par fer	the cauterization by fire with iron.
Une autre maniere de maladie i a qui est apelee «corrodens», et n’est autre chose que une mengeson de membre, car ele menjut les membres ausi com li feus les leignes seches.	Another type of disease is called "corrodens", and it is nothing more than a swelling of the limbs, as it also dries out the hands like the feet.
Se tu vois ceste maladie en leu qui puisse soffrir cautere ensamble feu, adonques eschaufe les cauteres clavile mout petit et grant, selonc ceu qu’il covient au leu ou li maladie est; aprés le cauterize de toutes pars tant que tu erraiche toute la corruption, et nen remaigne rien de li, que tout ceu qui est corrumpus ne soit osteit.	If you see this disease in the shoulder that can suffer cauterization with fire, then clean the cauterizations clavile as small and large as possible, according to where the disease is; after cauterizing all parts as much as you can, there will be nothing left of it, that all that is corrupted will not become osteit.
Et puis le laisse III jors, et met sus les leus cauterizez soffre broiet avec oile tant que les eschaudures dou feu soient ostees, et toute li corruption.	Then let it rest for three days, and apply oil to the burned parts as long as the blisters from the hot fire are still intact and all corruption has subsided.
Aprés lou cure d’oignemens engendrans char.	After the care of the burns caused by fire.
Et se tu vois aprés III jors que chars saine ne naisse, c’est boin; et se ceu non, si rencomence le cautere sus ceu qui est demoreit des leus corrumpus.	And if after three days no healthy burns are born, it is good; and if they do not, continue the cauterization on the parts that are still corrupted.
Et ceste mengeson est aucune fois esteit curee de medicine ague en leu de cautere de feu; mais toutevoie cautere de feu est de plus grant aide, et j’ai ja dit la cure de la medicine ague en la division: pren la quant tu en as mestier.	And this disease has never been treated with medical care in the place of fire cauterization; but all fire cauterization is of greater help, and I have already said the treatment of the medical care in the division: take what you have in your possession.
des porrelz qui vienent as piez	Of the porings that come to the feet
Mout de fois avient que as piez par defuers naist une maladie qui est apelee «clos» selonc nostre entencion, et est une grosse chose fautree qui blece lou piet.	Many times it has happened that the feet were affected by a disease called "closed" according to our understanding, and it is a large thing to be done which hurts the foot.
Et li cauteres de ceste maladie si est selonc II manieres.	1. And the cauterization of this disease is done in two ways.
C’est a savoir cautere de feu, et cautere d’aigue chaude.	2. It is to know that cauterization by fire and hot water cauterization.
Cautere de feu si est que tu eschaufe I cautere cheveit ausi com est une penne de vouteul, et soit fait de boin fer a la mesure qu’il puisse porpenre le clou de toutes pars, et qu’il i ait subtilz marges; aprés le met tout chaut sus lou clou, et torne ta main tot entor le clou tant qu’il viegne au font dou clou; et lou laisse ensi III jors tant qu’il encomence giter porriture; puis li fai un emplaustre de malves savaiges broiies avec seil, et laisse l’emplaustre sus toute la nuit, et li clous cherra et sera desracinez de ses racines.	3. Cauterization by fire is when you heat a needle like a quill, and it is made of iron according to its size so that it can bite the claw of all parts, and have subtle margins; after you put it all over the claw, turn your hand totally around the claw until it comes to the end of the claw's point; and it leaves for three days before it begins to secrete milk; then make a poultice of well-cooked, finely chopped herbs with salt, and put the poultice on all night, and the wound will be separated from its roots.
Puis cure le leu d’oignement enjanrant char tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, treat the wound with ointment by applying it as soon as it is healthy.
Et s’il sont convertit par defuers lou cors, et maintes fois avient et en mains et em piez, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere d’aigue chaude; et est en teil maniere: pren une cainne d’arain ou de fer, ou une penne de vouteul, et met sus lou clou et l’althelul, c’est asavoir porrelz verrues; et met la cainne sus si qu’ele porpreigne tout entor, puis i met un poc d’awe chaude, et retien bien ta main, et presse ta main en tornant si que li marge de la cainne viegne a la racine dou clou, et puisse trover l’aigue chaude voie parfonde jusc’a la racine; et soffre li malaides un poc la mordication de l’aigue chaude une houre; puis le laisse ensi, et il se derracinera tous a tout ses racines.	And if the wound becomes infected many times, and in the hands and fingers, then it is necessary that you have a cauterization of hot iron; and it should be done in this way: take a iron nail or a copper penny, and put it on the nail head and the nail shank, so as to make a wound; then put the iron on so that it burns all around, then put a little hot water, and hold your hand well, and press your hand while turning until the edge of the nail touches the root of the nail, and you will find the hot water way perfectly fitted at the root; then suffer the malignant burning of the hot iron for an hour; then leave it, and it will fall off all its roots.
Ensi fai un aprés autre, tant que tu esraiches toz ces qui sont au cors, puis les cure des oignemens qui engenrent char.	1. I make another after that, as long as you are aware of all these that are in the course, then you cure the wounds that engorge blood.
li cure dou trembler	2. And you cure those that tremble.
Quant aucuns tremble de froidor de ners, ou de fievre quartaine ou d’autre, si covient que tu li faices IIII cauteres ou IV sus l’espinee dou dos, I cautere entre chescune espinee; et I cautere ou pez, et I sus l’estomac au cautere olivaire; si laissera lou trembler, et se hastera li santez de la maladie froide.	3. If any tremble from cold, or fever, or other causes, then it is necessary that you make four cauteries or four on the back of the neck, one cauterization between each spine; and one at the stomach with olive oil cautery; if it continues to tremble, and eventually the health improves from the cold disease.
des pustules puans	4. Of pustules that have burst.
Aucune fois apperent par defuers le cors bathes, ou pustules puans, que vienent de grosses matieres corrumpues.	None of the time appear by defuers the corps baths, or pustules come from large materials corrupted.
si covient au premier quant eles apperent que on faice cautere sus chescun chief de la pustule: un cautere subtil de fust de mirte, de coi li pointe soit emprise au feu, ou de racine de aristologe longe, ou au cautere lenticulaire.	If it is necessary to cut at the first appearance that they appear, then a subtle fire-hardened iron cautery is needed on each point of the pustule: an iron cautery with a sharp point, or the root of Aristolochia long, or a lenticular cautery.
Et aucune fois les cauterize on au comencement quant il aperent, selonc ceste maniere, et il ne puent croistre des enqui en avant, mais est desrompue li superfluitez dont il vienent, et sont sanez; mais il covient que ceu soit fait aprés l’evacuation de sanc.	And never are cauterized at the beginning when they appear in this way, and they do not grow new tumors forward, but are disrupted by the superfluity that comes, and they are healthy; but it is necessary that this be done after the evacuation of blood.
quant li artere est copee	When the artery is tied off
Maintes fois avient grans decorremens de sanc de l’artere qui est copee a la plaie que vient au pardefuers, ou a l’incision de l’aposteme, ou au cautere dou membre, et as semblans choses; et est mout grief chose d’estenchier.	There have been many instances of large hemorrhages from the artery that is tied off at the wound that comes to the perforators, or at the incision of the abscess, or at the fire cautery of the member, and similar things; and it is a terrible thing to enrich.
Et toutevoie quant ceu avient a aucun, si te haste de mettre ton doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne, et l’estrain mout tant que li sans soit apaisiez desoz ton doi, et que goute n’en isse plus; puis met au feu les cauteres olivaire plusors petis et grans tant qu’il soient tuit rouge; puis empren I, ou grant ou petit selonc la plaie et lou leu en coi li artere est route, et met le cautere sus cele voine ou tu tiens ton doi, et tien le cautere tant sus que li sans soit restainchiez.	And if there is none, then whatever you have to put your index finger on the wound of the vein, and hold it as tightly as you can until it is calmed down by your finger, and no more pain; then put on fire the olive-wood cauteries more or less according to the size, as they all turn red; then I, or as much or little as the wound and the skin allows, put the cautery on the vein where you hold your finger, and put the cautery on until it is no longer inflamed.
Et s’il saut fuers quant tu lieves ton doi desus la voinne, et li cauteres estint, si pren hastivement I autre des cauteres qui sont au feu.	And if it hurts when you tie the vein with your other hand after the cautery, and the cautery is extinguished, then take immediately another cautery that is on fire.
Et ne cesser de faire ceu l’un aprés l’autre tant que li sans soit estenchiez; et warde que tu n’ardes lou nerf qui est delez, et que autre malice ne viegne sus lou malaide; et saiches que quant sans decourt de l’artere, c’on ne lou puet mie bien restenchier meismement quant li artere est grans, se ceu n’est par une des IIII manieres que nos avons dit: ou par cautere, ou par extraction quant ele n’est mie traite, ou par fort liement de fil, ou par medicines mises sus qui ont pooir de restenchier sanc; et soit liee et estrainte avennament.	And do not stop doing this one after the other until it is stretched; and guard that you do not burn the nerve that is sensitive, and that no other malice comes to the patient's shoulder; and warn that when without cutting the artery, it cannot be well rested immediately when the artery is large, if it is not by one of the four ways we have mentioned: either by cautery or by extraction when it is properly treated, or by gentle twisting of thread, or by medicines placed on it that can cause inflammation; and let it be loose and drawn.
Qui i amenistrera restenchement de liier estroitement de drapelz ou de metre choses ardans sus, ou autres semblans choses, se n’i profite se poc non.	Whoever will perform the restoration of the tie very tightly with threads or to put things burning on, or other similar things, will not benefit from it if not.
Et se ce avient a aucun et il n’ait mie mire ne medicine present, si doit mettre son doi indice sus la plaie de la voinne si com nos avons dit, et bien estrendre tant qu’il soit restenchiez desus la plaie et desus la voinne; et ne remuer lou doit, mais lou moille d’awe froide sovent que soit mout froide tant que li sans soit congelez et engrossiez et restenchiez; et faice des enqui en avant ceu dont il a mestier de cauteres et de medicines.	And if there is none and no remedy or medicine present, then he must put his index on the wound of the vein as we have said, and firmly press until it is sore from the wound and the vein; and he must not move, but he must be very cold often that it is not frozen and swollen and sore; and he should make inquiries before those with whom he has experience in cauterization and medicines.
Ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille	Here comes the first sentence to translate: "ci encomence li secons livre des cures de taille
Nos vos avons dit ou premier chapistre toute maladie en coi il covient cautere de feu, ou de medicine ardans, et les oquisons et les causes et les estrumens et les formes des cauteres; et ai mis celui chapistre des lou chief jusc’a piez, et je irai en cest chapistre par celi meisme voie por ceu c’on trueve plus legierement ceu c’on voura.	1. We have told you in the first chapter about all diseases, whether it is to burn or to use hot medicine, and to cut, to causes, to stings, and to forms of cauteries; and I have put this chapter of the loaves of the chief, and I will go in this chapter by my own way because it is lighter to go where one wants.
Et ainsois que je encomence ceu, il covient, chier fil, que vos aprenez que en cest chapistre a plus de peril et de paor que ou premier des cauteres, et por ceu il covient plus grant cautele.	2. And if I begin this, it is necessary, my dear, that you learn that in this chapter there is more danger and fear than in the first of the cauteries, and for this reason it requires greater caution.
Car en l’ovraige de cest chapistre avient maintes fois evacuation de sanc a l’ovrir la voinne, et a l’incision sus aposteme, et as cures des plaies, et a l’estraction des saiettes, et a l’incision sus la piere, et les semblans choses; ou il a doutance et paor, et en vient li mors a plusors.	For in the work of this chapter, there is often the evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
Et je vos amoneste que vos n’entreprenez folie.	And I warn you that you are foolishly doing this.
Car mout de manieres de gens vienent en cures.	For many methods of people come in the treatment.
si vienent de telz qui s’aïrent si avec lor maladie qu’il muerent legierement por la forsenerie qu’il trueve de sa maladie, et de la grandour de son malice; et de ces doit on avoir paor.	If they come from those who are so easily with their disease that they die lightly by the severity of the remedy they take for their disease and the greatness of their malice; and from these we should have fear.
Et de ces i a qui te done son sens, et dit: «atendez, je sui garis»; et li maladie est despitouse.	And of these he says to you: "Wait, I am hungry"; and the disease becomes desperate.
Il ne covient mie que vos vos consentez a ces qui vienent a vos qui ont ceste maniere, mais mettez plus grant cusanson en vostre honor qu’en vostre covoitise, et n’ovrez mie folement mais saigement de ceu dont vos estes certain, et dont vos poez avoir pris et los; et usez de pronostication et de indication en cures de vos malaides a coi salus soit convertie; et ceu vos aidera a aquester bone renommee, et gloire, et memoire de loenge.	Only those who consent to these who come to you who have this way, but put more trust in your honor than in your covenant, and do not despair but wisely of what you are certain, and of what you can take and lose; and use prophecy and indication in the cures of your maladies as health may convert; and this will help to this good reputation, glory, and memory of long.
Tres chier fil, Nostres Sires vos doint boin entendement et droiture, et se vos vuelle espireir de la sainte inspiration de sa main, amen.	Very dear friends, our Lords give you good understanding and right judgment, and if you will seek the holy inspiration of his hand, amen.
Or je vos ai ordeneit cest chapistre en devisant par chapistres, selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre des cauteres, que je vos ai deviseit des le chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que vos trovez plus legierement ceu dont vos avrez mestier.	Or if you have ordered this chapter by consulting physicians, according to what is done by physicians who practice cauterization, which I have advised for the chief joints, because you will find it more easily that which you will use.
dou chief plein d’aigue	The chief joint full of water
Saiches que ceste maladie vient mout de fois as enfans a l’enfanter, et quant li baille estraint trop fort le chief de l’enfant; et aucune fois vient ceu de cause reponue que on ne seit.	This disease often comes from the mother during childbirth, and when the child is pulled too hard at the head, and never has it been due to any other cause that it is not.
Et je ne vis onques ceste maladie fuers qu’en enfans, et a toz ces que j’ai veus se hastait li mors; et por ceu me semble qu’il me vaut mues lassier l’ovraige en teilz cures.	And I have never seen this disease in anyone but children, and in those that I have seen die it was the child; and therefore I think that it is worth while to explain some of the cures.
Et je vis I enfant de coi li chiés estoit plains d’aigue, et li chief engroissoit chescun jor tant qu’il ne lou pooit sostenir; et crut tant li moistor qu’il fut mors, et ceste moistor si est assemblee desoz l’os sus lou syphac, entre lou keur et l’os; et li ovraiges si est telz se li moistor est entre lou keur et l’os, et li apostemes est petis, que tu fendes emmi lou chief une fendure large; et soit ausi longe com II nous, tant que li mostor corre; et vez ci la forme dou spatumile:	1. And I saw a child who was suffering from fever, and the father cried out every night until he could not bear it; and he thought that the fever was so severe that it killed him, and this fever is located between the bone and the hip joint, between the knee and the hip; and the dislocations are such that if the fever is between the knee and the hip, and the abscess is small, then you should cut off the head of the child with a wide blade; and so it lasts as long as the fever persists; and thus the shape of the spatulum appears.
Se li moistor est plus creue, et li aposteme soit plus grans, si fai II fendures en maniere d’une croix, selonc ceste forme:	2. If the fever is more severe and the abscess is larger, then I will make cross-shaped cuts according to this form.
Et se li moistor est desoz l’os, et li signes que tu vois les commissures dou chief overtes de chescune partie, et li aigue saut fuer quant tu la presses de ta main au dedens, et ceu ne t’est mie reponut: si covient que tu fendes enmi lou chief III fendures selonc ceste maniere:	When the moisture is removed from the bone, and you see the signs of the skin over the ends of each part, and the abrupt jump occurs when you press on it with your hand, and this does not seem to be true: if you find that you need to cut off the head in three pieces according to this method:
Et aprés l’incision estrai la moistor toute fuers.	Then after the incision, remove all the moisture.
Aprés estraint les fendures de drapelz et de poudres, et i met vin et oile, et laisse ensi jusc’a cinquieme jor; puis le deslie, et cure la plaie par tentes et par oignemens, et laisse estraindre le chief egaument, et done mengier au malaide viande seche de poc de moistor tant que li membre soit confortez et sanez.	After removing the fringes and powders, and mix in wine and oil, and let it sit for five days; then remove it, and treat the wound with poultices and compresses, and let the head be evenly dried, and then soak the dry meat in a little moisture until the limb is comfortable and healthy.
Et une autre maniere d’incision est que tu regardes ou apert li grandor de l’aposteme, et li assemblé de l’aigue; car aucune fois est elle devant; aucune fois derrier; aucune fois en destre; et aucune fois en senestre.	An alternative way of incising is to look at or open the large end of the abscess, and the surrounding gutter; for it is never in front; never on the back; never on the left side; and never on the right side.
Taille donques lai ou li aposteme apert, et l’emplissement de l’aigue, et lou fent selonc ce que tu en as le pooir; et warde que tu ne coper l’artere; et veigne flun de sanc, si que li malaides muere dou decorrement de sanc et de l’evacuation de moistor.	Measure the size of the abscess opening and the gutter fullness, and make it according to what you can; and do not block the artery; and come out with blood, if the patient dies from lack of blood or evacuation of pus.
de reume	of relume.
Quant il avient a aucun une maladie qui est apelee «catarre» as eulz ou au pis, et li maladie est anciainne, et li cure de medicine ne profite mie, adonques li derraine cure si est li cauteres avec ceu c’on li copera les II arteres.	When there is any disease called "catarrh" in the ear or nostril, and the disease is ancient, and the cure by medicine does not help much, therefore it should be treated with cauterization if it covers the two arteries.
Il covient donques, cant tu les vues coper, que li malaides faice rere son chief; aprés li frotte lou leu d’un drapel aspre tant que les arteres aperent, puis estraingne li malaides son col a tout I drapel; puis regarde ou li voine bait, et li leus de l’une et de l’autre sont aprés les oreilles, et poc sont reponues; puis signe les leus d’enche, puis cope l’une et l’autre d’un spatumile agut de II pars, tant que li taille veigne jusc’a l’os, et ceu soit par lou large dou chief.	It is therefore necessary, can you see the eyes, that the patient makes a cut on his head; then he should rub the face with a sharp cloth as much as possible, until the arteries are visible, then he should hold the head tightly with both hands, and he should look to see if the eyes are in place, and the eyes on both sides are after the ears, and they are quickly repaired; then he should mark the eyes as being swollen, and he should press each eye with a sharp needle of II part, until the size comes up to the bone, and that should be done by the wide part of the head.
Et se tu vues, boute le spatumile desoz l’artere et la cope au desus, en taillant ausi com II dois au traver.	And if you see, cut the cloth away from the artery and press on it with the needle, while cutting as much as possible, like II does to the bone.
Et quant li voinne est copee, si saut li sans en haut continuelment fuers.	When the vein is punctured, if the blood does not stop continuing.
Et se li artere n’apert au sentir, si covient que tu mesures la quantiteit de l’espaice de III dois, puis seigne d’enche et fent jusc’a l’os; et ceu qu’il covient dou sanc mettre fuers si est VI c/, et par aventure un poc plus ou moins, selonc ce que li malaides puet soffrir, et la repletion de l’artere; puis regarde la plaie: s’il remaint sus l’os point dou syphac, si le cope que apostemes chaus n’i veigne, puis estrain la plaie et lie, et la cure d’oignement tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And if the artery does not stop bleeding, then measure the amount of blood that comes out, and then cut and fill the hole; and if it is necessary to put in six sutures, and by chance a little more or less, according to what the patient can bear, and the filling of the artery; then look at the wound: if the stitch does not remain on the bone, and the one that was sewn does not come out, then tighten the stitch and tie it, and the cure with ointment as long as it is healed.
de emigrainne	Of the migraine
Quant emigrainne anciaine vient, et catarre agut, por les moistors des larmes et les chalors en temples et sode anciene forsenee et semblans choses, et il est medicinez par manieres de cures de medicine et tout ceu ne li profite mie, si estraions les arteres des temples et lou cauterizons, si com nos avons conteit.	When the migraine comes, and the forehead is pounding, with pain in the temples and headache, and sometimes other symptoms, it is treated with medicinal cures and all remedies do not help, if we cut the arteries of the temples and cauterize, as we have experienced.
Et li maniere de l’estraction d’elles si est que li malaides faice rere les poilz de ses temples, et entende a l’artere qui apert en la temple, car elle apert bien par son batement, et est poc reponue fuers que en aucuns homes qui sont trop froit; et s’elle est reponue, si estraigne son col li malaides d’aucuns drapelz, puis frote le leu d’aucun aspre drap, et arose le leu d’aigue chaude tant que li artere apere manifestement; puis pren le spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	And the manner of extracting them if the patient has hair on his temples, and understands the artery that opens in the temple, because it opens well by its beating, and is quickly repaired in no man who is too foolish; and if it is repaired, then draw the collar of the patient's hair from the temple, then rub the scalp with a dry cloth, and wet the scalp with hot water until the artery opens obviously; then take the spatula of this form:
puis escorche le cuir legierement tant que tu veignes a l’artere, puis la trai en haut as pinceures, et la depart bien des toiles que sont desoz li de chescune partie; et se li artere est subtilz, si la torne a la pointe de l’uncine, puis la cope de celle partie selonc la quantiteit des II chiés.	Then lightly burn the light leather until you reach the artery, then tear it at the top with your fingernails, and remove as many threads as are loose from each part; and if the artery is subtle, then the knot turns at the point of the uncinate, then the loop of that part follows according to the number of II chiés.
Car s’elle n’est copee, si ne saut mie li sans dou tout en tout.	For if it is not cut, then it will not jump out without pain at all.
Et trai dou sanc des VI c/, jusc’a III; et se li artere est grans, si covient que tu la lies en II leus d’un fil double fort de soie, que porriture n’i veigne devant le soudement de la plaie, et veigne decorremens de sanc; puis cope la superfluiteit qui est entre les II liiens en celle houre meisme, et puis, se tu vues, si lou cauterize dou cautere cutellaire jusc’a l’os tant que li chiés soient copez; et c’est li muedre oevre, se li malaides n’a fievre et il est de chaude complexion.	And cut out as much blood as sixth of a pint, and if the artery is large, then it will be necessary to tie it in two threads of double fine silk, which will not come before the wound, and will cause the drainage of blood; then cut off the excess that is between the two threads at that hour, and then, if you see, if the cauterization is as hot as a cauterizing iron until the chiés are tied; and this is the best way, if the patient does not have fever and has a warm complexion.
Car li cauteres est aide por finir les moistors: por ceu est il de plus grant aide as moistors.	For the fire cautery is help to finish the moisture: for it is of greater aid to moisture.
Ou il covient por l’estraction des arteres que om emplisse lou leu de viel coton et mette on sus tentes bien faites; et quant on les desliera, si soit curez de medicines seches que font naistre char, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se sans cort de l’artere tant dis com tu i oevres, si te haste dou coper par cautere, ou tu emple lou leu de vitriole et l’estrain a ta main que li sans soit estainchiez; et se tu n’as ceu present, si met sor le leu ton doit tant que li sans soit congelez, et arose le leu d’aigue froide tant que li sans cesse, et soit estraint si com il covient; et ceu qui est muedre et plus legier en l’estraction de l’artere est que tu cauterizes la voinne de cest cautere trenchant de II pars, mais li trenchant soient bien espés por warder plus longement lor chalor.	For it is necessary to extract the arteries with great care: that is, fill the vein with many pieces of soft cotton and stitch them well made; and if you untie them, be sure to use dry medicines that make water flow and stitches, as long as they are healthy; and if there is no need for a cautery, or use your legs instead of the cautery at your hand that is not yet frozen; and if you do not have this present, put your legs in such a way that they are not congealed, and wet them with cold water as much as possible, and keep them so until it comes out; and what is more difficult and lighter in extracting the arteries is that you cauterize the vein of this cautery trenchant of II part, but the trenching must be well spaced to last longer without pain.
Car quant li estrumens est trop tenves, si tient moins sa chalor.	For when the stomach is too empty, it retains less food.
Et doit avoir entre les II coutelz I doit de gros d’espaice, et puis quant tu as signiet d’enche les II leus, et tu mes lou fer ardant sus tant qu’il viegne jusc’a l’os, et cope la voinne en II leus; et soient esloigniet entre les II chiés car il n’est mie soudez de cest cautere dou tout en tout; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	And it should have between the two clips one that is large enough, and then when you feel the two holes are full, and you make your fire burn as hot as it can go to the bone, and cover the vein in the two holes; and they should be separated between the two heads because it is not suitable for this cauterization all around; and this is the form of the cauterization:
des larmes	of tears
Quant les larmes des eulz sont dessendans des voinnes que sont sus lou test dou chief de fuer, et il ne profite mie cure de medicine c’on i faice, et tu vois la faice dou malaide enrougir, et sent ou front ambulation si com de fremis; et sui oil sont tenve et moiste si que li poil des papieres sont cheut, et sont eschaufees les papieres, et escorchies de l’ardor des larmes, si ait mestier de ceste cure.	When the tears of the eyes are dripping from the veins that are located at the top of the head, and it does not benefit much from medicine, and you see the face of the patient pale and weak, and the front ambulation is like a shiver, and the papers are very thin and moist so that the papers of the eyes are wet, and they are burned by the heat of the tears, if it has to do with this cure.
Et l’apelerent li ancien «cure contuse», et est que tu faices a rere au malaide qui a ceste maladie les poilz qu’il ait ou front, puis li fai III fendures ou front igalment selonc la longesce dou front; et soit l’une des fendures ausi com II doi tout emmi lou front en avalant aval jusc’a neif, et les autres II as II costelz par desus les papieres, et te garde de l’incision des arteres que sont as II costez par desus les papieres; et aloigne ta main de la continuation des II mandibules, et soit chescune plaie la quantiteit de III dois au traver joins; et aies apparillie une piece d’esponge et mout de drapelz ses por essuer lou sanc, puis boute le spatumile agut de II pars de coi ci est li forme:	1. And it was called the "inflamed cure," and that is why you should shave the patient who has this disease, both on the head and in front, then make three incisions or front equally according to the length of the front; and one of the incisions should be made at the base of the forehead using a razor, and the others should be made through the papers, and keep away from the incision of the arteries that are made through the papers; and separate your hand from the continuation of the jawbones, and each wound should have three doses of III to the joints; and you will have appeared a piece of sponge and moisten the sweat of the patient, then put the spumilie agut of II parts of cloth that is the form:
des l’incision qui est dever la temple jusc’a la seconde incision; et escorche tout le keur qui est entre les II fendures a tot lou syfac qui est sus l’os, puis fai autreteil des la moiene incision jusc’a l’autre seconde, et puis estrai fuer cest spatumile.	1. From the incision that cuts through the temple until the second incision; and scorch all that is between the two fences throughout the entire facial bone that is under the eye, then make another part of the third incision up to the other second, and then extract this spatulum.
si boute en la premiere fendure l’estrument qui est apelez «cultellaire», et est tresbien trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part est souef, ne mie trenchans, et c’est li forme:	2. If the bone is broken in the first fence with the instrument called "cultellary," and it is very sharp on one side and very blunt on the other, do not be too sharp, and this is its shape:
Et met le costeit taillant vers la char aerse au keur, et lou costeit souef vers l’os, et lou boute tant qu’il veigne a la moiene fendure.	3. And cut the costelet along the bone to the knee, and the costelet is blunt towards the bone, and the bone as far as it reaches the second fence.
Et cope toz les vasselz que dessendent dou chief as eulz tant que l’incision soit continue jusc’a ceu qui apert dou keur, et puis autreteil fai en la moiene fendure jusc’a l’autre defuer; et puis estrai dou sanc igalment, et espresse lou leu por le sanc pris; puis met en chescune fendure une tente de viel coton, et met sus drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile et en aisil, et garde que apostemes chaus n’i veigne; et au tier jor deslie lou liien, et i amenistre grant planteit d’aigue tede, puis lou cure d’oignement basilicon avec oile roset, et d’autres cures dont on cure plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And cut all the veins that descend from the wound as much as the incision continues until it is fully open, and then another part makes the other end also open; and then extracts the blood evenly, and expresses the leeward for the blood taken; then puts a piece of soft cotton in each furrow, and wraps with fluffed linen threads soaked in wine and oil, and keeps it from being wet; and when the limb is dry, applies large amounts of tincture of wormwood with olive oil, and other ointments used for wounds, as long as it is healthy.
dou reume des eulz	The first line of the text translates to "He takes away the hairs
Quant a aucun vienent catarre agut acostumeement, et tu vois les eulz tenves et petis, et afoiblir la veue, et les papieres brulees; et li poil chieent, et ou chief en parfont a dolor ague, et li malaides esternue; adonques saiches par ces accidens que celles matieres et cil catharre ne vient fuer que de maintes voines, et li muedre cure que i est, si est ceste.	For if there is no catarrh habitually, and you see the hairs thinned and broken, and the eyes burning, and the papers burned; and the hair falls out, and it causes great pain to the patient, and the malady is severe; therefore, one must be cautious of these accidents that these materials and this catarrh do not come only from many veins, and the cure that it has is if it is this.
Et est que tu comande au malaide a rere son front, puis fai une grant fendure emmi lou front, et une autre dou large I poc.	And it is that you command the patient to shave his head, then make a deep cut along the front of his head, and another wide one in the middle.
