And begins with the burning of the left temple to the right temple, and it is the incision into the bone; and move your hand away from the nerves of the temples that move in the minge; and when the bone is exposed, if all the blood comes out onto a sponge, then place between the two lips of the burning and put cotton on top, and then wrap with linen; then lay rough edges in wine and oil, and keep away from aphthmia; when it is healed, if it comes to touch the bone as much as charms and begins to grow, then the care of things that are excised, which cause pain, do not use char.
En teil maniere: pren II parties de flor de froment, et de colofoine IIII parties, et en fai emplaustre; et l’aministre en ces plaies por enjanrer char per tout.	In the same manner: take two parts of wheat flower and four parts of linen, and make a paste; and apply this to these wounds for healing them completely.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	of the earwax
Tout ceu que chiet ens oreilles est une des IIII choses: ou grains, ou beste, ou piere de mine ou semblans chose si com fer; ou semence, si com jaisses, feves, pois; ou chose defluans si com aigue et aisilz et semblans choses.	All that comes out of the ears is one of the four things: wax grains, wax from bees, earwax or similar things like that; wheat, chickpeas, peas; or something that flows like honey and oil and similar things.
Quant il chiet en l’oreille piere ou autre maniere de chose que ne s’ajoste mie a l’oreille, ne ne croist en l’oreille, si met l’oreille au solel.	When he pushes something into the ear hole or another way of thing that does not fit well in the ear, and it does not grow in the ear, if he puts the ear to the sun.
Se tu vois la piere, si distille aucun poc d’oile violet ou oile de sisament, puis i amenistre extraction; et lou fai esternuer de condisi, et li estoupe les narines quant li esternuemens vient, et met entor l’oreille pieces de drapelz ou laine; et estent l’oreille au desus.	If you see the piercing, if no drop of violet oil or linseed oil distills, then the extraction is performed; and I make the patient lie down, and he snores when exhaling, and puts his ear pieces of cloth or wool; and the ear is at the end.
Mout de fois vient fuer par ceste cure; et s’elle ne vient fuer, se li amenistre extraction as pinceures subtilz, de coi ci est li forme:	This treatment is applied many times; and if it does not work, then the extraction is performed with forceps, of which the form is:
S’elle saut fuer as pinceures, c’est boin; se ceu non, si amenistre extraction a l’oncine subtil de petite doubleure; et s’elle ne saut par ceu, si fai une caine d’arain et boute lou chief de la cainne ou pertuis de l’oreille fort, et estoupe ceu qui est entor la cainne de cire mole si que li vens n’i puisse entrer avec la cainne; puis le trai fuer forment, car mout de fois vient fuer si com nos avons dit; et s’elle ne vient fuer en teil maniere, si prent glut de coi en prent les oisiaus, et met en som aucun estrument qui soit a point por ceu faire, et met un poc de coton entor; puis presse le glut sus la piere ou quel chose que ce soit, et trai fuer.	If it jumps with the forceps, it is wrong; and if it does not jump, then the extraction is performed with small forceps, of which the form is: and if it does not jump, then I make a hole in the ear and insert the end of the cord or the chief of the cord into it, and stop it which is at the outer part of the ear wax so that it does not enter with the cord; then the treatment is formed, as we have said, if it jumps many times; and if it does not jump in this way, then he takes glue on his fingers, and puts any instrument that can be used to do it, and puts a piece of cotton at the end; then presses the glue on the piercing or whatever it is, and makes the extraction.
Et s’elle ne saut fuer de toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si te haste de fendre l’oreille ainsois que aposteme chalz i veigne, et spasme; et li maniere de la fendure si est que tu faices premier sainier lou malaide de la cephalique, et estrai dou sanc selonc la mesure de sa vertu, puis fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains et li torne l’oreille au desus, et fent une petite fendure en la racine de l’oreille a la graisse ou leu dependant; et soit li fendure ausi com une lune, tant que tu viegnes a la piere, puis l’oste selonc ton pooir, et la suce hastanment a ta bouche; et la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If she does not fall from all these things that we have said, and you insist on tearing the ear even if it causes chills and spasms; and the way of tearing is that you first sharpen the blade of the scalpel, and draw out the sinus according to its strength, then hold the scalpel between your hands and turn the ear towards you and make a small cut at the root of the ear in the fat or depending on it; and the cut should be like a moon, as you approach the point, then the bone according to your power, and the saliva hangs in your mouth; and the cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se c’est grains qui est ens et il enfle, si aministre extraction; et si’il ne puet issir, si amenistre I spatumile tenve subtil selonc ceste forme:	And if it is a grain that is in and it swells, then give the extraction; and if it cannot be extracted, then give me the spatium (spatule) tende subtly according to this form:
et amenistre incision de celui grain.	and give an incision to that grain.
Mais ne faire mie ceu quant tu penses que li grains est moistes por la moistor de l’oreille, tant que tu en aies fait maintes pieces; puis l’estrai as pinceures subtilz et au succier, si com nos avons dit, si que li estractions soit aligie.	But do not cut it off if you think the grain is swollen by ear moisture, as many times as you have done it; then extract it with fine tweezers and gum, as we have said, if the extractions are dry.
En l’aigue donques que chiet en l’oreille covient que li malaides use d’esternuement de condisi premiers, et ample l’oreille de viel coton.	In the fever therefore that happens in the ear, it is necessary that the patient uses the condiement of the first essence and makes the ear ample with soft cotton.
Et soit gisans sus celle oreille meisme ou li aigue est.	And let them be placed on the same ear or where the wound is.
s’elle saut fuer per ceu, c’est boin.	If it jumps for that reason, it's good.
se ceu non, si prent maintes pieres selonc li longesce de ton doit tenves et legieres, et les eschaufe un poc au feu; et em mette li malaides une ou pertus de son oreille, et saille sus i. de ses piez d’autre part, et fiere d’une autre piere sus la piere qui est en l’oreille; et ne cesse de faire ceu de piere em piere tant que li aigue isse toute fuer, et ensi saut elle toute fuer; et se tu vues, si prent I jonc, et boute l’un des chiés en l’oreille, et l’autre chief emprent de feu tant que li plus dou jonc soit ars; puis refai autreteil d’autres jons tant que li aigue isse toute, si com nos avons dit en la piere.	If it does not jump, then take as many piercings as possible according to the length of your tooth, and heat them slightly; and put the forceps on one side of the ear, and insert it into the other part, and fix it in place with a hole in the ear; and continue making these holes one after another until the wound is completely healed, and then it will be completely healed; and if you see, if it jumps, take one of the teeth in the ear, and the other tooth will be taken out by fire as soon as the more painful one is taken out; then make other holes as many as possible until the wound is completely healed, just as we have said in the hole.
En l’estraction de la beste, s’elle est de petit cors, si com puce et semblans chose, cure la si com nos avons dit en la division; mais s’elle est de grant cors c’on la puisse sentir, si amenistre extraction de pinceures; et c’est li chose plus legiere a oster qui soit en l’oreille.	In the extraction of the tooth, if it is of small size, like a pea and similar, it is treated as we have said in the division; but if it is of large size, one can feel it, if the extraction of forceps is done properly; and this is the lighter thing to do in the ear.
En l’estraction des vers enjanrez as oreilles, quant tu lou cures si com nos avons dit en la division et ou traitier des distillations, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu regardes l’oreille au soleil: s’il i apert nulz vers, si les trai as pinceures subtilz, et s’il n’aperent, si prent la cainne de coi ci est li forme:	In the extraction of the ears' rings, if you treat it as we have said in the division and if you use distillations, and the treatment does not profit, then look at the ear with the sun: if there are no holes, if you take fine forceps, and if there are, if you tie a string of this size:
Et soit estroite desoz et large desus.	And let it be tight and wide and long.
Et boute lou plus subtil chief en l’oreille selonc la quantiteit de la soffrance dou malaide, puis succe forment a tot la caine; fai ceu sovent tant que tuit li ver issent.	And bind the ear more tightly according to the amount of suffering the patient endures, then gradually form it into a ring; do this often until it fits perfectly.
Et s’il n’obeissent a issir, si estoupe entor la cainne de coton si com j’ai dit en la piere; et s’il ne saillent fuer si com nos avons dit, si aministre distillations que li ancien ont esprovees en l’ocision des vers, et tu les troveras ou traitier des distillations; et si distille tes oiles et tes medicines en l’oreille a tout cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme si com tu vois:	And if they do not fit, if the cotton glove swells as we have said in the ear hole; and if they do not hold well, if you have followed our instructions, then administer distillations that the ancients used in the decision of the verse; and you will find them or the oils and medicines in the ear with this instrument, and so form it as you see:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain estrois desoz a I petis pertuis, et desus overs por distiller; et por presser dedens la distillation a I estrument d’arain bien fait por ceu, et se tu vues pren I raseur et envoloupe entor la pointe avenanment coton; puis i giete ton oile ou ton jus, et ceu que tu vues de tes medicines en la cainne, et li caine soit en l’oreille; puis boute dedens lou raseur a tout lou coton, et presse ta main tempreement tant que li oile soit distilleit ou chevement de l’oreille; et lou sente li malaides dedens, et soit li distillations I poc eschaufee au feu ainsois c’on la distille en l’oreille; et garde qu’elle ne soit trop froide, car li medicine ne seroit mie si bone.	1. And let silver or gold be boiled in the small piercings, and then strained through a fine sieve; and to press the distillation into the well-made silver instrument, and see if you have the rasor and envelop it at the point of the earring; then let the oil or juice gush out, and whatever you see of your medicines in the line, and the line is in the ear; then dip the rasor into all the cotton, and press your hand firmly until the oil is distilled or comes from the ear; and it will feel the medicine's effects, and so is the distillation in the pother bowl, if it is not too cold, as the medicine will not be good if it is too cold.
de l’estoupement des oreilles	Of the ear's chill
Aucun enfant naissent qui n’ont nul pertus ens oreilles; et ceste meisme chose avient as homes par estoupement de plaie, ou de char nee dedens l’oreille, et cist estoupemens vient aucune fois em parfont en l’oreille, si c’on ne lou puet veoir; et aucune fois avient I poc defuer lou pertus, et lou voit om bien.	No child is born without a cold in the ears; and this very thing happens due to inflammation of the ear or from a hard blow to the ear, and these colds never appear in the ear if one cannot see; and never has there been a case where the cold was not seen.
Celle donques que vient em parfont, si c’on ne la puet veoir, est de grief sanation em plusors dispositions, et en cele c’on voit covient que tu mettes l’oreille dou malaide au soleil; et regarde dedens: se tu vois l’opilation apparent, si la oevre a tot cest spatumile de coi ci est li forme:	That which comes out of it, if one cannot see it, is a sign of improvement in the cure in many cases, and in those cases one must put the ear to the mouth of the patient; and look: if you see the exudation apparent, then that part of the swelling has disappeared.
Et soit agus et trenchans devant et derrier tout plain, si qu’il ne blece l’oreille; se li opilation est de char nee ou cors de l’oreille, si la tien as pinceures subtilz, et la cope legierement, tant que celle chars soit toute ostee.	And so it is and trenching all around and underneath, if it does not prick the ear; if the exfoliation is of char or cors of the ear, if the hand has subtle pincers, and the cup lightly, as long as that char is entirely removed.
Et se li opilations est em parfont en l’oreille, si pren I raseur subtil legier et l’eschaufe un petit au feu, puis li met ou cors de l’oreille.	And if the exfoliation is in the ear, if I take a soft and light raser and scrape it slightly and heat it up a little, then I put it or cors of the ear.
Se tu sens l’opilation dont li malaides sent grieteit a l’oïr, perce legierement, et garde que tu ne grever les ners de l’oreille; puis met en l’oreille une tente selonc la largesce dou pertus, et la moille en l’oignement egyptien.	If you feel the exfoliation that the patient feels pain in the ear, scratch gently and make sure not to hurt the ear nerves; then put a tent according to the large pustule, and apply Egyptian ointment.
Fai ceu aucun jor tant que li plaie soit soudee, ou tu pren une tente et la moille en aigue rose, et poudre sus vitriole broiet; et se tu vois enflee l’oreille, si couvient que tu traies la tente et remue une autre tente moillie en cerote qui soit fait d’oile roset et de cire, tant que li enfleure soit ostee; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Do not cause any pain as much as the wound is sore, or take a tent and moisten it with rosewater, and sprinkle some powdered vitrol; and if you see the ear covered, then roll up the tent and move another soft tent made of oil of rose and wax over it until the wound is clean. Then apply the cure as soon as it is healthy.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si plonge une esponge et drapelz en aigue froide, et le met sus l’oreille, et use d’autres cures qui oste lou decorrement de sanc qui sont ou traitier des destillations.	2. If the dislocation occurs, then dip a sponge and wring it out with cold water, and place it on the ear, and use other remedies that stop the dislocation which are treated with distillations.
de la char des papieres	Of the parchment's folds
Cist althelul que vienent em papieres des eulz quant ils sont moiste et sont sec, si covient que tu les estendes de tenailles et de pinceures, et le cope d’un spatumile de ses racines; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet.	This is the second sentence to translate. Please follow the same instructions as before:
Et se sans en decort, si le cauterize dou cautere lenticulaire subtil, et li cauterizeir aprés l’incision vaut mues; et maintes fois repairent, cant aucune chose demoure de lor racines; et quant elles sont cauterizees par feu, si sont arses celles racines et ne revienent mie.	And if without decortication, if the cautery is a subtle cauterizing cautery, and the cauterizer after the incision is not harmed; and they are repeatedly reset, none of their roots suffer anything; and when they are cauterized by fire, their roots are burned and do not return.
de la gresle	of the grit
Maintes fois vienent em papieres des eulz unes choses que semblent gresle en sa forme et en sa duresce, et por ceu est ceste maladie apelee «grandine», et est une assemblee de moistor grosse en la papiere desus et desoz; li ovraiges est telz: pren warde se li grandine se muet d’une part et d’autre, et c’est legiere chose a savoir; fent la donques dou large, puis l’escorche de chescune partie legierement, puis la prent as pinceures, et la cope.	Many times come from the paper things that seem gritty in their form and hardness, and for this it is called "grit" disease, and it is an assembly of large moisture in the paper on both sides; the treatment is as follows: make sure the grit does not move on one side and the other, and it is easy to know; then make it wider, then scrape off each part lightly, then put it in pincers, and close.
se tu ne la pues coper sens percier un poc la papiere, si ne grieve rien au malaide; et se li fendure est grans, si l’assemble a une costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et s’elle est petite, si n’i faire point de force, car li oignemens la restoure tantost et enjanre char.	If you cannot feel it with your hand, then it does not matter; and if it is sharp, then assemble it with great care, and cure it as much as possible; and if it is small, then do not make too much force, for the restoration will be done quickly and easily.
Et se li grandine est dessendans au dedens de l’oreille vers la partie desus, si enverse la papiere, et estent la grandine a unes pinceures, et la cope et presse d’une part et d’autre; et se li papiere est esloignie par l’incision, ce ne grieve rien; et quant li grandine est copee, si leive l’oil d’aigue salee, et cure le leu de ceu qui enjanre char tant que li malaides soit sanez.	If the snowflake descends towards the earlobe, and it is reversed on the paper, and the snowflake is held with forceps, and the paper is pressed from both sides; and if the paper is moved by incision, it does not matter; and when the snowflake is covered, then lift the salty oil, and cure the earlobe as much as possible until the patient is healthy.
de la graisse des eulz	Of the fat of the hairs
Exinach est une graisse qui est enjanree en toiles des papieres desus, et ce avient plus as enfans c’a nules gens, et grieve mout a lor eulz, et li vienent li catharre as matinees, et ne pueent regardeir la lumiere dou soleil por ceu que les larmes se hastent a lor eulz; et por ceu se couchent il sor lor faices adés, et dorment sus, et sont lor papieres desoz lor sorcilz moistes que li enfleure et li apparance ont covert de l’exinach qui apert en l’oil.	Exinach is a grease that is engrained in the papers of the pupils, and this happens more often with fewer people, and it grieves their eyes, and they come to the catharsis in the mornings, and cannot look at the light of the sun because the tears have reached their eyes; and for this they lie on their faces, and sleep, and are covered with the grease of their moist papers that is absorbed by the enfleurage and the appearance has become covered with exinach.
Et quant tu presses lou leu a tes dois et sent l’exirnach entr’ous.	And when you press your hand on your two and feel exinach in your eyes.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain; et puis pren I drapeil de lin, et appareille une tente em maniere d’un cercle selonc la quantiteit que conteigne exirnach de chescune partie, puis le met sus li; et presse a tes dois d’une part et d’autre, si que li exirnach soit assemblez emmi le cercle; puis fent em mileu de la moistor au spatumile trenchant une fendure dou large, et ne soit mie plus grans que li plaie c’on fait a la sainie de voinne; et fent le cuir em parfont tant que tu veignes a l’exirnach; et em plusors dispositions vient exirnach de la fendure, selonc la forme d’une piece de graisse blainche.	1. The manner of the incision is if the patient puts his head in your hand; then take a cloth from linen, and make a tent in the shape of a circle according to the quantity that contains the exudate from each part, then put it on; and press with your two hands on either side, so that the exudate is assembled in the circle; then make a mileau of the moisture at the incision, trenchant a furrow of large size, and not more than the wound you make at the healthy part of the vein; then sew it as far as you see the exudate; and in other positions, exudate comes from the furrow, according to the form of a piece of greasy white fat.
Estrai la donques a tout une piece de drap charpit entre tes dois au defuer, et torne ta main a destre et a senestre tant qu’il soit espars; et garde que tu n’ajoster en la fendure, que tu ne viegnes a tout le spatumile jusc’a l’oil, que tu ne le bleces.	1. Pull the thread through all pieces of sheeting between your two hands, and turn your left and right hands in such a way that they are even; and make sure you do not pull on the fringe, that you do not go to any part of the suture, that you do not twist it.
Et se li exirnach n’apert en l’encomencement de la fendure, si acroi un poc la fendure legierement tant qu’il apere; puis l’estrai si com nos avons dit, puis moille drapelz en aisil et en aigue, et met sus le leu, et estrain de bendelz.	2. If the thread does not open at the beginning of the fringe, then lightly open it as soon as it appears; then pull it as we have said, and then knot the threads in a loop and tie them with a knot, and place them on the shoulder, and tie them firmly.
Et si a de tels homes qui broient seil et mettent sus por corrompre cele moistor qui est demoree.	3. And if such men who bruise their sails and put on to corrupt the moisture which is dried up.
Puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the doctor when he is healthy.
Et s’il vient au leu aposteme chaut, si lou cure d’emplaustres assouajant tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess comes to the leu, then the doctor should use incisions that are gentle when he is healthy.
des poilz des papieres	hairs of the papers
Quant em papieres naissent poilz ajostez autre que li naturez, et sont enveillit, si nuisent as eulz, et font venir manieres de maladies si com larmes acostumees et mollifications des papieres et albugine, tant que c’est cause de la destruction des eulz; et est li cure selonc IIII manieres: ou par cautere ensamble feu, ou par medicine ague selonc ceu qu’il est devant ou chapistre de cautere, et est fais ou par incision et costure ou par caines, selonc ceu que je dirai.	When hairs are found on papers other than their nature, and they are awakened, if they harm the eyes, and bring about diseases such as common tears and softening of the paper and albugine, until it is caused by the destruction of the hairs; and the cure is done in four ways: either by burning together with fire, or by medicine according to what is before or in the chapter of cauterization, and it is made by cutting and stitching or by ties, according to what I will say.
Il covient que tu mettes lou chief dou malaide en ton sain, puis torne la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre; s’elle est convertie, c’est boin; se ceu non, si i boute une aguille a tout I fil desus; et soit ce delez la marge de la papiere ou li poil naissent delez ces poilz, et trai I fil au desus a tout la papiere, et la torne au raseur; puis fent en la partie desoz la papiere, desoz les poilz ajostez, a tout le spatumile copant, des le grant larmier jusc’au petit; puis estrai I fil, et met desoz la papiere une petite tente de couton et de drapeil, puis seigne sus la papiere une figure d’enche, si com la fuelle de mirte, et toutevoie il covient que li figure soit selonc la quantiteit que tu vues eslever la papiere qui est devisez a toz.	1. It is necessary that you place the handle of the maid's lancet in your hand, then turn the paper of the oil to your left hand; if it turns, it is good; if not, then insert an awl into all the threads of the filament; and let the margin of the paper or the hair that comes from these hairs be at the edge of the paper, and turn the filament to the raseur; then cut off the part of the paper opposite the lancet, straighten the hairs, and apply it to all the stitches, from the large one to the small; then pull out the filament, and put a small piece of cotton and a drapery on top of the paper, then sew around the figure on the paper, as if it were the buttonhole of a glove, and it should be according to the quantity that you see rising the paper that is marked with the dots.
Et si a teil qui a mestier c’on cope grant quantiteit de la papiere selonc ceu que li papiere est mollifie; puis fent a tout le spatumile sus les II lignes que tu as signiet, et comence des lou grant larmier jusc’a petit; et soit li une des fendures pres des poilz naturez en la groissece d’un raiz, puis boute l’oncine en l’un des II angles dou keur, puis l’escorche toute; puis assemble les II levres a une costure d’une aguille a tout I fil de laine subtil, et essue le sanc, et fai aerdre la superfluiteit des filz sus les II sorcilz a tout aucunes choses gluans, se tu vues faire ce; et se ce non, si n’en aies cure, puis laisse la costure et les filz jusc’a III jors ou IIII; puis cure la plaie sens costure de choses sechans et constrignans, car li papiere se relive au soudement de la plaie et l’assemblement de li, mais li costure est muedre (si com dirent li ancien), et c’est ovraiges sens paor; et si a une autre maniere: et est que tu seignes la papiere d’une figure qui soit ausi com li fuelle de mirte, si com nos avons conteit, a III oncines desevrez selonc la forme qui est ci:	If a part of the body has a large amount of paper stuck to it, according to the type of paper, then cut all the threads along the lines you have written, and start with a large sharp scissors at the beginning; and one of the holes near the natural hair growth in its lengthening, then pull out the hair at one of the two angles, then burn it; then assemble the two lips at a stitch with an awl at all the fine thread of the yarn, and draw out the suture, and sew away the superfluity of the threads on the two corners of any thing gluing, if you see this done; and if not, then leave the stitch and the threads just as they are or four or five; then cure the wound at the costure of things that are dry and constricting, because the paper relieves the wound and its assembly, but the costure is dead (as they say the ancient ones), and this is overrated; and if in another way: and it is that you see the paper of a figure which is also like the fur of the marten, as we have counted, at three incisions will follow the form that is here:
puis cope ceu qui sormonte as petites forces igalment selonc la forme qui est ci:	Then comes he who overcomes with equal strength according to the form as it is now:
Et se tu n’as pooir de tenir les tenailles, et li chose n’est mie igalz, si prent une aguille ou il ait I fil, et la boute emmi la figure; et boute I autre fil delez lou grant larmier, et lou secont fil delez lou petit, et assemble entre tes dois les filz igalment; puis lieve ta main igalment, et lieve tout le cuir sus coi tu as signiet, si com nos avons conteit, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie par costure, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se aposteme vient a ton incision, si l’apaise de cerote et de semblans oignement assouajans; et aucune fois avient que li poil de la papiere sont convertit: si covient que tu uses ceu que nos avons dit de l’incision; mais li costure en l’une et en l’autre est plus artificialz.	Then if you cannot hold the nails, and the thing is not even, then take a needle or a thread, and pull it out; and take another thread of equal length for the large arm, and a smaller one for the small, and assemble the threads evenly; then gently close your hand evenly, and gently stitch all the edges where you have sewn, as we have experienced, then close the lips of the wound with stitches, and treat it until it is healthy; and if the suture comes to your incision, if the edge is smooth and even; and never has there been that the hair of the paper is converted: if you use what we have said about the incision; but the stitching in one and the other is more artificial.
Li cure des caines si est selonc ceste forme: et est que tu convertisses la papiere et la fent dedens selonc ceu que j’ai dit, et puis fai II caines par art, et II liiens subtilz ausi lonc com li papiere et li largesce dou spatumile est; et cope as II chiés de II pars ou tu tiens les filz; puis assemble l’un et l’autre subtilment sus ceu que sormonte de la papiere de l’oil, et estrain les II cainnes des II parties forment; et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, et li cuir qui iert estrainte morra et nercira et porrira, tant qu’il cherra par lui.	1. The cure for rabies follows this form: and if you convert the paper and make it according to what I have said, then make the dog's jaws according to art, and make them subtle as long as the paper and the broadness of the tail is; and cover as the heads of the parts you hold the threads for; then assemble one and the other subtly under what surpasses the paper of the oil, and straighten the dog's jaws from the two parts formed; and leave no others, and the leather that is stretched will die and turn black and rot as much as it can.
S’il tarde, si le cope a unes forces, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et quant li plaie iert soudee, et si ert levee li papiere, et ne poindront plus li poil; et c’est li forme des II cainnes que tu feras selonc ceste figure, et selonc ceste quantiteit de lonc et de large:	If it is delayed, if the wound has force, then the care as soon as possible; and when the wound is healed, and the paper is lifted up, and the hair does not bind more; and this is the form of the two points that you will make according to this figure, and according to this quantity of long and wide:
li ovraiges est telz que tu preignes une aguille subtil, et i boute I fil de soie souef et subtil; puis assemble les chiés et noe l’un et l’autre subtilment, et soit li longesce des filz une palme de lonc; puis ordene en la chasse I autre fil subtil de soie briément, et noe les chief dou fil; puis mette li malaides son chief en ton sain; et soit delez lou soleil si que li ovraiges soit declairiez, car c’est uns ovraiges subtilz et menus, puis boute l’aguille a tout la chasse en la racine dou poil ajosteit, et la fai percier en la papiere hastanment tant que tu la traies desus lou poil natureil; puis estrai le poil jusque sus la chasse, et boute en la chasse celui poil, s’il en i a I ou II ou III ou plusors; puis estrai ta main tant que li poilz veigne fuers a tout la chasse en la papiere avec lou poil natureil.	The incisions are such that you will use a fine needle, and a thread of silk fine and thin; then assemble the ends and gently pull them together, and make the length of the threads as long as possible; then take another fine thread of silk finely, and pull the other end, and put the mallet on your hand; and if the incisions are clean, it will be because the incisions are subtle and small, then pull the needle through all the chase at the root of the natural hair, and make it perceive in the paper as much as you move it against the natural hair; then pull the hair until it is all through the chase, and pull out the hair in the chase, if there are one or two or three or more; then pull your hand as much as the hair comes all through the chase with the natural hair.
Et se li chasse est traite et li poilz ne vient fuer avec li, si trairas la chasse au desoz a tout le fil que tu i as ordeneit, tant que li chasse veigne fuer dou pertus desus et que tu la voies par la vision de l’oil; adonques si trairas la chasse et le fil, et clo l’oil et lou laisse clo II jors ou III, tant que li poil s’aerde en son leu et naisse li char sus; et se li poilz est petis, si acompaigne I poil lonc des chevoulz naturez, et soit alevez avec celui ou tu le laisse, tant qu’il soit eslongiez et puis le lieve.	When the fur is cut, it is treated and the hair does not grow with it, if you treat the fur as far as the end of the thread that you have ordered, as long as the fur grows with difficulty and you see it through the oil; therefore, if you treat the fur and the thread, close the oil and leave it closed for two or three days, as long as the hair grows in its place and the char is born; and if the hair is short, if it is accompanied by one long tail of nature, and is separated with that which you let it be, as long as it is elongated and then tied.
de la porriture de l’oil	Of the oily substance
Quant ceste maladie qui est apelee «aleacrati» ou li porriture vient en l’oil, si en i a de II manieres: l’une natureil, et l’autre innatureil.	When this disease, which is called "aleacrati" or the oily substance comes in two ways: naturally and unnaturally.
Et avient par soudement de plaie, ou de tailleure ou de cautere, et par semblans choses.	And comes through wounds, or cuts, or burns, and in similar ways.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige en li est que tu fendes celle soudure, et dessevre les levres de li, et met dedens tentes de lin, et la lie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et ne covient mie que tu uses en la cure de li de choses que sechent et restraignent.	And the way of the ointment is to apply it as you do with the wound, and lick the lips of it, and put lint on it until it is healthy; and only what is needed is to use in the cure of it things that dry and restrict.
Car se tu fais ceu, si revient li maladie pire que li premiere; mais i oevre de choses amollissans, si com fenugreic; et l’arose d’aigue ou altee et semence de lin soient cuites, et oignemens dyaquilon fondut en aucun des oiles, et i envoloupe une tente, et le cure de ceu.	For if you do this, the disease worsens than the first; but the work of things that make one worse, is like fenugreek; and the root of Agnus Castus or the seed of Linum is cooked, and all oils are melted into none of them, and it is wrapped in a tent, and the cure of this.
Et li tresors de ta cure si est que tu te dones en garde qu’ele ne soude mie selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant; et cist ovraiges que nos avons dit nen est fuers que adresemens de ceste maladie, qu’elle ne reviegne selonc la forme qu’elle fut devant.	And the treasure of your cure is that you give in guard that it does not sound like according to the form it was before; and this work that we have said no one has been found that cures this disease, that it does not recur according to the form it was before.
de la char qui vient en l’oil	From the charge that comes in the oil
Ceste maladie que est desoz qui vraiement est apelee «axacrati», et est naturelz et accidens.	This disease, which is truly called "acarati", is natural and accidental.
Li accidens vient de plaie et de fendure et de cautere et de choses semblans; et li voie de l’ovraige en li si est que tu preignes un aguille, en coi il ait I fil double, et la fiche en la char, et li fai percier des le senestre larmier tant c’a destre, si que li filz veigne en II chiés de la char; puis estent la char au desus a tout l’aguille, et la cope a I spatumile large.	The accident comes from wounding and bruising and cauterization and things similar; and the sight of the patient is that you see a needle, if it has double thread, and the char in the shoulder, and it feels like the left side is further than the right, so that the thread comes in the head of the shoulder; then the char is at the end of all the needle, and the cop is in the large spatulate.
Et se li figure de la papiere revient selonc ceu qu’il covient, c’est boin; se ceu non, si pren I raseur et le met en la fendure, et torne la papiere, et fent II fendures ou costeit dedens la papiere; et soient li chiés des II fendures des II angles de l’incision que tu as copeit, et soit fais uns angles si que quant elles sont assemblees, que li figure soit ausi com li figure d’une lettre qui a non «I griesche»; puis oste celle char, selonc la quantiteit que ses costez est agus desoz, de ceu qui enseut la papiere, puis ajoste les II parties desevrees, et les cout d’un fil de lainne; puis lou cure de ceu que nos avons dit des medicines mollifians, et de tentes, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the paper returns according to what is needed, it is good; but if not, take the rasor and put it in the wound, and turn the paper, and make two or three wounds, and let the chiers of the two angles of the incision be together, so that when they are assembled, the figure may be like that of a letter without "I griesche"; then set the char according to the quantity of the edges that the rasor has cut, from which it draws the paper, then adjust the disconnected parts, and make them of one thread of linen; then apply what we have said about the mollificating medicines and tents, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li maladie vient de fendure ou de costure ou de cautere, si covient que tu fendes une fendure plainne desoz les poilz des papieres, et selonc ceu qui est ci devant; puis desevre entre les II leivres d’une tente, si com j’ai dit; et doit on faire l’ovraige selonc la forme de la maladie, car elle est mout diverse en forme, et li saiges maistres appareille engien de tout som pooir coment il faice revenir la figure a sa forme natureil; et li malaides meisme, selonc ceu qu’il i covient d’ovraige et d’estrumens em plusors dispositions.	If the disease comes from frost or friction or burning, then it is necessary to remove a layer of paper from the hair, according to what is in front; then enter between the two legs of a tent, as I have said; and it must be done according to the shape of the disease, because it is different in shape, and the skilled masters can adjust everything according to how it comes back to its natural figure; and the patient themselves, according to what they need from excision and extraction in various positions.
dou soudement de la papiere	I would shave off the paper.
Quant ceste soudure avient a mains homes en teil maniere que li papiere desus est sodee avec le blanc de l’oil, et ne puet movoir ne faire ses ovraiges naturez, si covient donques que tu i boutes la pointe d’un raseur desoz la papiere, et la lieve en haut; et l’estent as pinceures, tant que tu copes ceu qui est aert au spatumile subtil, qui ne soit mie trop agus ne trop trenchans, si que li malaides ne puisse soffrir que li spatumile trop agus ne blecent l’oil; et soit ton incision, dont tu escorche celle assemblee, legierement, si que li papiere reviegne selonc sa forme natureil; et est sanee toute celle assemblee, et font aucune fois en l’oil aigue salee, et le leve d’aigue douce, et de coliere; puis met entre la papiere et l’oil une tente de lin, et met sus l’oil laine moillie en abun d’uef; et aprés le tier jor use dou coliere et des choses soudans tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. When this cauterization comes to the hands of women in a certain way that the paper attached is soaked with white oil, and cannot move or perform its natural acts, then it is necessary that you cut the tip of a razor with the paper, and lift it above; and the pins are placed on the subtle spumous matter which is not too much nor too thin, so that the patient does not suffer from the spumous matter too much nor let the oil become rancid; and your incision, which you scrape off that assembled one, gently so that the paper returns to its natural form; and it is healed completely, and no once in the acidic cold water, and the levain douce and the coliere; then put a linen tent between the paper and the oil, and put on the oil fine hair in an abundance of yew; and afterwards the third day use the cold and sour things as long as it is healthy.
de l’ungle de l’oil	Of the finger of the oil
Saiches que li ungle est selonc II manieres: elle est nervouse et semblans a I dur syfac, et une autre qui n’est mie nervouse, mais est semblans a blainche moistor congelee, que quant on la touche de fer et on la cuide panre as pinceures, si ne puet om; et l’une et l’autre semblance encomence devers le grant larmier, et croist poc et poc tant qu’ele cuevre toute la veue et toute la lumiere et le movement de l’oil.	There are two ways in which the finger appears: it is nervous and resembles hard skin, and another that is not nervous but resembles dry, moist glass that, when touched with iron and cooked with pincers, cannot be moved; and both resemble the greatest terror, growing little by little until it covers all vision and light and movement of the oil.
Et li maniere de l’incision si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz; et lieve la papiere a ta main, puis coil l’ungle as pinceures de petite doubleure, et l’estent au desus; puis pren une aguille, et i met I poil de cheval, ou de vaiche, ou de buef, et I fil fort; et double la pointe de l’aguille un poc et la fiche emmi l’ungle, et la perce a tout l’aguille, et lie l’ungle d’un fil et l’estent au desus, et escorche a tout lou poil le costeit de l’ungle qui enseut la prunele et la soie au poil jusc’au chief, puis cope lou remanant en la racine dou larmier a tout lou spatumile subtil et as petites forces, et laisse la char natureil ou larmier, si que par l’incision ne veigne li cors des larmes acostumeement; et aucune fois s’estent li ungle a l’oncine soulement, et au fil, si com nos avons dit; puis l’escorche on a tout le spatumile souef de coi ci est li forme:	And the way of the incision is that the surgeon places his finger in the wound, then operates on the nail; and gently fold the paper to your hand, then take pliers with a small diameter, and hold the horsehair, or sheephair, or beaver hair, or the thread; and double the point of the needle a little and the thread enters the nail, and perforate all the needle, and tie the nail to a thread and pull it out of the wound, and scrape off all the hair from the costeit of the nail that extends the prunele and the silk to the chief, then cut the remaining in the root of the most terrible part with subtle forces, and leave the natural or terrible form, so that by the incision does not come the tears customarily; and never has the finger stayed at the wound only, and over time, as we have said; then it is scorched all the spatumile soaked in coi ci is the form:
Et garde que li spatumile ne touche la toile charnue et la rompe, et que li prunele ne soit percie; et aprés l’incision giete en l’oil un poc de seil broiet, et dou coliere fait de litargire, et le laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; puis le cure de ceu qu’il i covient tant qu’il soit sanez.	And keep the spatula from touching the charred skin and breaking it, and make sure the pruning does not pierce; then after making an incision in the oil, a small piece of hemp is added, and light is given, and it is left until the next day; then the care for what is needed until it is healthy.
Et se li ungle n’est mie nervouse, et tu ne pues bouter l’aguille, et li uncines n’i puet entrer, maintes fois est curee ceste semblance d’ungle de medicines; et naissent sicom j’ai conteit en la division, et se tu la vues coper, si oevre l’oil dou malaide, et pren le spatumile legier poc agut selonc ceste forme:	And if the nail is not nervous, and you do not push the needle, and the unci do not enter, this appearance of a nail is often treated with medicines; and I have seen this in division, and if you see it cope, then use oil on the nail according to the form of this spatula:
Et reis l’ungle desus subtilment, et se tu vois qu’elle amenuise point et li rasion i apresse, si distille de ta bouche en l’oil coliere fait de litargire et dou coliere rouge et seil broiet, et estoupe l’oil jusc’a l’autre jor; puis rencomence l’autre ovraige selonc ceste meisme oevre, tant qu’elle soit toute ostee.	And remove the nail subtly, and if you see that it does not change and the skin is pressed, then distill from your mouth into the oil made of laurel and red college and white sorrel, and it stupefies the oil to the other day; then continue the other prick according to this same work, as long as it is completely healed.
Se aucune chose ne t’est contraire en l’oil, si com aposteme chaus, adonques la lait, et cure premier l’aposteme chaut tant qu’il soit sanez, puis rencomence l’ovraige si com devant, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If nothing is against you in the oil, as with an abscess, then the milk, and first treat the abscess as soon as it is healthy, then continue the prick as before, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li apparance de la chair dou larmier nuit en l’oil par grant nuisement, si la sospent a l’oncine, et en cope une partie et non mie tot, que cors de larmes n’i viegne; puis distille en l’oil coliere rouge qui est fais de litargire.	And if the appearance of the flesh of the arm is dark in the oil due to great intoxication, and it is exhausted in the bone, and only a part is not entirely, that there are no tears; then it distills into the oil that is red and spicy, which is made from sweating.
de la char qui naist sus la prunelle	of the wood that was carved by the plum tree
Es eulz d’aucuns homes naist aucune fois char rouge, et cuevre la prunele et restraint sus les papieres et les torne au defuer, et semble une rose de balauste; et li ovraiges si est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, puis li oevre les eulz, et coil toute celle char as uncines convenaubles a ceu, et la sostien a la force; puis cope la premiere char, et vai tout copant au raseur jusc’a la fin, et te garde que tu ne bleces l’oil a l’ovraige; et soit li incision dou spatumile que nos avons dit en l’incision de l’ungle et as petites forces de coi on oste lou sebel, si com li forme aprés cest chapistre lou demostre; et quant li incision est acomplie et ostee toute li char, si emple l’oil de seil broiet ou tu i distille coliere rouge et semblans medicines corrosives, et met sus l’oil defuer coton avec abin d’uef, si qu’il soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut; et s’il i demore rien, et li sans chaus te sormonte, et tu doutes aposteme chaut, si laisse l’oil et cure l’aposteme de choses apaisant aposteme chaut; puis revien a ton ovraige tant qu’il soit sanez, et ensi fai cant chars est ajostee en l’oil par ceste semblance.	Some men have never seen red wood, and cut the plum tree and tear off the leaves and roll them on paper and tie them with strings, and it looks like a rose of balsam; and if the patients are such that they put their head in the ointment, then they apply the ointment to the wounds, and spread all this red wood as adjustable charges for this, and support it with force; then cut the first charge, and take everything to the rasor just at the end, and keep the oil away from the opening; and the incision of the spatumile that we have said in the incision of the finger and small forces of coi on the bone, if it forms after this chapter as we have shown; and when the incision is completed and takes all the charge, if you use ointment of hemp or oil distilled red and resembles medicines corrosive, and put it on the ointment with a piece of cloth, if it is assured of aposteme chaut; and if it does not cost anything, and the without chaus comes over you, and you doubt aposteme chaut, if leave the ointment and cure aposteme chaut with things calming aposteme chaut; then return to your opening as soon as it is healthy, and then make many charges adjusted in the ointment by this appearance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you treat every weak point of the natural way; and of the accidental way, in fire; and do not force your hand into any of these burns as long as you see that the member is affected by that burn.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	These are red veins that are covered with oil, and they touch the eye and blunt the oil for all time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	Therefore, the first thing you see is the oil, and if it is red, it is false, and there is no other disease than this redness; therefore, in this way: instruct the patient to put his head in your hand, then tie those veins all around according to your wisdom, and make them double according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And let there be as many as one thousand degrees in one corpse according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	Then use your forces subtly on those hairs that are still attached to the oil, and remove them as soon as you can see them; do not cut the oil with the points of your fingers, and perform this operation before midday in the sun, and be very careful in your operation so that you do not cut into anything else; and when you have done this, distill the green and red oil that will come out to corrode what is left.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	And if you cannot cut all of it in that hour, make a plaster with the pain-relieving oil and leave some parts until the pain is relieved and the swelling is reduced, then resume according to this method as long as it is safe; and this is the form of the forces:
de la fistule de l’oil	Of the fistula of the oil
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula of the oil is called "arissati" when it is cured by cauterization and by using burning medicine according to what I have previously mentioned, and if it is not completely healed, then it should be opened at the site of the incision, and all the moisture that is inside should be removed, as long as the os is discovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the os is discovered, and you will see corruption and blackness, if all the instruments of this case are of the same form, and it is called "spray chief," and should be made firmly in the chief, and should not be pointed like a lime if it is in the present form:
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And bend the corrupt bone of the leg, then twist it between your two hands, and press your hand a little as you feel that corruption is removed; and do this no more than once, then restore the leg with medicated ointments.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If the wound is seen and cleaned, and the belly is cleansed, and the abscess in the belly is seen and remains for forty days, and it does not relieve or become gangrenous, and no other remedy is found than to bring the fistula back to the urethra according to this form: then take a second piece of bone from the bone the second time by chiseling and by medicated ointments, and if it comes out with the wound according to this form, and so is the head of the chisel at three angles, and the fistula should be softened as much as possible according to what you see:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the forceps on the edge of the scar, and move your hand away from the oil I pod, then turn the entire forehead until it pierces the bone and feels the pain as if you are holding your hand on your neck; and then restore the dry medicine leg of the patient as I have shown you, and when the child grows and hardens the legs, if the matter is in the neck, then it is a lighter thing for the midwife.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the oil's end
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the wound is completely open and there is no discharge from the navel, and the midwife does not arrive, then you must apply the ointment to the midwife; then cleanse the wound with a sponge that does not hurt by sucking, then place it on the oil I lien made of acacia and aloe and incense and sarcocolle, and then strain the oil, and apply it to the bands and cloths; and if the cloths are too wet, double each by four, and then put one on top of the other according to the amount that the child has used; then strain the ointment with bands firmly formed, and resume the sucking without hurting; then loosen the bands and let the oil be dried overnight and in the morning, if it is tight, tighten the bandage, the navel, and the midwife; and if not, then see if the ointment is healed, it is good; if not, then repeat the application and the bandages and the midwife and the sucking as long as it is healthy.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	Great disturbance of the eyeball
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When disturbances come to the eyeball, it opens wide and presents a mass of paper as small as a grain of resin; therefore, if you cover your eyes, the eyebrow is so thick that you can insert an awl at the root of the part where the eye socket is, then insert another awl where the double thread of the eyebrow is; and see, leave the first awl according to its position; then press on the double thread and draw out a part of the eyeball, and hold it tightly, then remove the awl and put some ointment in a large amount of urine; and leave it until the threads are no longer attached to the eyeball, and cure the wound with comforting things as soon as the pain is healed; and never leave the wound uncovered by the eyebrow, as long as it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs grow long and thick, then prick them gently with a subtle needle that comes from the oil, and wipe away the moisture and let them fall, and come back together as soon as possible; then pluck them once they are healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil's bowl
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease called "alcunnati" is not other than the bowes assembled in the oil, resembling bitter-tasting dew; and this manner of appearance of the shoulder is when you make the patient sit at the physician's seat and right side up, then take the chief between your hands of II parts, and pull as much as you see the bow coming to the desus on your hairs; then it should be clean, and the light should not come out of it, and see what the malady does; and if it does not come out, think that it is bitter, and if the dew comes from the bow is not assembled as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you place the patient's arm in your hands, then take the subtle spatula and insert it under the corneal layer through the continuation of the conjunctiva with the cornea and the sclera, as much as possible; and when it comes out, let it drip into the cold water mixed with honey, or hot or fenugreek is boiled and honey, then it should be treated with another treatment until it is cured.
des aigues de l’oil	of the cold water
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have seen the appearances of the waters in the division, and when it comes to measure; if according to the health it is.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	1. It is necessary that you hold the patient's arm in your hands, towards the light of the sun, and make the healthy and tight oil squeeze out; then place the paper of the oil on your left hand so that the hairs are on the left, or on your right hand so that the hairs are on the right; then take with your right hand, if the hairs are on the left, the instrument called "almagda," or with your left hand, if the hairs are on the right; then place the point of the instrument at the coronet through the narrowest part of the oil in the blenchor of the hair at the smallest part of the arm, then push the instrument called "almagda" gently, and twist your hand until it pierces the blenchor of the oil, and feel that almagda enters the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the almagda hole be at the front of the measure of the espagice which is in the prunes at the end of the nose; and this is the coronet of the oil; if you see the bone in the paper for the clarity of the cornered skin, and then place the instrument where it is in the eye or where the eye is, then press the hole after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If the patient feels faint now, if they see the surgeon in front of them and the instrument before them.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After resting for a little while, and the patient feels better, open the second vein, insert the forceps with the instrument, and when it is firmly held and does not move, gently twist your hand a little at a time; then remove a few drops of blood, and lift the oil from it.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then pour the oil into the wound, either coarse or finely ground in oil and a large amount of oil, and mix it with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Yes, and those who are ours, put on cloths with a large amount of oil.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	And if the stone cannot enter the kidney through its hardness, because it has too many sharp hairs, then you must use the instrument called "alberit" which is in this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And by piercing only the conjunctive, and not too deeply, but make it subtle, then insert the stone, as we have said; and at the end of the operation, the patient should be lying on his back in the dark room; and he should be given light foods, and no movement to the right or left, and he should be placed according to his position, and then leave him alone in this house, and close his eyes, and make him see anything he wants, and then put it back where it was on the ninth day; and it is only necessary that you do this in the eye of the cure or after the incision now, but it is necessary that you remove it, because the heat rises suddenly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	When the patient feels pain, move the oil in front of the ninth day, and apply the ointment that calms the pain; and when it is soothed, close the eye and put it in your face to cover any joint, and stay in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	Then go to a small house and convert into your case; and advise that no disciples should undergo this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	Then some came to us who were from the Yrach, who told us that in some years it happened an omen of the end of the world, but we have never seen it here, nor do we read about it in ancient books; and by chance, this is a new thing.
