Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And be the head of this very subtlety, and the tail in three angles.
de la char sor le neis	of the fire sor the need.
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	No time are born or dislocated any different kinds of fires, for there are none that seem like scorpions at the mouth of the teeth; and if it is of such kind or has a dislocated fire surrounded by different colors, and if it is a dislocated fire with good color.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In that case of these fires which are not enhanced, and do not enhance, it is necessary that you place the patient between your hands before the sun; and blow on his nostrils, and make the onion touch those fires, and then remove them; so that you can hold it steady in the subtle spatium of a part, as long as you feel that this fire is all set.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is nothing else that can be done, if you examine all the instruments subtly and lightly, without causing any harm; and if it does not overwhelm you, or cause an abscess, if it is a malignant one, then quickly cauterize as much as possible, until the bones are not stained and are all osteons, then apply ointment or wine.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If you do not have any other choice, if moisture comes to the palace, and it is healthy; and if moisture does not penetrate as much as it should, then it has caused damage to the bone of the tooth, or the instruments cannot be cut: therefore, it is necessary to tie a thread of linen around a large knot, and it should be in the hands of those who are making it; and put the head of the sharp edge into the child's mouth, and let it odorize as it comes out through the mouth; and many times make this for the child in schools, and it is a light thing for those who see it; then hold the end that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other hand that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and keep them side by side until they are all done.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	1. Do as much as you can see that the child has corrupted the char, then take the son's penis, cleanse the blood, and wipe the son's penis with Egyptian ointment, and put it back in the urethra as before; do this 3 times or more, as long as the ointment corrodes all that is left of the char; then put a piece of cloth on the urethra for some time until it is healthy, and if he has any skills in drying herbs, then use them; and this is the form of the instrument to purge the child's penis, or it is used to distill the oils and medicines or the urethra.
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	And let it be of silver or gold, resembling a hollow lamp, like a cane, and you will lead it thus; and if you see, if a cane is closed, and it has flat ends to expel the wax, and there should be a hand at the head to hold it when heating the oil or no liquid.
de la char sor le neis	And of the char for the head.
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	Many times the head is infected with a disease called "telul", and grows and becomes large, until it is visible to look at; therefore it is necessary that you cut it at the beginning, and all of it, then put on the cauteries or the burning medicine; and if you delay it as long as it is large, if it is hard, of a dark color, poor sense: if it does not touch any iron because it is enchanted, for when you cut it never once, if evil comes to the patient; and if the cauteries are too hot, not of iron, but you see that you can cover them, if the patient's mouth is open and the cauteries are too painful, and you can cure him of things that are dry and restricting.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	When the joint is cut and bruised
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Said that when a solution for continuation comes from one of these cartilages, it does not last long, and is only in some people.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	It is therefore necessary to do this if there is none in any case; look if the wound is fresh at all its base; and then treat it with a bandage, until it is healthy; and if the lips are already swollen on both sides, it is necessary that you scrape all the parts of it as they become healthy, then assemble the lips with a bandage, extract it, and powder it with dragon's blood powder and incense; and put some pieces of plaster on it, of strong or other plaster soothing, and leave it as long as it is soothed by it, then treat the ointment as it is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	1. The manner of the sewing if you assemble the solution: either by needles, as we have said in the sewing of the abdomen; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	2. of the abscesses of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	3. that the teeth of the gums are hard, resembling grains of sand, and smaller and larger; therefore, it is necessary to open the lips, and each tooth is extracted, and they are held with pliers and pulled out in each part; then use the lemon after the incision of vitreoli broiet, as long as it is not dried; and then the lemon juice, and cure the lemon of things dry until it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	Of the thigh bone
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times the thigh bone is dislocated, which is called "albulus"; if you can hold it with your nails, and the hip with its root, and leave the wound or the sinus; then put on the leg a vitrol-powdered bandage, or other adhesives and desiccant; and if the bone returns after the incision, and many times it does, if it is second time cauterized; and this is the form of the strumens.
des sordens	of soreness
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	None are ever assembled at the root of the teeth, the teeth being sore and sharp; and none are ever the black and yellow tooth, as long as corruption comes to the gum, and it becomes the yellow tooth; if you can make the patient hold his tooth in your hands, and his gums be in your holy mouth, and expose the teeth or the sore spots, as long as there is nothing; and then I make of black and green, and of yellow and jaundice, and of other stains, as they are made; and if this is the first reason, it is good; but if not, let it recur in the second day and night, until you have all exposed; and take care that the teeth have different forms of strumens to relieve, according to what the patient demonstrates, for the raser which is used to sharpen the teeth has other forms than those used between the teeth; and these forms and others are prepared with you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary when you treat the tooth of your pain that you delay as long as possible and as much as you can, because it should not be done; for it is a substance of high value, therefore there is no excuse for not doing it.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	When the patient is forced to take medicine, then you must be sure of the tooth's pain.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Many times the patient's pain has passed, and make sure it is not toothache, and give the tooth medicine; and do not leave the tooth's pain because of this, as long as the tooth is extracted, for we have already wanted to do this for these better ones; and when you are sure of the tooth's pain, if it comes out completely from the tooth, then scrape it with a spatula hard enough to warn the gums of all parts; then the mouth has your needles in the first pocket and the second, as much as they are well inserted, then they confirm the needles; and put the patient's head between your hands and hold it so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After the tooth is extracted sensibly with forceps, and if it does not slip, then take none of these strings and pull lightly on each part, and move it as you have done first.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the teeth are felt and drawn out, then it is best to fill them with cloth, wherever the holes are; and if the extraction is done subtly with needles, which does not break the tooth; and it is wise to overturn the gum over the tooth to clean the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And be very careful not to break the tooth, and there will remain a part, and it will return to the patient due to the malice of the root and greater pain in the first.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	1. And you should not make a knife like those that ignorant healers make, who with their haste and their hardiness break the needle never, and they do not harm anyone what we have counted; but they make it once by the weakness of this great disease through its roots that they do not endure, or by the needle that they break, as often as we want; and when it is cold, if you wash the handle with wine or vinegar and silk; and if they come out of the suture and enter, which often happens, if you use the handle of vitriol, then if it does not work, if it cauterizes.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The forms of the wisdom teeth, or the first molars, are long and thick at their points and roots, and they do not double in size when you grind the tooth; these are the forms:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And they should be thick members if they do not break when ground, and they should be made of good iron, and they should be teeth that can be held tightly.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root of the tooth dries out when ground, it comes to pass that you must put the gauze on the cheek for an hour or more.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the root is smoothed, it cuts the points called "algorifs," and if the heads seem well-shaped, they should be made like a lime and this is the form:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not come out of all these thorns, then it comes that you pull out the whole branch at the root, and put in the instrument called "athali", which is known as a "palinch", and its shape is like this:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And it should be as thick and strong as possible, if it does not break the skin, and if the root jumps from this, it is good; but if not, then use all the force, and the forms will come after like this:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you use it with two rains, then the shape is like this:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other instruments that are before in the reason of the teeth, and with this instrument which seems like great thorns, whose shape is like this:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And so it is that the fracture is not too difficult to break, and the tools are sharp and of good quality; and other fractures, which are not as contrived; and the surgeons master the subtlety of their instruments according to their own will and the disease they demonstrate, because they have some diseases or the ancients did not teach any instrument for the diversity of bones and hands, or it breaks not at the right angle or other bones, or it fractures, if it seeks the fractures that I have said, and helps with gestures, according to the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And be large and well-holding the bone, so it does not break, but can hold and set; and then restore the strength of the medicines appropriate for this, and if there is in the bone a fissure, and it is small, if all this instrument is needed:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears to not follow the natural course of the body, and its form is misshapen, and at the same time in women with multiple teeth, if it comes out after the tooth, and it is not in its right place, and it cannot be soaked or polished: then remove it; and if it is with the tooth, if it takes this instrument whose form is like the small beak, and is sharp and tempered in iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And quickly and quickly in the hands, for the hardness of the teeth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears like this, then you can tie it with a part of the rope as this is formed:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	And it is like the rope for making hooks; and in the rope the teeth little by little in the hands lightly, so that it does not move until it chips; then the end is without any rasping, and if the teeth are too sharp and they bend the tongue, then it is necessary to tighten the grip as much as possible so that it does not bend the tongue or distort the speech.
quant li dent lochent	When the teeth rot
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the teeth rot (before), either by percussion or by chewing, and the patient cannot press on them as they chew, and you treat them with restraining medicines, and it does not work; if it comes to being restrained by a golden thread, because the silver threads turn green and putrid, but the gold does not move at all; and if the thread is too thick or too thin, according to the quantity of space between the teeth; and if you see the teeth, take a golden thread and a silver thread double between the two healthy teeth, then place the threads between the decayed teeth, as long as you see improvement in the healthy tooth on the other side; then resume the covering where you left off, and gently and wisely pull your hand, so that it does not move at all; and if your finger is at the root of the tooth if it can escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then fasten the head of the thread to some nails, and assemble them, and place them between the healthy teeth, and put it on so that it does not bend the tongue; and then leave it as short as possible, and if it does not hold, or the thread slips, if the other threads are tight; if it holds and serves for all its length, and this is the form of the teeth and the shape of the incisors of the second teeth and the second molars, as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth comes out, if you put it back in its place, it should be done gently and not forcefully, as we have said; and it should never be made into a bone-like tooth, and you put it back in its place where it was, and if it does not hold, and is held for as long as it can be, and it is tight as we have said:
de coper lou liien de la lengue	Of the copper wire of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is the tongue that comes out of the mouth or nature; or by accident of wounding; and the wires are such that you open the mouth of the patient, and it has its head in the mouth of the healer, and relaxes the tongue; then cut off the nervous wire as wide as the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if it becomes hard or breaks, and this is due to pain, if the tooth bites it and cuts off a large part of it; and make sure that the fingers do not become too tight, for the artery that is out; and when you have done, if the tongue is red and swollen, or cold, then put the tongue in a linen tent; and the patient will be examined every night by the physician, so that the patient can be cured.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the wound becomes infected, if it is not treated with warm vitrier broth; and if it does not heal, if it is cauterized with a slow fire cautery, which is good for this; then the treatment of another treatment until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound appears to be red or black or hard, and the patient does not feel it, and it is not touched, because it is gangrene; and if it is declining into a blennorrhoid, and it is moist, and the sanies ooze from the urethra, and the wound is filled with a subtle spumous substance, and the discharge is from one part and another; and if the patient does not heal in your care, if you treat it with warm vitrier broth as much as possible, then return to your care as soon as you can manage everything; then lift the leg of silk and seal, and the treatment of other treatments until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	gums of the chin
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	Never comes the gums of the chin called "godaths", and they are properly called amandas, and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they are not healthy, then keep them: if they are hard and of small size and white color, and not red, and not hot, and not cold.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if it is red and the root is large, and not hot, and not cold, then do not touch it with iron, for the treatment of blood; but let it remain until it is dead, and then you will take it out, or it will break by itself; and if it is of a bluish color and the root is subtle, and you have prepared the instrument to cover, but first look at whether the gums of the chin are relaxed and calmed.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Now place the patient in front of the sun, and make sure their head is in your hands, and they open their mouth and take the tongue between their fingers, and press the entire instrument against the back of the throat, as it should be; and whether it's silver or gold, subtle as some nails:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can you press the tongue against the entire instrument, and see the abscess if you look in the mirror, then take the thumb and index finger, and try to pull it out more than you can; and do not use any tools with it, then put the copper on the instrument, as it seems like some forces; and all the teeth are crooked, and one place is another, and they are very sharp, and it is made of iron or steel:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	If you do not have this instrument present, if you have needles, then the form is like this:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	Then, cut from one end and the other part; and when you have cut one of the hairs, cut the other in the same manner, and after the incision, make the physician hot, wet the reed, and make it hot and wet, and let the blood come out, if the reed is hot, or if the pimples of grapes are cooked, or if they are fueled with mirte, and similar things, until the patient is not stained; then the cure is as long as the patient is healthy; and no other abscesses are born in the mouth than the two hairs, if they are cut correctly like the two hairs.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with a small abscess in her throat, which was causing difficulty swallowing; she had closed off most of her throat so that the woman could not breathe through the clogged channel, and could not drink or eat, and died if she delayed for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess was so large that it required two incisions through the two holes.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I then opened the abscess and found a large piece of bone in it, which I removed and cleaned out a large portion of the bowel; I then opened the other hole and closed the woman's mouth and pressed on her tongue; after opening the abscess in these places, I took out a small amount of pus, and she was then able to swallow water and wine, and continued to drain the abscess for several days; the abscess gradually shrank and filled the socket that I had created, until it became large enough; at this point I cauterized the wound in her throat: she did not heal quickly; and I left these parts, and only God could do more after me.
de l’uve	Of the urethra
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the urethra is drawn down to the urethra, and it is long and straight, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is very large and curved, it is called "urethra".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When the urethra is treated as we have described in the division, and the cure does not benefit, you see that the opening of the abscess is soothed and subtle, and it can be copulated; and that which is curved assembled and not long; and it is bloody or has a pus-like color or black, and you expel the incision of the wound.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It is necessary, as you see, according to the manner I have said, of the patient's gut and length, that you set the shoulder in front of the sun, and press the tongue on the instrument we made the memory of before; then fix the oncinette in the eye, and draw it out, and the cottle at I-II incisions as I said in the incision of the two amandines.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you do not copy too much than the superfluity that is over the natural term; for if you copy more, you will grieve the voice and speech; and after the incision, use what we said in the incision of the two amandines, and cure as long as it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient suffers from pain in the other side, then you should use an engine for the fire cautery of the other side.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the manner of cauterization is sharp when it is hot.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the patient places his head on your shoulder, and then presses his tongue on the instrument we have mentioned in the chapter of cauterization, and confines with hot, sharp force, so that it is not too thick or too thin; and by using this instrument's form, the shape is:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient has a hair or puts medicine on his cheek, as if from a spoon, and places the instrument in all the medicine on his eyeball; and the patient is faint with pain in his side, if the saliva and mucus come out of his mouth from the medicine given, if it does not reach his throat and chin, then hold your hand over all the medicine and press on the eyeball, as much as you can see the neri and the pain of the medicine is calmed; and if you see, take cotton and wrap it around any instrument, and moisten the cotton in the medicine, and pull the instrument through all the cotton in the catgut, as much as the cotton sticks to the eyeball; and do this often, as long as the cauterization is perfect, then let it dry, and after four or five hours or days, if you have skill to re-cauterize the medicine, if you resume, and after cauterizing the discharge enters the eyeball, wrap it in cotton and mouth it, and clean what is inside the medicine; and be washed with cold water, and use gargles as long as it is healthy.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is safer than incision alone. If it is treated with fumigation in this way, take chalk and sulfur and origin and chamomile and rosemary and similar herbs, mix them all together or any of them in one pot, and add water; then boil; and the cure will be well glued with hard earth, and the pot will have the instrument made this way:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And it should be of silver or gold, and one of the ends of the sharp instrument is put into the mouth of the patient as much as the vapor ascends through the urethra, until the urethra is mortified; afterwards, it often returns, until the urethra is dry, and make sure you do not do this at the beginning of the onset of gangrene, because many things come; and only do this if the decline of gangrene has begun.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a knife and cut the ear of the patient if the mouth of the patient has not been too tight; for the earlobe does not hurt the patient's mouth, and it is a good cure together with salve.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it has happened that the throat was pierced by a hook or a fishbone, or nothing at all; therefore, if you must see what is there, and press the tongue against the palate with all the instruments, so that you can see the thing; and whatever it may open and be bent in the throat, it is necessary to make the patient vomit unless the meat is cooked in the stomach; by chance if it is turned by vomiting; or if the patient swallows a piece of sponge, or a piece of gauze, or a root of lettuce, or a crumb of dry bread; and then wrap it with a sponge and then glutinate it; and when it comes to the mouth, if it is pulled out, and then draw it out further; and if it does not come out as we have said, then take the instrument in the form of a hook:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	1. And let the forceps be placed on the ear if it can more lightly enter the mouth, and lift the head; and warn that you should not touch the epigastrium, as all will vie for it, nor should you cram too much bone into it; and it is best that the patient or the thing being operated on be held, because if it is let go, or it is dragged further along the instrument evenly, as far as it can be.
de la sansue de la gorge	2. of the throat's gaping
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	3. No time is wasted in medicine when I have said in the division, by the cure of medicines; and when it does not profit, then look into the mouth of the patient's face under the sun, then press the tongue to the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	If you see the bone, if it has all been cut with a sharp knife, or if there are small thorns that are worth this.

de squinance	The first line of the text translates to:
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The first line of the text translates to: "The ancients used to say and speak about the tailoring of the throat; but I have never seen anyone do it in our land, and this is the scripture of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	The first line of the text translates to: "To those who have dislocations, it is necessary that the cut made at the throat, which is called 'epiglottis', be avoided; and none can help in this, because all the wounds and the pain of the patient are at those who have dislocated their jaw in the mouth, or in the throat, or in the eye.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the disease is in the hollow of the thigh, it is necessary to cover the epigastrium to avoid the destruction that comes from dislocation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to cut the epigastrium, that we cut it at three or four circles, or one small cut through, between the two circles, according to the quantity of the cut, and not in the cartilage; and then it is possible to section the epigastrium without causing pain, and the wounds are long enough.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the masters are poor, then it comes that the gut of the neck extends to the entire onyx, and then cut as far as it goes to the cartilage; and avoid the veins of the throat, if you see nothing, and then cut the flesh, as we have said; and it is demonstrated by the section of the flesh that it would be broken through the leg that is broken, and by the lack of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez. Therefore, they keep the wound open because the patient cannot breathe, and he respires through the wound, and it is kept alive; and for this reason, the ancients ordered the wound to be left oversized until the malice of the disease had passed, and it had passed in three or four days. And therefore, they ordered to suture the wound and cure it, as soon as it was cured; and I will tell you what I see.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte. de la grosse gorge	Of the large jaw
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	A hernia of the neck is called an "aposteme of the neck," and it is often large, with a dark color like a bruise, and is more common in women; and there are two types: natural and accidental; a natural one has no engine.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	An accidental hernia has two types: one that resembles large muscles, and another that resembles a hernia caused by arterial pressure; and it can cause pain, and it is not easy to fix with small incisions, and the surgeon must probe all around the introitus: if you do it like the fat, and it cannot be done for any reason, if the cope, so as if you cop the thigh, there is none; and he should search well, and the cure should be done in the same way as it is, to make it perfect.
des nous	Of the head
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways of us, of which I will tell all the appearances; and it comes that I must make a difference between the newborn and the born.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that issue is calenture and fever, as long as the inflammation has not passed, and it is accomplished by the phlegm; therefore the fever and the calenture rest.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With the newborn there is no calenture or fever or pain, and it contains the sweat, which is its own bag and is according to the color of the corpse, and begins also like a blister, and becomes large; and they are according to two appearances, either white or moist, or pink, and the color is as I said in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	It is necessary, when you come to the cure of a newborn, that you first examine and search for the entangled one in all the instruments called "entangler", according to what its form brings or chapter that comes after.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	The manner of incising the abscesses of the body is that you prick or more wetly than you thrust into the abscess, and turn your two points and points, as you see that the stones have perceived the keur, then that it is according to the size of the abscess; then draw out the entangler, and hold firm in the one that you throw.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	1. If moisture occurs, it is cut off, as it appears, just like other abscesses; and if after the entropion no moisture comes out, it is fat, so it is crossed, and taken with forceps, and slightly burned at each point and warded with the nut; and if it is not pulled out cleanly, it is pulled out in pieces as much as possible.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if it does not come out cleanly, it will return to us many times; and if it loses a pouch, and does not grieve, if you apply some corrosive powders to the wound, and tighten the wound, and put soothing remedies for abscesses on it, and cure other wounds as much as possible; and if it is large, if you cut off the lips of the wound, and cure the one who infected it.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	When the vein is difficult to pierce or if it is too small, use the glass splinter and leave it in for 2-3 days, until the wound stops bleeding and the swelling subsides; then return to the compresses as needed.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	Here are the forms of the gauze bandages, which are of three types: large and wide, medium and small; and there are three varieties: large, medium, and small, to encircle the fistula openings; they are also like the beaks of birds, whose horns are counted, and they are of copper, or iron, or silver, and those that are yellow are more valuable than those that are black, to encircle the beaks of fistula openings; and there are three varieties: large, medium, and small, according to the quantity of the larvae of the abscesses.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	1. The forms of claws are of different appearances, as you see here: large, medium, and small; and if the claws have three types of beaks; and if the claws have three beaks and are of three types; and if the claws have two beaks and are all claws with one beak and are of three types; and all these are necessary in their legs.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	1. The heads of these are sharp, and such as cannot cut anything finer than one part, because they burn the nose, for if they did not cut the vein or nerve, the patient would be harmed; and these introducers are returned in forceps, so that the surgeon does not lose them during the incision of abscesses; and there are three types: large, small, and medium, as you see; and they are used only in the legs, like arms, hands, fingers, and toes, and in similar parts; and no other instrument is ever made that resembles the blades of forceps, according to this form, for if it were made smaller, it would be like the blades of lancets.
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	And he places it on no occasion in the shoulder that is strong and resistant to wounds and arteries, and it never returns according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	Never have the breasts of other men swelled when they attempt to correct this corruption, as they seem to be female breasts; and they become laden and swollen, and those who see them cure them if they conform to this form of this line .b. up to .g.:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then scarify the fat, and use the wound with medicine burning char, then sew the lips of the wound together as much as possible until it is healthy; and if the breasts are clinched, and are swollen because of their greatness, so it is in women, if they are sewn together at the ends of one and the other, so that the smaller line contains the larger according to this form, from this line .b. to .g.; then scarify the skin that is between the lips, and remove the fat, and do what we have said about stitching and powders, and what is necessary in the cure, as long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, or the incision is not fully made because the patient does not rest, or due to the decay of blood, if you fill the wound with cotton wool soaked in corrosive ointment, and leave it until it absorbs the exuding blood and the fat, then cure it as it becomes healthy.
des apostemes des asselles	The first sentence to translate is "des apostemes des asselles". The translation of
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	These apostles that come out of the hooves are ways for scrofulous hard nodules or callosities to form, and they contain moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	Therefore, which contain moisture, must be cut according to this form, along the line .b. and .g.
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels within the abscess are out, if you employ a piece of clean linen, leave it there for another day, then take out all the linen and treat with ointment as needed until it is healed.

And if the abscess resembles scabs, then it is like we have said in the thorns, and if the wound is deep, then it should be cauterized as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is ruptured, and the curb is seen that is above it, if there are many abscesses, and also the vein becomes empty and abscessed; and if the conduit is found when it is for the artery, then it is the abscess that is long; and when you feel with your hands, if it is tightly held; and when it is for the vein, if it is cut apart; and it is madness to pull this abscess, and at the same time when it is loosened and the knots and corners are loose and out of other parts, and it is large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. It is necessary to avoid the treatment of fire, and the one in charge must also avoid it, and in the one who is of a wound made by an arrow that passes through the skin; then cut the artery as it is discovered, then take out a needle, and make it pierce on the other side, and tighten the artery with two threads according to what I have shown in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then the bone that is between the two links of an introducer as long as it does not move, and so free the graft; then apply the treatment that is needed according to what is required, as the wounds want; then cure this according to the size of the vein, if the aposteme is through the vein, then take in your hand what you need from the aposteme all over the body, then pull out the needle with your hand that holds the aposteme, and make it percute, and if it is double, then draw it on the other side; then tie the aposteme as I have said, or the one of one of the two parts as the two heads of the fil; and if you doubt that the fils do not come out, then take another needle at the end of all the fil to tighten all the aposteme at the incision of the first needle, and tighten the fils in four threads; then cut the aposteme as much as it has superfluity, then cut the superfluity of the keur and leave what is tied; then put on the wound a moist cloth with oil, and then take care of the dressings and ointments as it is healthy.
des apostemes des ners	Of the abscesses of the nerves
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	For abscesses of the nerves come in the artery and vein, they come when the nerves are too tight or due to too much work, and similar things happen.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens with splints and must be used in as many places as possible, and it is a grievous abscess, and its color resembles the color of the heart, and it is more frequently found in positions that cause pain; when they are pulled out, they form, and they feel painful to the touch, and not as much as in the chest, but rather like a curd; they are all very difficult to remove, and do not move before they are fixed or released, and the one who is in joints does not have the strength to hold on; by chance, there is contraction; and he who is at the knee or at the front, makes the skin sweat.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is small, and it is held with nails, and the poultice is applied to its root; and if it is large, and it spends in the bone, and burns it, then the bone and assembles the wound at its seam, and the remedy is applied as long as it is healthy.
des grosses boces pendans	large pus hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	Never comes in the stomach and does not affect other parts, and it is a disease called "funge" by its appearance of "aus", and it is at the subtle root, and the head is large; and in it there are many and some great ones; and I saw one who had it in his stomach which were more like "funges" than anything else, and they had no difference, and they were white, and had a small root, and were pointed, and they rotted with moisture.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I found them and discovered in one there were eighteen ounces, and in the other six. The incision is made if you look at the patient's hands to see if they are moist, and the color of the artel is bluish-green and moist with a subtle root; if the cope is large, and they are in your presence, the fire cautery is performed.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart. Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For these are infected gums, and I will treat the sore here after.
quant li boude ist fuer	When the boudoir is full
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When the appearance of the boudoir comes from a cauterization of wound or friction of soap, and is in the belly and has some of the dung, if it happens in other ways, or of sweat which cuts veins or arteries according to what is before, or of ventsitite; and if it is through the rupture of the gum and the issue of the dung, then the color of the gum appears like the color of the corpse, and is light thing with pain, and open of various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is from the intestine, then it is more complex, and when pressed on both sides, it returns, and by chance it may be stretched, and enlarges the opening to the bath and with great effort.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is due to moisture, it is a light thing, and opens well when you press it with your hand; it does not cause any constraint. Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If it is necessary to leave the treatment.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For there is doubt and fear, as I have said in the chapter of abscesses, for the artery and the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.
