dou chancre	The translation of "dou chancre
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	We have said in the division that the appearances of a chancre are like, and we say that it must be overseen by medicines, and that it must be treated with iron; and we say that the chancre is infected in the marriage, and with great caution in its cure, and we tell the old man that when chancres are in the loins or can be treated if they are like those that are in the mammary glands, and in the joints, and in similar places, it must be done entirely at the beginning; and when it is large and ancient, if it is not possible to approach it, because I have never seen anyone healed from it; and no one has ever been cured of it before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. And the cauterization, when it is in the flesh or can be cut, is that you never purge the caustic of black coal; then make it cleaner if there is visible fullness, then cut the caustic with a knife to do the cauterization; then your bones or chicken will rot, and all hair will fall, and all nails will feel nothing left; leave the blood all flow, and press well the wound in your hand or on anything, and if they dislocate after cauterization, it is because the caustic was too hot, either on the artery or vein, if the cauterization is so hot that the flesh is burned; then apply another treatment as soon as it is healthy.
de ydropisie	The first sentence to translate is "de ydropisie
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	We have said in the division the appearances of edema, and how the assembly of the fever is made, and the signs of each appearance, and the cure done by medicines, and that which is cured by fire: if it is only; and one should not touch fire in these two appearances: this is to know, tympanites and yposarche, for it is a mortal thing; therefore, when you treat edema called "eclites" of medicines, and the cure does not profit, if you look at the malaides are weak, or if there is another disease than edema, if all and solution of the belly and similar things; if it does not touch fire, because it has doubt; and if you see the malaide of strong virtue, and it has only edema, and it is not too much nor too little, then you should over: gently hold the malaide with your hands, and press the belly as far as the fever reaches the lowest part of the piss, then take the spumous spine according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And now, let us proceed to the second part.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And now, let us proceed to the second part. If there is no pain, and the point does not enter more than an inch into the intestine when it is felt, then look if the pus is mixed with the intestines: if it comes that you cut through the abscess at the third finger, then you must cut right below the nail; and if the pus is due to liver disease, then you must cut at the third finger on the left side; and if it is due to gallstones, then you must cut on the right side, and only the surgeon's knife should pass through the flesh without the superfluities reaching the weak part of the body; then clean all the skin with the instrument, and the bone, and gently lift your hand over the entire area between the skin and the scab as you would when scraping a thumb nail; then cut the scab until the area is dry to the touch, which is the sign of an abscess, then pull out the instrument, and this is the form of it:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	1. It resembles a silver needle, and is light or feather-like, and in the part closest to the tip there is a small pertus; and sometimes it costs three parts, and two in another part, and one in another; and the head is cut so that it resembles a pen, and this is the shape of the incision that the scribes make with the pen.
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	1. The head of the needle is sharp, so that when it reaches the angle, now use the instrument; empty the first third or second, for if you see more than it should in that hour, by chance it may die from the resolution of its spirit in the arm, or it may lose strength, or approach death; but according to the quantity of its courage, and according to the dispositions of the courage of the patient, and his hands; then remove the instrument and hold the angle, and it is held now by the tongue that stops the pertus which was just cut, according to what I have spoken, that you should do according to this manner; then resume the instrument the next day, if you see the patient suffering from this, and take a small quantity of saliva; do this every day, and keep away from any fire as much as possible, but a little heat is necessary.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	If you doubt the patient's condition, and they have fever, then the treatment of burial or sand bath is suitable; if it is relieved by drinking or bathing and sun exposure, and the patient becomes weak; and the treatment of dry medicines as soon as the patient is healthy, and cauterization on the stomach, liver, and spleen after removing the fever, as I have said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the end of the bowstring
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is ever born without having a pustule on the bowstring, or if the pustule is small, or it is not present in his leg.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If the dislocation is so great that it cannot be perceived with any pin or even a very small needle according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	Then use a small needle or pin to pierce the skin, and tie it and the other end with a thread. After three to four days, if the needle is closed, urinate, and then remove the needle. If it doesn't happen, it's because the urine that comes out loosens the closure.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	If the pierced spot is small, and if it is treated with a small needle according to what we have said, it will swell.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the dislocation in their shoulder are lucky, because no one is born with a dislocation at the top of the thigh, because they cannot urinate before they loosen their thigh; and they cannot enjoys it because the matter cannot come out quickly enough, and this is a serious disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the manner of the incision, if the patient is seized with pain on his back, is that it is the head of the gouge and the hook as large as a penny, if it pierces the flesh, if it can; and you must prevent the loss of blood that comes often, and if it does, if the wound is clean and clean, and cure the wound as soon as it is healthy.
des pustules de la verge	of pustules of the gouge
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times, pustules come in the gouge, and it has a horrible appearance; and among them are malignant and non-malignant; if you prescribe them to be removed under the subcutaneous fat, and cut and clean them all, then put on cotton wool dipped in Egyptian linseed oil; then the care of the ointment is done as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	If the boil is malignant, with a putrid smell and drainage, then you must perform a cauterization.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	After you have cut it, and the boil is still present, and it has both hair and flesh, then you must remove the part that was hair first; and if it is still present, then remove the part that is flesh.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you cut it in pieces, if you are not sure which part of the boil is causing pain, and it turns black and corrupts in its center and around; then remove all that is black and corrupt, then apply honey and flour made from the scraps of roasted peas and vinegar, and repeat the treatment as many times as necessary until it is healed.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And if blood comes out of the wound, then follow this form of the moon cauterization:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if blood comes out of the wound, then follow this form of the moon cauterization: it is knowing, at the cessation of the flow and the corruption; and if the head of the thorn is corrupted and returns, then if you bind or lead it with a string, and let the salve pass among; and when the thorn comes to the end of the tail that has not been circumcised, or has come through wound or abscess, then it is necessary to scrape it with the instrument's blade, as long as the roots are loosened, and release the thorn from the tail of all parts; and if this is a difficult thing to do, then scrape it in the spatulum of any part of the thorn and the hair; then apply a small amount of element between them, and put a subtle drapery of cold wet linen that does not adhere to the hair.
de la circoncision	The first sentence to translate is "de la circoncision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a continuation of other wounds if done properly; however, when we perform this operation for our own will, and as parents, it is the best work we can do, and the most gentle for health.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancients did not call circumcision their children's circumcision because they did not use it in their law, and we only have what we have acquired by experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	Because I want the greatest part of masters and doctors who performed circumcision inside the diaper, and had strength, and at all ages; if it were the case that he would lose his head because he had too many, and by chance if he cut off more than necessary, and then he would regret it.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	When the wound is closed, and there is double pain, and the circumcision is not sure of the point of the painful member; and the circumcision of the finger by chance escapes the iron, and cuts the skin, and many times do not have the circumcision, and I want it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the circumcision made with force, I have found the benefit of the experiment, for the forces cut both sides equally, either better or worse.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Because when you press your hand, if it fits well in I all that you hold; but that the thread should be well stretched over the skin; and that the first incision should be made in the right way, so that you do not think the child understands, that you only fasten the thread around the finger, and then tie it as you please; then tie it between your hands all straight, and put the forces between your hands or between your fingers that the children do not see, and no of the strings; then put your hand on the finger and blow or keep your breath, and hold it up as much as the thread of the finger is assembled, then mold it well of the dirt that is in it, then tie the lower end with a double thread, then tie the other line to the second index, and cut between the two lines, then gently lift the tip of the finger, and draw the knot through the hole; then leave the sutures in place for a while, because they are the most painful; and sprinkle some powder on it and on the powder with a piece of bread cooked in clear rose wine, preserved with olive oil and fresh, and let it sit until the other day, and the cure will be completed as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the forces at the mummification is this: the two heads must be even and tight, and the heads must be as large as the hands equally.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of mummification is when the flesh comes out at the incision; therefore, it is necessary to extend the skin to your nail, unless the grip is torn; and it should be even, and if you do not hold it with your nail, then the skin.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	And if they pass three years, and what is out of order is flattened, if you let it be as long as the grip is at ease, and it is lightly burned; if the skin is like this, and you hold it from the part of the grip, it will not hurt.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. Treat the leg with things that are damp and powdery wounds, which we have said or treated as powders, and if it is not too much over measure, it will go away; treat the leg, just as we have said, as soon as it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	2. Retain urination.
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	3. If urination is caused by opuration of the urethra, or congelation of the sanc, or bowels, or chole, or similar things, which we have said in the division; and if urination is discharged, and you see the retention by the urethra which is at the jaw or lower part of the bladder, then it comes that the malaides are stuck to the genouls; and they should be placed on the back, and extended the belly from the part where the urethra is, and restrained the malaides as much as they can; and then the col of the bladder is constrained to the expression of the urethra at the desus, because if urination is discharged, and the malaides feel great pain, then it comes that you must administer extraction with all the instrument called "siringue", and its form is: and make a thin silver thread, as fine as the hair of an owl; and make the cord of a palm of half a yard, and make it fine at the head.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides. des maladies de la vessie	Of diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When there are scorchings or pains in the bladder, or if there is vomiting, and you see water and medicines being distilled, then do this to all the instrument called "caustic," and it is shaped like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if there are three punctures: two on one side, and one on the other, as you see; and it is read by the medicine that burns well without addition, if you can draw the moisture, and then bind it with your hand; and when you see your medicines flowing in the bladder, put the tip of the cautery into the moisture, and pull it towards the traction which is in it; if you draw the moisture into the cautery, and then forcefully pull on the traction; if the moisture enters, and comes to the bladder now, if the patient feels it, then this is the form of the subtle clyster that one clsters the bladder: if this is the case:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or archae, and the head is higher; and then take a sheep's bladder and put the moisture that you see clisterizing the bladder, then place it between the two seals to form a double-layered pouch, and heat the moisture with the fire; then cut the clister on the edge, then hold your hand on the bladder all the moisture, as if the patient feels that the moisture has reached the bladder; and if you don't have the bladder, then take a piece of parchment, and make the circle, and perforate it around the hole; then pull the strong thread through these holes, then assemble the circle as one does with a nail, and put what you see of oil, moisture, and tincture, and tie it in the instrument; and do as you did with the bladder, pressing with your hand as much as the moisture reaches the bladder.
de la piere	Of the incision
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have said in division the ways of incision, and the extraction of arrowheads; and we said the difference between the incision as rains, and those signs, and in what piers one must over on size; and in the vessel, and in the verge; and I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the incision which is more often in the vessel is in children, and it is a sign that the heat of the vessel has leaped to the subtlety; and it is open and great in the verge, and it grows many times, and then becomes violent; and then the children's wounds are closed; and it is light in the cure of children until they are four years old, and it is heavy in the bellies of the young and the old; and it is the cure that is lighter in those who have large wounds than in those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	When we come to treat the patient, if we first clean the wound with a cloth, we must clean all the feces that is inside the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never closes once it has been pricked.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the wound with your fingers, stand up and move downwards until the hole reaches the bottom of the bladder, and does not rise once above; then place it between your hands, so that your thighs are lower than your belly, if the bladder is completely deflated below; then cut and touch the wound; if you feel the hole in the area, then now cut at the hole.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier. And it is between the joints and the foundation, not to be confused with the cost of the left side; and it should be on either side of the incision, and the two should be either at the foundation or the incision, and the size should be large enough to cover if it becomes wide due to the incision, and should be tightened according to the size of the incision, not too much; by chance, the pressure should be applied if it is at the foundation, so that it does not cause discomfort during work; and the edges should have a part that is pieced or has angles and margins: if they are rough to pass through; and if a part is sutured, it resembles a glass, and curves, whose end is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	1. Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already done that.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	I will prepare it according to this form and make it at a 30-degree angle, with one side being the base.
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge. de la piere des femmes	of the bone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	If there is only one wound in women, and if there is no wound at all, then the cure is difficult for three reasons: the first is that it happens by chance when the woman is virgin; and the second is that it is not possible to find a woman well-experienced who has been betrayed as much as she has, even if she is cast.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. de hernie carnouse	of hernia of the intestine
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	Grease is nothing else but an assembly of moisture or white lead, which is derived from the seeds; and it is called "lead"; and it is never properly in the texture of the seed, if one cares to make sure that it is another seed; and this is the fat between the white lead that we have mentioned; and there was no lack of it.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this grease is such that it comes from the seeds, and it is expanded by that matter.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	1. And no time does it come from striking on the bones, and this moisture is of many colors: either it is a declining color to jaundice, or it is without redness, or black, or clear white, and this becomes more; and these are the signs of this assembly, for if it is white as we said, and the wounds are closed, then it looks like a bone, and does not open the pores, because it has moisture throughout.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	2. Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the introcution, judge which is denser.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then, if the patient is healthy according to the touch, then take the knife and make a cut on his back, making it as high as possible, and then take the scissors and cut off some of his clothes; then do the same on his side, and command the attendant to do the opposite, and extend the verge to one of the two costels of the knee cap; then take the spatula and clean the knee cap between the two costels until you reach the patella, and make a straight cut along the patella, leaving the skin white, and scrape it gently so as not to hurt it; then pierce the white part of the eye with the needle at the large pucker, and remove all the white, and then put your thumbnails, and set the white back in place; and do not touch the knee cap, but only the white, and scrape it gently on both sides, so that if you do not do it well, the white will come back; and if the wound bleeds a lot, then take the hemostat and hold it in your hand as soon as you have completed the wound with white; then assemble the two knees of the knee cap in one stitch, and treat it as you would any other wound, until it is healthy.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit. de l’aposteme des coions	Of the abscess of the gums
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	Saws that in the section of this ramify it is often done in different ways, and I think it is better to leave it; and I will tell you the method and appearance of the abscess.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say therefore that every abscess comes either by the head or the gums, and also in cases like this; and it is not uncommon.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to know by the superfluous sour and acrid matter which is expanded in the gums, or by percussion; and the color of the abscess is according to the color of the tooth; and there is no pain, and it is a greedy abscess; and sometimes there are grayish-green and purple abscesses, of a fuscous color, and never come from an artery or vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by an artery, if it is closed by the arrangement of the abscess, when you press on it with your two hands; and only then can you touch it.

Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	1. Therefore, do not force the patient to endure percussion, but make them do it as soon as the pain is eased; and then place the patient on the bed, and have two pillows or blocks under their head, and support their back and assemble their limbs as far as possible to support the leg; and let their fingers be spread out, and put their knees against their chin, and tie them well with a belt; then proceed towards the patient's left side, and introduce the instrument that is placed in the mouth of the mare, after which comes the form; and it is necessary that when you are introducing this instrument, you fix the rite first so as to know the fit of the mare, if what enters from the instrument does not fit more than it should, and does not cause the patient pain; and if it is larger, then it is necessary to cover the fit of the mare with cloths, if the patient's grief is not increased; and it is necessary that the instrument's handle is placed at the end, and that it is marked on the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement. Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is dressed in the marsh, then it comes to your attention that you should not cook with iron, but cure as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of childbirth

Labor is first in the dance that the woman knows the figure of natural childbirth, and the signs if you see her pressing against the wall, and desiring to smell the aroma: therefore hurry to give birth to the child; then assure yourself that these children are according to the natural figure, and they are from your womb, and the second one with them; and when you see these signs, it comes to gently press his belly, so that the child is quickly born; for when he descends from his head, if it is with the second one, and is monied by good hygiene, and this other one who comes otherwise does not come naturally.

de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	Of the child's foot that was cut off

de l’issue des gemelz	Of the issue of twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	It is said that twins are born many times, and never in three or four; and this is a strange thing, and not often seen.

Two things are strange, and do not live long, their name is unknown; I know that they are multiplied, and are produced by the faculty that determines them, which is linked to the body; and they never come out naturally like all at once, as we have said.

dou ramener la marris a son leu	To bring the shoulder back to its place.

Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	1. This instrument is all around, and its appearances are numerous; and when one sees them, the more one operates, the higher the skill required for such a quantity.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	2. If you do not despise the instrument because you have not seen it, for its requirements are not easily overcome.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	3. When the second child is retained in the womb, it comes to pass that you command the midwife to pull out the hair, and then the child is pulled out with difficulty, and your hands are forced to the mouth and nose; and if she jumps because of this, it is well.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If this does not work, then I will try to take and make a suture or cover it, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the wound, such as chamomile, rosemary, anise, camomile, chamomile, and centaury; all these herbs, or none of them, are cooked or can be boiled in water; then put a bandage or suture if possible, and the other end in the mouth of the wound, and tighten it as much as the vapor comes out of the mouth; then I will make it tighter, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If the second part is difficult.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	After this treatment, if she remains in good health, the physician orders her to gently moisten her left hand with ointment or linseed oil, or musk, and then apply it to the affected area. She should repeat this process until the second dose. When she finds it, she should carefully stretch it slightly, so that the stitch does not come out during extraction. However, it is recommended to move lightly to the right and left, and then pull. If it comes and becomes sore,
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the mouth of the stitch is very tight, we have said that the cure is to stretch and fumigate herbs; and if she does not do everything we have said, she should only pull; but it is best that what is in the mouth of the stitch is tied to the woman's navel, then the ointment is applied with tetrafarmaçon ointment; if it becomes red and is reinserted, and it comes out; but all the same, when she porrists if it comes out with a bad smell in the stomach and head, and makes the physician sick.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it comes to that, then let there be safe fumigations for this: no of the old ones have experienced fumigation of cresson and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument is made with it that it fumigates the woman with the retention of flowers and secondines if this is.
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it seems like a dog, and one places the subtle head in nature, and the large chiefs under the fire; and it is the fumigations of charcoal, and the smoke as long as it is gray, and another one begins.
de percier lou fondement	to test the foundation.
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many children are born who have not felt the foundation tested, but if it has been subtle and sharp for some time, then it is necessary to test the foundation again if it has not perceived the sharpness of the spatula at its own time, and does not perceive any damage from touching it; then it is mixed with fine grain in wine and oil, and the cure of ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not happen, if you put on a piece of cloth and leave the wound open, and if it is not sewn up when the child is seen in the chamber.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And never has this remedy failed for a wound or abscess; if it comes to that, if you cure it: if it is like the cloth for the wound.
de la fistule dou fondement	of the fistula with great foundation.
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the foundation are nodularity, and grow when they come from the lower part of the incision, or in the space between the two parts; and if it is an old nodularity, it moves, and becomes more bony or subtle, and never are these fistulas permanent; they are known for this reason, either by egestion or ventosity when the patient has egestion, and by chance in some cases.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	If there are fistulas that pus comes out of the uterus, and half of the vagina; and they reach where the joint of the cornua is, and to the knot of the ovaries.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.	And if you know where the fistula is at its base, and it is not too deep: and if your index or pointer points to the base of the fistula, and insert a fine awl of iron or silver into the fistula when it does not have any bends.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if there are bends, then insert a small tent or horse hair into the fistula as far as you can feel it in your hand; and if you do not feel it, and there is no purulent discharge, no vomiting, and no abdominal pain, as we have said: sharpen the tent or horsehair until it pierces.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	When the fistula is present in the uterus or carried by the urine, if the urine jumps, and cannot be soaked by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is perceived at the joint of the thigh, if it is near the knee; if it is not tortuous and the pain of the entrail, if it is that it goes to the belly, and there is no remedy with medicine by touching; and in these fistulas there is no cure but labor, and vanity of proud people who come to them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	In the one that is not perfect and not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have experienced, and it is that the patient comes between his hands on his back; and he supports his legs until they reach their thighs, and they are leaned towards the belly; then bend a tent of rye or plunk if it is tortuous, as long as you check or the tension comes.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	When the patient feels pain at the base, if you suspect it is a dislocation, then it is certain that it has happened; and if you can discover or feel between your thumb and index finger, which part of the bone is fractured, then you should carefully examine it. If you cannot find any fracture, then it is not a dislocation.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	It is difficult to heal all injuries, but this is rare; and if you can, then you should do so as follows: if the cauterization is made subtly according to the size of the fistula, as said before; and the patient should be led through the fistula as soon as it starts to ache at the base; and repeat this 2-3 times until you are sure that these charges are straight, which resemble a quill, like a feather of a swallow; then the dressing of soft threads is made, as soon as it is straight, then the dressing of ointment is applied, smearing char and soaking.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If it is in good health, then so be it.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If it is not in good health, then so be it. If you try to remove it, and it does not yield to the force applied, and you cover the area with a thick cloth or ointment, you will see the fistula open at this point; if the end of the fistula comes out before the covering, and then cauterize after, until it reaches the top of the tent; it will be delivered from the tent, and will remain; then mend those charms that seem like a needle's point, and none will remain.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	If it does not please you, and cuts between you and the wound, whether by fire cauterization or medical boil.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cauterization, there are two main things to know: to know the strength of these burned chars, and the evacuation of blood and the coagulation of moisture; then the care of soft tents made in burr or in the crotch, as long as it does not bend, and it will remain in the bend; then cure the wound of sore throats with dry char, and these are the dry medicines.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it is restored, if it is healthy and does not return often.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes suddenly with great force, and it is moved away from the body, and its base is damaged, and you should investigate this.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and if it is the cloth or the sackcloth or the charcoal, if it was only a sign of hope and expectation, by the administration of one of the three methods: if you cauterize as we have said, or if you cope it gently, or if you peel if it has tents and cures as we have said; and do not push too far in front, if you do not cover the part that holds the foundation, and let the discharges pass through the desired sense; then the cure, as we have said; by chance if it becomes healthy, or you remove that covering and the mundane when it is coped from the foundation, or by tent or another appropriately chosen instrument; then mold the char that is in the wound as much as you can; then study to restore the wound, and to prolong the fistula in the part further from the foundation: if it is still a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And no time are fistulas made in this way: and when you reach the end of the fistula, it is either costive or too much founded on the skin, if you take a tent according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And if you cut it in two, and pull the tent through all of it in the fistula as much as it is at the head:
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is perse in the border of the founded dough, then pull the thread from that puncture, as much as you reach the head of it; and cut off the end of the thread, and assemble the two ends, and stretch them apart, and leave one or two; and keep it once, until the threads are loosened and healed; then cure the wound as much as it is sore and sound.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not perceive, if you try to feel it in all ways that you can, it will not be too difficult.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it is not necessary to make the dressing too tight, and then the cure, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spiny thistle, from which the fistula is made if it is long and thin, and on the other hand, because it does not fit well, as you can see in this:
des emorroydes	of the embryos.
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Embrios are of two kinds: either they are densified at the foundation, like resin grains, and become smaller and larger, and are cut through, and become one or more, and are deft at the foundation and in the head of the foundation; but those that are dense have little moisture, and are cut through with a little bit of turquoise or a little bit of wine, and have the color of coral; and the treatment of those who have densified the foundation is that you command the midwife to expel the moisture in chambers as long as the foundations are firm, and when the babies appear; if you hurry, and she can use needles or hold it in her nail, then cut into its roots; and if the uncinate cannot hold it by its moisture, then bend it to the side, or to cloth, or a piece of camomile; and remove them from your two hands, then cut them, and powder some hot powders that are in the cauterization leau; or you can cauterize as it is said in the cauterization chapter, and cure others as long as they are healthy; and if the foundations cannot issue, then clysterize the midwife with clyster biting and sharp with washing what is at the foundation, so that it may issue openly; and if the midwife's mouth is not closed, then clisterize the midwife with clister biting and sharp, and if the foundations are dense, then the treatment is light; and it is that you cut them with your nail or needles, and cure them as we have said, so that they may be healthy and not fear the incision by fire.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1. If it comes to pass that you must undo the stitching according to this manner: take one thread, thread it through an awl, and then pull the thread out and make the awl pierce from another side, and turn the other two ends of the thread double on the awl, and if they are wide; and then draw the thread tight, then knot it, and draw out the awl, and do this to all the others, and leave the excess suture dripping with oil or ointment; then put the foundation cloth greased with oil or ointment on the wound, and put it on the wound, and instruct the patient to lie down; and then let it be, and when it is dry, if the cure of sewing and other cures are needed, as soon as it is healthy.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	The first sentence translates to: "If the joint is not firmly set.
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	The second sentence translates to: "Often, the joint is not firmly set due to moisture in the intestines, and by constriction, and when the disease is severe, and medicine is ineffective.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The third sentence translates to: "If it comes to pass that you resort to the point of a spatula or your nail to scrape out the pus, which does not allow it to moisten; then treat as much as necessary until it is softened as before; and if it cannot be soaked, then repeat the scraping more forcefully than before, until it is sane and burned; then treat as much as necessary.
dou fremit	The first sentence to translate is "Ou
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The first sentence to translate is "Ou
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	The first sentence to translate is "Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see that I make this of a bone of iron or steel according to this form, and it is subtle and thin and true:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see that the cauterization does not burn, if it is in front of or in the chapter of cauterization.
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of clyster.
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	Never is made a clyster of silver or alloy, nor of melted or hammered iron; and never is made these small and large stummings, according to which they are obtained.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	Therefore, in the treatment of children who are weak and painful, they are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the small and great burn is such that it covers a wide area, or the belly is influenced in this manner:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	And if there is a depression or the belly is distorted, as you see, and the head is perceived to be deformed; and it is in one of the costals II pertuss, and in the other I; and it is the belly or where the medicines are placed in a vessel of a beast or parchment, and all around the small pertuss are perceived, and between each pertuss I must insert a spice, then weave through these pertuss I tighten the thread, then gather the belly as if it were a swine; and when the medicine is given, if the instrument before a strong thread has a knot, then close it; and this is the form of a circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	And let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and anoint the head with oil or unguent of urine or something similar, then lightly smear it; then the surgeon uses his two hands evenly, as much as possible, then removes the bandage, and gently places the patient's legs on the table, and if the medicine seems to be working, as much as it can; and if the patient sleeps a whole night, it is more help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you dislocate the abdomen due to disease, and the medicine seems to be working, if it recurs as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the swelling is or crush, or gangrene, whether the clyster is also subtle and fine as with a child; and this is the form of the subtle clyster that is drawn when the skin is stretched.
des plaies	wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have said in the division of wound treatment; and you will say the treatments for hands and medicine, according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are diverse according to what they are made, and according to the instrument or the wound is made, and of how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by piercing with an instrument, the size of the needle or lancet, or spear, or shield, or seizure; or according to the wounds made according to the parts of the body, as a wound that is made at the collar, or the chest, or the shoulder, or the belly, or the liver, and I will tell you the treatment for each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds on the chest, because the reminder will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or head, and the bone is not broken, if it is of bleeding from the wound or similar things, and the skull is entirely torn and the large wound is, and you slightly doubt of gangrene: if the latter comes sooner of the cranial part itself if there is little blood from the wound, and it is healthier on the opposite side; and avoid the surgeon's fullness with wine and large meats.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it does not become healthier, if the meat is anemic, and does not drink wine, and does not eat char, and puts on the wound, it seizes and comes, ointment with oil of rose only, or with wine stiptice; and if it does not seize, then it puts on the wound, it is fresh at all its wound, and it is not moved by the air, dust, which I will say a little later; and if it becomes dry, then it puts on some ointments, as long as it is healthy.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, like that of a spear and similar, and the lips cannot be reassembled by tents, if they can be reassembled by sewing, if I say as stomach wounds, from the stitching.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone, and it can be seen, and only holds by a pin, if the patch; then treat the wound with medicine, and restore hardness in the leather of the thigh, and instruct the patient to consume large meats, such as beans and cooked flour, as well as poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you eat or wear leather, and it does not reach the bone, if the patch is made of total porridge, and grows wet, then treat it; and if arteries have been cut in the wound or vessel, which cannot be healed by medicines, if you want the artery to close, and if you loose the thread, if the cord is a fil; and if this does not help, if cauterized.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the cure is light: and it is that you put on this powder that smells like none other than what the doctor has touched.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the manner of the powder is: take some incense; burn three parts of dragon's blood; three parts of live chalz, and the fine powder, and apply to the wound, and draw it together, until it heals well and adheres to all its edges; and then close it well, and leave it to drip if it does not bleed, for the medicine is only applied as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never once has it been done with anything but fire, when there is no incense or blood of the dragon, but that the artist has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the artist has moved the wound, immediately in this manner; but use some digested powder, or make some thin paste of flour of oats and honey, until it bends downwards; then apply other cures as long as it is healthy.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the bone fracture comes with the wound, and it is small, then use fine forceps; and I will tell you more about this later in the chapter on major fractures.
de la plaie dou col	Of the wound of the shoulder
