Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	A wound comes of the shoulder
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the shoulder, and there is no other cause than to treat the wound, and do not restrict anything, because the nerves will retreat; and do not put anything on the wound, because the substance of the nerves is cold, and the continuation is with the brain, which is the colder member; but if the medicine is available, like calm water, mixed with oil rose, and cold water, and other poultices in this way, and moistened ointments.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the wound is large, if it is bound with bandages, then the treatment is as soon as it is healthy.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	If the wounds are deep and full of bones, if the hole is lower on the leg; and if the artery is cut, and blood comes out, if it is stopped, and the bleeding stops, if the cauterization is successful; and if the spine of the neck or jaw is cut, or the tooth, and the guide is kept, as soon as the tooth is cut from the jaw bone, and does not touch the jaw but is replaced according to its natural shape; then the stitching is done, and a few days are left, then the treatment of broken bones is done as soon as it is healthy; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, if you want; and if there are pieces of bone, if they are pulled out as much as possible, and those that you cannot pull out, if they leave the wound open and clean and healed, and allied to the issue; and if the wound is fresh, if powder is applied on the powder I have mentioned.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	If it has bone in the wound and there is an abscess, then the treatment is as I have described in this chapter.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the wound from a lance or a spear
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a wound from a lance or a spear, and the wound is gushing blood, then look at the wound's appearance: if it is mortal; and if it is not gushing blood, and it is fresh all around, then in the first hour put powder on the wound, and do not tie it with anything but the wound's own suture, and revive the patient to the chest; but if there is no ointment, then put cotton in the wound for moisture, and make the patient sleep on the wound for three or four or more hours, until spasms or trembling of the chest are not caused by lack of moisture; and when you see the bones in order, then know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the wounds and other wounds with cleanliness and care, as much as possible; and if it cannot be healed, and operates, according to the sutures that have been made; if the treatment is done as it should be.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is an incision of a sword or a knife, and it is simple, or front or back, if the treatment is done by the person in front; if it is large, use poultice; and if it is small, use powder, and if it is infected in the bone, and in the pieces, if the wound wants to heal, and the pus comes out if they are separated; and if they do not separate, leave the wound open if it is allowed, if the extractions are extracted; and other wounds on other parts are judged as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre." In English,
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The first sentence to translate is "dou derrompement dou ventre." In English, it means "great pain in the stomach." The translation of the entire sentence is: "The stomach pain is great and intense, and no time it causes the intestine to be torn, or the intestines to be pulled out, and the suture is more tightened, and never a small wound can be mended as the large ones, because the intestines swell so much that they feel the pain, if they are mended more times, and because it causes the wound to become more severe, because the intestine is pulled out more often, and because the costure of the stomach pain is in four ways: the two common costures come in the costure of the stomach pain, and the costure of the other wounds of the belly and the two other costures that are proper to other wounds are common as other wounds; and all of them are more proper with the costure of the stomach pain, and I will say each one and declare it.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I say that when the wound is small, and there is no inflammation in the intestines, and it is easy to set, this is one of the two ways: either because of the size of the wound, as we have said, or because the intestine is contracted due to the friction.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is inflamed, handle it in this way: moisten a sponge or a soft cloth only, or rinse it with hot water and add vinegar and salt, and gently push the intestine as far as it will stretch without tearing; never forget to do this repeatedly, and it will eventually become relaxed.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	When you see the flame departing, if the intestine of the wound or gash and veins are cooked, for this is the cause of the entry of little thing; and if it cannot enter, then make a small pouch with the wound instrument and cover the blood clots; and the first cure is to cut that, which no one should cut without great necessity and no one has; and this is the stitches for the wound: if they tear from the corner and do not turn, and see this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestine springs forth, if you return it according to its natural form in its own place, if you can, for this is good.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is wide, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you are able to make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should raise his head and chest higher than the surrounding parts, and thus the wound in that part will be higher than the other. And then you must manage this in large and mangled wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	When the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdomen, if you are able to make the patient lie on his back and raise his legs higher than his chest; and if it is in the lower abdomen, then he should raise his head and chest higher than the surrounding parts, and thus the wound in that part will be higher than the other. And then you must manage this in large and mangled wounds. If the wound is small, and it is in the lower abdomen, then you should take a clean cloth and dab it with water, and then assemble the corners of the cloth; and this is the common method of bandaging, and it is that you prick an awl or more, according to the size of the wound, then leave the bottom of the wound open, and insert an awl or a strong thread; and perforate the leather with the awl as far as the bottom of the wound, and assemble the four corners of the cloth around the awl; then pull the thread double through the awl, then assemble the corners of the wound together, and leave the bottom open, and insert another awl; then follow the same method as before, until all the wounds are bound; and the awls should be clean and of different sizes, because small awls can pierce the whole belt, and large ones cannot enter well; therefore they should be clean; and do not put the awls too close to the wound and the leather, so that they do not open the wound before the suture; and then cover the awls with cloth, so that the patient does not bleed at night, and put sheets or blankets on the cloth to hold it in place, and leave it as long as the wound is soft; and this method of bandaging is more comfortable for small wounds, because it is common to prick an awl or the second suture, and it is that you assemble the four corners of the leather and the four corners of the cloth around the awl or the strong thread; when you have perceived the four corners of the wound, then pull the awl to the place where you started, in the same way as you did with the threads; and put a piece of cloth between each suture, which will secure the wound, and this bandage will help the patient, and I saw a wound that one had, in the belly, which was caused by a suture, and it was more than a palm in width, and it had intestines for more than ten palms in width, and it was the wound in the belly.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I took the intestine and after it had been out for 24 hours, it was 15 years old, and the wound was healed, and I cured it, and it became healthy.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And he looked for signs that it would die, and this was a miracle; and I did not use any medicine because I was in the league where no remedies are found, and I washed more than twice a day on the wound with honey water until it became healthy.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or shall I tell you the two main ways of sewing: take the needle, and pull out the thread at the end of the part that is too long; when it has perceived the right direction in the right place, if you have pulled out the needle or the thread or you have pulled out the needle, and make it perceive another part of the part that is too short; and the ends understand this sewing if you do as the tailor does with the threads, and leave once the seam one way, and take it back the other, until the sewing is completely done.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of stitching, which Galen calls his own, is the most common and is done as follows: take two needles of the same kind and thread them with the thread, then insert one needle into the flesh near the wound and leave the other end of the thread outside; then turn the needle and pull out the thread from the part that is opposite to the wound, using the other needles that are on the other side; and this is the most common way of stitching.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	1. If Galiens hears this speech, and no one testifies, then we must sew the belly to the eyes, or it will come undone; and it must be sewn on one side, and the other side, in the manner of those who are twisting; and we should know that when the rupture is near the belly, if it is more painful than others in the belly.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	2. The judgment of the wound is whether it is like the judgment of other wounds: and if you touch the fresh wound with all its sand, unless it has moved, then pull out the intestine and the gut; then put on the powdered charcoal, and if it has moved, then put on any ointment that is present, as long as the wound bows; and cut the thread, and be sure of the suture, and the mirror; then cure the wound as you would with others, until it is sound; and if you have no medicines, then put them on, as much as they come out to grip the belly, a thin cloth, and rub it twice the jaw until it is sound.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you have no other skill in other matters than treating wounds; and if you doubt that the wound is not serious as to the principal members, then it comes that you lightly moisten with oil of tamarind or rose oil, and put on garments, and desox the assesles; and if there is pain or rash in the belly, and often comes, then if the clysterize with red wine, and also if the rash comes to the intestine; and the perce penetrates, and sauces that when it is the large intestines, it is lighter to heal than the small.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The small intestine, which is called "young," cannot heal until it is unwound, and this is due to the tightness of the veins that surround it, as well as the subtlety of the entire body and its proximity to the nerves.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	If the gut jumps out of the wound, and it is reset as if it were the small intestine while it is fresh; and if it becomes swollen and turns black, and you see the black leu that has been cut, because it has veins and arteries; then cut what is between the ligaments, and bring the heads down from the part of the wound until the extraction is aligned with the jumping gut, and the wound bows.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the bursting of the belly
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is ruptured and the wound is small, if it can be restored with a few stitches, because I have seen that some were healed by the point of a lance; and this was the wound on the left side of the stomach, it became infected and formed an abscess, and in it was the excretion and vomiting; I treated him according to what I could, and did not stop subtleting until he was healthy, and I examined him.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him sewn, I doubted that the patient had no harm in his belly; but he had none, but delayed better measures, and ate and drank; and they said to no one whoever had a small wound in the intestine, that one must stitch it in this way: first pull out the testicles as large as possible, then assemble the lips of the wound, and when the mouth is over the testicles, if you can draw them with the lips, then close the testicles, and hold it so that it does not slip, and then do another contraction in the same way as before, until the wound is completely closed; and sew the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	The first line of the text translates to: "If the end of the bowel is inflamed and causes no harm to the patient, and it can be tied with a thread as fine as a hair from a beast's intestine, in this manner: take the end of this thread from the bowel that is mucus-free, and then tie it to the end of this filament with linen thread, then thread the filament through the needle, and sew the intestine, and then untie it at the rupture; and this manner of stitching is not worse than according to the way of marriage and hope; and if the wound is large and wide, even when it is in one of the large intestines, if it does not heal or become healthy, it should be tied with a subtle tie.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	All wounds and abscesses, when they heal, are called 'fistulas' if they are completely closed, and likewise if they are small and rounded.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And a fistula is according to the truth of nodulation, which is hard and filled with pus, or one feels pain, and is as small as a penny feather; and never in a clear jump, and sometimes wider; never tight, and sometimes fuller; never narrow, and sometimes wide; and I have spoken of this in the division of wounds, that any wound that is not healed, and has no pain, is only due to one of the seven causes: it is to know, by the small amount of pus or blood; or by malice; or because the pain is too great, and touches the lips, which does not allow the pain to leave; or there are too many boils; or the lesion is porous, and the matter is of poor quality; or the remedy is not good for the cure; or because the corruption is like a pestilence; or because the property in the region is slow digestion, and slow health, and runs away by nature; or there are veins or bones: and I have shown all these causes and their signs and remedies with medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	1. It is necessary that I inform you of the treatment for fistulas, which is performed by handwork.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	1. Fistulas occur in all parts of the body; for there are fistulas that come from large veins, arteries, nerves, or the face, intestine, bladder, or any of the ribs, or the spine, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if a part of this occurs in the primary member, it is similar to this.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	1. All the fistulas of this kind are of bad fortune and ignorance; but if there is no fistula that does not come from the part I have mentioned, and you are seeking the cure, and you see it performed, then take a needle or a nail, if the fistula is straight, as you wish; and if the fistula is crooked, then use a fine needle, for the points do not penetrate well into the crook; and if the fistula is in the hands and you cannot find it by needles, then use a nail from the same place, for the moisture is thinner at the end of a hole than at the beginning, and makes it more porous; then you will know whether it is bone or nerve, and whether it is hard or soft, and ask the patient to feel the pain when you press with your hand, and let him know if he feels any; and when you truly know the place and whether it is far from a joint, a nerve, an artery, a vein, or any of the parts I have mentioned, then follow my advice according to what I have said, and the cure will be the same as I have said, and the corrupt parts that are degenerated; and then the cure, once it is healthy and the fistula is well-lined in its place, if you follow it as much as you press, then use soft needles in medicinal ague, and insert them at the mouth of the fistula while the medicine corrodes the excess that has been added to the fount; and then use warm ointments in a clean vessel, as long as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy by this, then the cauterization is as we have said, and if the bone is corrupted by the fistula, then the cauterization is as we have said.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	1. If the limb does not pain or is dislocated, as we have said; and if the bone is discovered, and it becomes corrupted and blackened, as long as the corruption remains, then the treatment of such things depends on its health; and if it is healthy, and the bone bows so much that it becomes unsound, then the limb must be set in place as soon as possible; and if it cannot be set, then you should know that you are not strong enough to do it: if the bone is discovered and it pains as much as it can while you are present, and all the corruption is removed, then restore the bone; and if it becomes sound, then it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If this does not work, you should know that the corruption is too far advanced to be cured; if there is no other remedy than cold leeches of nature; and if there are small bones corrupted, and they are drawn out with needles, if the instrument provided for this purpose can be used, and if there are many bones, do not leave any behind; and if moisture makes things worse, and there is no error or pain, then copper and mustard should be applied, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	If you do not cauterize the bones at once, and put something on the wound that is irritating, and leave it so that the bones are moistened with pus, and if they are large bones, such as those of the thigh or knee, and only treat the corruption until the blackness has spread all over the bone, then restore the wound; and if there is a large part of the bone that is corrupted, and comes out in pieces, and it is necessary to sew up the wound, and then cure it as much as possible; and I will tell you about a fistula that came into a man's leg, so that you may give an example and help in your practice.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	The text describes the case of a young man who suffered from pain in his leg for a certain period of time. The cause of the pain was a deep wound that had become infected, and the infection spread to the entire leg. The leg became inflamed and turned into an abscess, which eventually ruptured and caused severe bleeding. The patient was treated for two years, but no progress was made in the art of hand surgery until I was called, and I examined his leg and the medicines used to cure it, as well as the corrosion caused by the wounds. The patient's face became red due to the infection, and he had a yellowish tint to his complexion.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I sewed a tent in one of these holes, and then checked all the holes, and found that some came together at the other part of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I then tried to sew it, and found a part of the bone through one of the holes, and I found the corruption spreading along the bone; I knew that what I was seeing was corrupt bone, and I made sure there was no more corruption, as much as I could; then I started to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, but I couldn't close it; then I found the corruption continuing in the bone, and I closed it with medicine; but it became healthy and was healed quickly, and I didn't want to reopen the wound because of the patient's suffering and the pain of death that I had caused him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For because the evacuation of blood is often, but it was completely healthy, and a hard stone was found in the bone, and it was well positioned and had no harm or contradiction at all, nor in the air nor coming out.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in no part of the skull, then it should be done in this way: take the strings, and draw the end of the string that is open at the top of the bone; command that it does not extend further; and take another string larger than the first one, and tie it to the string that is out of the bone, and hold the head, so that you can pull the broken string away from the bone, and cut the string where you see it, so that it does not break the string; and put a table or a board on the bone to cover the broken string; and it should be done as much as can be seen and felt, and done again as often as possible.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	1. If the bone is rotten and does not open, and the corruption is in a large or small area, if you cut through the whole; then remove the instrument, and then separate the part from the other, and make sure the corruption is on the end of the bone, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, if it corrupts the joint, and it is the bone or it contains something else; and if the corruption is in the continuation of the joints, if there is no other enemy than dough cope; and if the corruption is on the hand or on the foot, if it is very strong, but you must investigate the corrosion as it opens; and it will cleanse in all ways that you want, but the bone or the flesh will not do you harm; and be careful of the incision and the tools that cover these bones, according to the seat of the bones and the appearance of the bones, and their size and subtlety, and their growth and their smallness, and their hardness; and for this it is necessary to adapt each appearance of the tool to your own; and be careful that the work shows the instrument you have, according to the knowledge of this art, and the testimony of the ways of the diseases; if the instrument you have does not fit according to what it should.
dou feu	The first line "dou feu
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The second line "Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer;
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	The third line "Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras;
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	1. And if the wound becomes infected, when you apply it, whether you burn it with any restraining powder; then return to your medicine as soon as it is completed, then tie the swollen member with a bandage, and cure it as soon as it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to the man in his time: he had a black spot that seemed burned by fire, and this corrosion came first in his wounded hand, and it destroyed all the hand; when the man saw the corrosion, if he could not cover the hand, it became healthy; and later, after returning to the corrosion or two of the hands, it came to me, and I put certain things on it after the circumcision of the corpse, and I could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I cut off the hand, and I did not want to hope for a cure; and I also thought that if I cut my hand, it would not die, because the strength of the woman was weak; and he desperately returned to his land, and he covered his hand with something, and it became healthy; and I did not know until then that one has to suffer this for another part, if one has a trade in it.

des vils	Of warts.

de la voinne civile	of the civil vein

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	2. Those that are born between leather and hide
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois.	3. This disease is called in our land "disease of beef" because it often occurs with many wounds, and is a small wound that passes between leather and hide, and goes up and down the entire body, and is felt very well on the member of the member, as soon as it goes through the skin or if it touches it, and is caused by the humors of some people, such as snakes, vipers, and scabies or worms in the belly; and one doubts its malice, because when it passes through the body, it goes to the head, and comes to the oil, by chance returns, and destroys the oil; and this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture. Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This disease is called "winding" in our land, and is a pain that comes in various parts of the body, and spreads from one part to another; and I see what I have told you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was called a woman patient, and I saw one of my arms, and saw a small bulge in the vein of the other arm; and afterwards, I saw it rise as quickly as anything, as if it were live silver when it cut through the other arm; the pain left that arm and moved to the shoulder, and then spread throughout the body, until it came to the other arm; then she told me that it turned inside out along the entire body, just as you see.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marvel at how it moves from limb to limb, as I have never wished for this disease to occur in this manner.

Indeed, I wished for the pain to move from one part of the body to another, but I did not want it to be so severe. Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	Saiettes are various, according to their appearances and according to the hardness of the bones they pierce.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of saiettes is that some have large points, and small, and curved, and straight; and some have sharp angles, and others have rounded angles, and others have pieces; and one that pierces in any member in different ways: either in the principal members like the head, chest, liver, spleen, lungs, stomach, intestines, bladder, and similar members.

Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	of veins which are safe to open are XXXI, of which there are XVI which are the two "herbage" arteries behind the ears, called the "aspirate" veins; and the two veins in the temples that are; and the vein that is cut in front; and the vein that is cut at the top of the head; and the gounds which are on the collar; and the veins that are in the lips of the mouth, and these are the veins called "augeherich"; and the veins that are in the lower part of the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	1. The veins that are commonly found in each arm are usually five: one is the cranial, which is on the western costal side, and it is called the "crushing of the head" (vene dou chief); the other is called the "fast" (faste), and it is composed of the cranial and the basilar, and they are called the "crushing of the belly" (vene dou cuer) by the people; and the basilar if it is on the eastern costal side, it is called the "crushing of the abdomen" (vene dou ventre) and is located under the fascia, and it is the one that is usually found, which is open clearly under the bag.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The saved vein is the one between the auricular and anal openings, and if it fails; and in the leg, there are three veins: one is the corbier of the left groin, and the second saphene which is at the ankle of the right groin; and the vein called "nessel", which is in the ankle of the other groin; and in the other leg, there are three veins like those.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The healing of the veins after the ears if helpful for old catheters and drains; and the quality of the healing, as I tell you, and it is that you return to the mouth of the patient, and rub the leu or the veins with a rough cloth; then strain the mouth of the patient's collar as much as the veins appear behind the ears in the dependent dependents of the chief: take this for your own, and if you feel the pain in your own, then sign d'enche; then take the lancette, and cut through the vein bone, then gently hold your hand over all the veins until the curve and the leather and the vein are well done through, and make sure the sanc as much as you can see; then rest and lie, as long as it is healed; and I have already said the incision and the cautery of the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	1. The health of the two arteries in the temples, if they are old, hardened, and accustomed to it, and if they are affected by watery eyes, and if the patient feels pain; and if the physician draws the collar tightly, as the veins open widely; and he feels the warmth of his thumb on your cheek, and then becomes cold; then he should gently press on the vein above your index finger, cut the lancet, and gently pull the vein up, and the covering, just as you have done in the other veins, and make the incision according to your need; then release the physician's thumb, and put your index finger on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then form the wound, and leave it as long as it is sane; and we have spoken about their insertion and extraction, or the beginning of this book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The patient's condition of the vein at the front is as serious as the condition of the cranial sinus with ancient facial diseases, migraines, and bruising; and if it is true that the patient pulls on his neck while twisting, then take the instrument called "fossaeur", whose form is like this:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point on the vein, and firmly with your hand or another thing, and let the blood ooze out according to the quantity you see; then tell the patient to relax the neck, and hold the vein as long as it is safe and never once with a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	Everyone, it only matters that the flames are too hot; and the right way is to cross it, because the bone is close, and by chance the flames break when it is subtle.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The health of the two veins that are in the rings if they help the limbs, and the knee, and the wound, and the eye in the oil, and diseases of the face; and the quality of its health if it is that the patient pulls his neck twisting any line, as before; then the right way, and so is the health of the vein, a little long but not wide, and not hot, because there is no char.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are slight, by chance they are very sudden; then make a deep cut, as much as you can, and then stitch the cloth, and sew it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	If the wound of the vein is not deep enough and there is a chance of infection, and maladies of the face, as well as rashes that come on the face, and especially when it is old; and if the quality of the wound is that the skin is tight around it, then hold the wound steady in your left hand, and take a small, subtle flame, and touch the corner of the lip that is between the two nostrils, because the vein does not open very well, and it will now start to bleed; and do not apply too much pressure, and make a deep cut according to your need, then sew it up one night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the shape of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The patient's health depends on the second fingernail if it helps in the relief of pain, the beginning of menstruation, and various diseases such as empyema, corrosion, herpes, and gums; and the quality of the health if it is that the physician pulls on his collar with both hands, as we have said; and the physician being at the head of the patient's chest, and the patient's chest being held at one end, then the vein is made long and wide, then the sinus is drained, or as much as possible; then another part is done on the other vein, then the ligature is loosened, and the veins are gently pulled out so that the physician does not tighten; and it is left for the morning, if the wound is healed.
de la sainie des leivres	Of the health of the deer
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	The health of the teeth of the lips is aided in the mouth, and corruption of the genitals, and cracks in the lips, and toothache and tooth loss.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is to make the patient stand before you, and hold their chin as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the teeth, of which one is on the right side and the other on the left, and they are black because of their dark color and because they have thin black gums: therefore cut both, and if you do not know them, and you are in doubt, then cut the largest of each part, and all the same way, for it is a similar manner.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	Of the healthy tongue, the language
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	Of the healthy veins, the language
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins that are commonly found are healthy in two ways: either by pinching them with the fingers, or by using a small needle like a thorn, and they are called "anesil"; and they are wide and thin according to the size and constriction of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The form of the fire cautery is such that it is named when it is first made, and it is wide as you see.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is used to open the veins of flat hair that contain large clots of blood and are problematic; and this is the form of the fire cautery.
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	And it is more suitable for the subtle veins, and it is safer for the subtle veins, or if there is subtle blood clotting.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The health of the basilica, which is one of these veins, helps with diseases that are caused by swelling of the throat, and the neck, and the chest, and the stomach; and it is necessary for the physician to make wise decisions and to ward off the artery that is affected.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	If the artery is pricked, and blood comes out, then it should be tied off if necessary; but it should not be pricked with hot iron, but rather cut if possible.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	If the basin does not open clearly, and you must hold it, and change another one; or you do not want any rain in the basin, or you want to remove the vein from the arm: it opens clearly; and the fire is tied off with hot iron, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	If you see the vein of the wound, and you must hold the arm, and touch the vein as far as you can reach; then sign the vein is full, and then tie the arm, and cut the vein with hot iron; and watch that you do not injure the artery as you see the vein swell, because it is the artery: therefore stop.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see coming out from above as the urine of a child, and it is red and subtle, that it is not from the artery: haste to, and put your hand on long, then oste your hand on the bone that is without pain, which many times comes; and hold the shoulder, and let it be, and do not move the wound; and so be afraid, and do not move until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if it is not without pain, and it hurts you, and the doctor is not present, then perhaps the artery has opened, for the head of the wound; and subdue it.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	1. Take a scalpel from the fistula, and make it sharp, and take one of the halves and tie it well to the other; if it is without staining, it is good; if not, then the cure, as we have said, with the powders that stain blood; the stains are not more severe in other positions for the small wound of the wound, and the pain of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	2. The health of the vein is in its environment if it treats the wound with blood from the head and chest, as we have said, because it is composed of basilic and cephalic matter; therefore, the surgeon must be careful with the nerve that is affected, and if it does not become too much in front, and it relieves the nerve, and it becomes swollen and healthy, and by chance cannot heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open any holes for its subtlety, then it must be the surgeon to cleanse the instrument with wine; and remove the nerve from your body.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is blood between the two veins, if it is long.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	The salve for the head if it helps, that it attracts blood from the head and helps the wounds; and it is better to touch with olive oil or with mirth oil, because it is the most safe of all the veins, because it does not harm the nerves or arteries.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	All, it is better to use the lighter tool, and do not hurt anyone the first time, and then continue; and by chance, the salve may cause some pain in some people, but it does not hurt anyone the first time.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of health depends on your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you need to know about health is that it is not acquired overnight, but must be maintained to avoid diseases coming; and it should be made in one of the three veins: the head, fast, and belly; and it should be done at the beginning of the day, and before noon, and after dinner, when the sign of repletion appears; and it should be done on the first or second day, after two or three hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	The health that is maintained with diseases has no fixed determination, but rather when the child is of twelve years or the woman of four months and a half, it should be made.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	Nese should not be made healthier than those who have passed 60 years.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	If one appears healthier than those who have passed 60 years, it is because they have not defecated for a long time, if they have a lot of food and drinks retained in the intestines, if they do not have excessive fatty or alcoholic foods; and if they become healthier after a passionate attack of colic, vomiting, and abdominal discomfort, and many women menstruate, and many women urinate, and many women defecate, and many women sleep, and many women wake up, and many women eat and drink, and whatever virtue it may be, by the arm or by the course; then subtly the humors are reduced if they are not too large by meat and by drinks and by medicines, if you have enough; then take a bath, nothing else will help, to reduce the heat and to become healthy from the inside out, as we have said; and keep away from excessive work, labor, luxury, and such things; and be modest and joyful, and be healthier than those who are sick; and rub your arms twice or three times with cold oil, then stretch your arm with the elbows extended as much as possible, because if it is too tight or small, you cannot do it without help; then rub your hands with a little oil, then put your left hand on the same spot where the intestines are, and touch it gently until it becomes healthier.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	For there are veins that run like cords in the healthy, and if they are many, then when one is set on fire, it withdraws from the flame, and cannot open the vein, and then it is one of those; and if the vein is too tightly closed, then it is the patient's wound that is too tight, therefore it is necessary that the physician be advised in these matters.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	And if the vein opens for the first time, it is good; but if not, then it continues a little more of that joint or suddenly, and if it does not open, it is because it is contracted.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	When the patient looks at it and the pain subsides, the patient should leave it alone for one or two hours, and do not tie the arm: by chance, scars may appear; do not enter the bath, then resume the cure if it pleases; and when the wound is small, or the cut subtle and you doubt that there is as much blood as you see, because it is more in the wound than you think, and the work is done quickly, otherwise the patient will suffer much when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see the shoulder swell, if you do not restart the cure and put a little oil on it, because it softens the chest of the pain, and dries the oiled part; and afterwards apply oil to each wound that you have sown in the wounds, to strengthen the course of the pain; and this itself makes triage and bowels of the abdomen, when it is put on the shoulder; if subtly it does not come out and dries when it is too big.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	When there are large abscesses that keep coming back, if they are not healing within a few days of the vein opening, and you have wet gauze on hand, and it is held for an hour, then you should do this after the sanc is drained from the vein, and if there is no blackness or discoloration at the site after several days, then you may not need to do anything else. If you see this, do not apply any aloe or other remedy in the form of milk, mustard, or similar substance.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times abscesses and inflammation occur at the sanctuary of the basilica: then place your hand on it, and if it feels painful, compress the hand with your thumb.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	1.
