If you do not put anything on the part we have said, because of accidental cut without the artery; but I apply a dry plaster to endure the limb, then another treatment, until it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	2. And apply to every pain according to its quantity of virtue and color of the poison.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	3. For if the blood is black, do not let it flow until it is red; and if you see it large, do not let it flow until it is thin; and if it is too hot, do not let it cool.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	4. And it is good for the one who is in pain and sick, and has skill in extracting poison, to make a larger wound, and let the flames be wide; and for the one who is weak, do the opposite, and it will become healthier often and easily, and it should be made healthier by cutting across, not by pricking; and this way of making healthy is saved from the spreading of poison and the weakness of the nerve, and it is worth much that the healthy wound is not wide.
Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	For the one who needs to be made well, it is necessary to give him flat bread in the juice of ripe grape must; if he is cold, then three or four times, or more, and if he has a cold complexion, then before the flat bread in honey or honey syrup with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and chives, and well-scented honey.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if he feels better after vomiting, after the evacuation of blood, it is necessary that he drinks charbroiled honey and a subtle scented honey, and uses other things as we have said in the division or chapter of sincope, for the evacuation of veins.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	If he sees his arm swelling again, and becoming more so, if it comes to that, when he is overcome by great weakness, which he gains a little at a time, according to the amount of his strength continuously.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And if he sees his arm swelling again after the first time it was weak, and he feels strong, if he is strong seven hours after the first time he was weak, or after the second hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And if he feels strong from another part, if he should become stronger on the second day or the third.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has blood from the heart that has been inflamed, and causes fever; if it comes to a great quantity, and opens the wound as much as it can; then when you treat all the conditions of health, and place your hand on the chest where it is healthy, so that the death does not come from the chest of pneumonia, and this happens many times when the patient becomes indifferent; and it does not matter if you see the arm swelling again and let out blood the second time, and the wound is closed, so that you press on it; but if it is cold, you must extend the arm quickly, because it would be wrong; but leave it as long as it is healthy the second time; or if you do not reach the point of flame, until the cold that is in the chest thaws out and puts back the wound a little, and presses lightly on it.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	If the vein is inflamed, and it is not held steady, until the abscess is relieved.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	If it is necessary to draw the blood twice, if the vein is in the same arm or in another arm, or in the other hand.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The arm is healthy because the vein of the shoulder is not affected by the dislocation.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	If the arm is injured, and the patient has hot water in his hand, as long as the color is red; then it should be tied loosely, if the vein appears well, then the hand should now pass through, not too wide or too long; and the wound should be large enough near the joint of the hand, and if it cannot be stopped, it should re-warm the hand in hot water, and let out the blood as much as possible; if this is the case, do not warm the hand in hot water again, because it will cause more inflammation than necessary; the injury of this vein is safer than all other veins, because it has not been torn or damaged.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The patient's hand is injured and can cause all sorts of stomach ailments, and this is the way to treat it: apply heat to the hand, and soak it in hot water as long as the vein remains visible; if the hand becomes cold, wrap it in a warm cloth and do not let it dry in the wound, and do not put it back in cold water until the skin is no longer visible in the wound.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated enough blood as is necessary for your skill, if you put the vein oil and seal it firmly, and then do the same to each vain.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The patient with the hand on the left side is suitable for treating mouse disease, and I do everything as I have said for the right.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The health of the gallbladder is suitable for treating all diseases that are poor in the chest, such as diseases of the lungs, and retention of flowers, and disease of the arms and legs, and old wounds, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of their health is that the patient is not afraid of acute fever, and wipe the vein as soon as it bleeds, and press on the joint at the puncture; and if the vein is at the ankle, and through the puncture into the rain, then the rain is safe, or larger at the ankle, which is better.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you have clean hands, if they are not dirty, and the wound is large, and it has to be crossed as in cutting; then the scars will appear.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if you cannot remove it, then put your hand in cold water, and let the wound dry well.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if the wound becomes clean the first time, and recurs in the second place because the wound is salty; do not doubt of nerve, as we have said, and then make a suture with the other hand perfectly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The pain in the sciatic nerve is at the ankle of the foot, and its cure is the pain in the knee, when it is full of blood.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	1. And the quality of his health if he is subjected to or bathed, and draws in his ankle IIII times while twisting, as otherwise the vein will not open; and if it opens, then the healthy in all ways that you can, and crossing; and it is wise that you copy it, as the wound is safe and it is returned to the hands of men.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	2. And if you do not copy it, then the healthy of the wound that opens or is deep, and towards the small toe, and cover with needles; and make as much blood as you see, and then release the limb, and put on cotton and draw; it is now healthy.
des sainies de ventouse	Of causes of birth
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventuses are made of horns, or antler, or iron; and ventosations can be done in two ways: either by cutting and drawing blood, or by cutting without bleeding.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosation which is made by cutting is done in two ways: either it is all fire, or hot; and ventosation which is made by cutting and drawing blood is made in twelve courses of the chest, where the one part is all the head, and the other part is the collarbone; and the other is the shoulder; and the other two are the costal bones; and the ventosation of the chin; and the ventosation of the shoulder blades; and the ventosation of the crutches; and the ventosations of the arms; and the ventosations of the legs; and the ventosations of the ankles; and the ventosation does not touch any veins, only small veins that are scattered in the chest, and for this reason no one is harmed as with a wound; and it is only necessary that it be anesthetized, neither hot nor cold, in no disease that comes from repletion, as long as the chest is empty.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	1. And if necessary for diseases come to seek, or by habit, if the midwife each hour at the beginning of every month, or at the end, and also in every ten; for there are those who, when they have to assist at childbirth, have a heavy burden; and if such as truly experience fullness and fever in their face, and in their chest, and in their belly, and in their collar, and their eyes are closed; and those who truly experience a chill in their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and spit out blood; and if there are such as truly experience fainting, and see by only cold blood, and death, and strange things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	When we saw these signs, and at the same time when the month was over, we commanded them to fast for three hours after noon.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The salve of the mouth helps to alleviate the pain of the head... that comes with these wounds, and it is only after all the blood has been evacuated; and this fasting is in the care of the salve of the head, and it is only for those who have a cold complexion or have had a fever, as this does great harm; and for this reason, the watchmen use it, and those who have cold diseases.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who often get better, if they become oblivious, and therefore it is necessary to put the ventouse a little further down due to the fear of oblivion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	The ventouse is in the neck of the shoulder and the base of the skull, and therefore it is used for the relief of pain, and to relieve the stomach and intestines, and for all, and for repletion; and it is necessary to insert it slightly, because if it is too tightly held, it can cause oblivion or stomach and intestine distention.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	The ventouse is placed on the costal arch of the neck to relieve the pain of the head, and it eases and relieves migraines, and prevents strangulation, and relives the pain at the roots of the teeth, and it is in the neck of the skull; and it is necessary that you command the patient to express their hand when putting it on, so as not to cut the artery, and to prevent dislocations.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The windings of the throat are not worth the disease of the mouth, and the corruption of the genitals, and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and it is in the legs of the sickly lips.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The windings of the shoulders are worth the disease that comes from chlor and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The windings of the elbows are as valuable as three wounds in the arms, because they attract blood from these large wounds; and it is commanded to the healer not to make them too tight, because the elbow is naked of covering and knows how to numb and harden.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The first line of the text translates to: "The forceps that is used on the mare's foal if it has not given birth in due time, and has diseases, and it is necessary that the forceps be large and sharp, so that it can properly grip; and by chance, if it is too delicate, it may break; and it causes great pain.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The second line of the text translates to: "If the forceps on the legs are open, as they attract blood from all parts of the body, and relieve old pains of the thighs, and buttocks, and bladder, and draw the foreskin; and they are in the legs of the II Sophonies, and the II Chevilles, and they make the body weak after long use, and cause pain in more positions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	1. The manner to insert the needle if you put it first empty, and then again, and move it gently, and continue doing this until you see the redness and swelling, and open the wound; then clean it, and replace the needles, and prepare the position of the cors (a type of bandage) because there are those who have very delicate skin and large pores: if you manage to injure once only, and make wide wounds, and a few puckered ones; and then lightly rub.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	2. And if it is large, if it wounds twice: the first time by making the vein more subtle.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is not treated immediately, it can be wounded a third time; and when we wish to draw out little blood, we only succeed once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we wish to draw out much blood, we often succeed; and if it is not treated immediately, it can be wounded a third time, and it may end in death, especially for those with thick skin and hard bones, and those with pores that are easily penetrated, which should be oiled with the opening oils of olive, or almond oil, or sesame seed oil; and if it is in wool, olive oil, or cresson oil, or lis oil, or chamomile oil, or another similar oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the excess is large and cold, take warm oil, or balsam, or anise oil, and apply it.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the skin is dry and large pores, it is not recommended to apply oil, but it is recommended to wash after the ventilation of rose water, or cold water, or mushroom water, or violet water, or porcelain water, or other similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And if the mouth is dry, if it rises from honey, or rose water, and summer, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	Those who have excessive superfluity rise from wine vile, or ague of sweat, or decoction of anet or chamomile, or other similar things; and they do not become healthier before bathing but after bathing, an hour or two; and they do not sleep before ventilation, and they must wake up when it is time for ventilation, and when it is ventilated.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And when those who are healthy become enfeebled, and their thirst is too great and inflamed; if they consume cold things, such as pomegranates, endives, and leeks, and similar things; and they drink punch, and char of chafing, and moist meats.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	1. Those who have a cold complexion, if they drink honey syrup and sweet wine, which is between vinegar and new wine, and drink little, and drink punch and small pears and peppers; and when they start to sweat, they must drink more than they usually do; and it is necessary to give some men once a trial or massage before the ventilation, or afterward, to comfort the main limbs; and it should be done subtly, but only those who are cold should drink.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	2. The wounds that are made to hurt are those that are made on the liver, and on the spleen, and gout, and on the stomach and bowels and bladder and gallbladder, because this member does not suffer much pain unless it is attracting pain from one part to another, as we do when the mammary glands are sick; to reduce the viscosity that is in the member, as we do on the stomach and bowels to make the member more comfortable; and to relieve the pain when it has opillation or incision, if it is attracted by accidental opillation, or if it is without piercing of the loin; and then it is made as soon as it is placed on the liver and spleen when it has retained much viscosity, and these wounds are administered empty to suck only; and they are never administered together with fire, and never with hot aqua tede, as in some diseases that cause great pain, and in this way we fill the wound with hot water or with the herbs that have been cooked.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The form of the vacuum administered by fire is: It has two palm-wide and half-inch branches, and has one cost at the end of the small puncture, as if to insert a needle, and has a groove of iron or steel in front so that it does not bend the patient's arm when putting it on the limb; and in the middle, there is a hole of iron or steel to insert a thong, and according to the diseases and weight of those who take them, the vacuums of children are different from those of adults, and are not as wide as those of the thin, but as wide as the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	1. And it must be put on this dressing to the limb: take the wax candle or liniment, and put it through the hole of the vessel that is in the dressing, so that it does not burn the patient; then put it on the limb, and you must have the wounds as we have said, if you see, if there is vapor, and you take off the dressing; and take on the liniment as before, and renew it often, if you can.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	2. In the dressing where it is maintained in sickness with pleurisy, there is no vent, and no wound, and it is not maintained except when it is clear of fever, and it is put on the limb only then; and this is the form:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without being sterilized, they are only used in the limbs where it is possible to put a ventouse, such as the lips and genitals, and similar parts; and in them, if they are dry like charcoal, or neis, and others like that; and the quality of the user is that when you find without without being in soft waters, if you take them; you put a nut in soft water, as long as they are similar, and have no bellies; then it is healthy for the vein and the ventouse, then clean the member as much as it is red, and put on the nails; and when they are smooth, and close, if it is the one or it is possible to put a ventouse, you put it, because this is afterwards.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not, then raise the leg of the injury, and then the ankle; and if the patient is healthy too soon after the surgery, then apply cold linen to the wound, and leave it on as long as the wound is swollen; and if the swelling increases, then apply hot vitrol or galls, and similar things, as long as it is swollen; or you can half the fever blisters and let them stay on the leg as long as they are burning at the leg, until it is now anesthetized; and if you have more injuries, then take more fever blisters.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	1. If the wounds do not take on the salve, then cleanse the lesion with fresh blood or thread as much as it will absorb, and then insert them, and as they feel the wound, if they sting; and when you see that they smarten, then put a little aloe and silk or charcoal, or smoke now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	2. This is the beginning of the book of wounds.
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	3. These cauteries are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are a restoration of wounds and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	4. Explain to me, dear friend, what the science of this cauterization is, that none of the ancient books or letters have shown it; and for this reason, the science has been lost in our land, because I have never found any book; and I do not know if there are any, except perhaps through the science of the ancient books, or by my own study and treatment of the science, and by experiment, and by the habit of my life; and I have described in this cauterization what is contained in it, and summarized at the end, and shown clearly the forms of the strangulations that are made, as I have done in these two chapters before.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	1. It is therefore necessary that we say the introduction of this book, the words and chapters, and the surgeons understand their meaning, and they should pay attention to the truth, so that those who have experienced it and learned this noble art can teach others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	1. I say that if there is any breakage, dislocation, twisting, or tightening, and it comes to nothing, if nothing helps, then like the weakest of men, women, or children; or if it is not very tense, or too loose; and if the hands are too cold, it means cold joules, and char of deer and rabbit, and do not drink any wine, nor eat thin charcoal, and do not fill the veins with blood too much, until you have no doubt of apoplexy or expansion of matter in the member; if the patient's face returns to its former state as it was before.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	When the bones begin to heal, if it is necessary to remove the patient's meat that causes great swelling, or if it has viscosity, like wheat cooked in hot water, and tests, and pies, and pancakes made of wool, and eggs, and fresh fish, and large wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For the swelling decreases and the fracture is less soon.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And you advise that the bones broken by hard blows and decreeptures cannot be well repaired or stitched according to their nature due to the weakness of the members, but not as those of small children; but if it is necessary to repair the large tendons that were torn and joined to the member together, as much as possible, and do not leave any part of its work, and for this reason it is necessary to cut off large pieces of meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	The treatise explains that there are various types of fractures, each with its own characteristics and causes.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	However, the fracture of the head is different from that of the arm or leg, and I will explain all types of fractures in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	There are fractures that occur when falling, and others that result from being struck, similar to the size of a quill used for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	If a fracture is accompanied by a wound, it can be a small cut or nick.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	Each fracture has its own mechanism and appropriate instruments for restoration, depending on the type of fracture and the patient's memory. The fracture of the bone is caused by twisting and widening due to the force applied, and may be difficult to reduce if the patient resists. If there is no deformity or pain, it may not be a fracture, but there may be deformity, a cut, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If you cannot move it with your hand alone, but apply the medicine that comes after, and then gently pull it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And you check the fracture that will be in the arm, and the two parts are disjointed, you can now properly align them, unless the wound bleeds again; and if the wound bleeds again, until no blood comes out, as long as the wound is calmed; then it should be aligned gently and wisely, and you should check that the restoration of the arm is lighter than the restorations of other parts or pieces; then gently pull it now.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	1. If there are pieces in the bone of the foot, and they are of the second part, it is hands or fingers, or a part of your hand that is small members, or two cords, or one cord and your hand; and place the member according to its natural figure, so that when the parts of the broken member are realigned, if you adjust with your hands the additions in their places in the mouth that you please, and keep that by your dislocation no harm to the malady or pain; and adjust well the two heads of the bones according to the best forms.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	2. If it feels good in your hand when it seems that it is not well: if it curves beautifully, and is not strained too much, do not press as those who come by their dislocation cause pain and contraction to the member, as we have wanted many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	When the limb is in pain, if the patient holds it still, neither by day nor by night, nor when turning, nor in any other way, and ensures that the limb is securely held so that it does not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when it does not feel any pain, if it is not yet dislocated, and it is necessary to put the limb in proper position so that it does not feel any pain; and keep it in place until it is fully restored, and the quality of the broken member is according to what I will tell you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	It is known that the broken member can be different in size and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	1. For if he has many limbs, as if it were brais and doss, and similar: if they cover the cloths of fine linen and silk; and the large ones, as if they were cuxe and jambe: if they cover a wide and hard rope, for the wide limbs embrace all the large member, and draw it evenly, unless it has no taiche; then they lightly thread the ends, three or four times according to the member, and draw the hand a little by all the limb, then go to the break of the fracture and draw it less, that the fracture may slightly move the break; and soften the limb a little and a little, as you pregnantly take part of the healthy part of the leu sain, then take another limb, and turn the end towards the broken part; then return to the part opposite the break, and draw it gently, not too much nor too little, as we said in the first fracture; then put between the ends of lin or silk, as they are equal, until they are all alike, then put all the stitches well made on, if it has not aposteme or enfleure.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	If it has swollen or become infected, if you put something soothing on it, such as alum or a piece of flax, or a bandage made from linen, or a piece of palm fiber, and leave it alone for a while; then pull your eyes together, and they should be even one-half of a wide cord, or of flax that is worn out, or of bands made from palm fibers, and they should be in this shape:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the piece you put on the wound be larger and wider than the others; and it should also be long as it is for the little or big member; then pull your eyes together in the same way as you did at the first hour, then tie a thread around it, like you did in the first hour with the wound; the more stretched it is, the less; and the thread must not be too tight or too loose, and it should be of linen; for if the thread is too thick, as I have seen the works of the women who make the hours of the linen ties, and it is a great error, because the hour cannot be equal if it is too fine, and it only serves to have less space between each eyelet.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is dislocated due to the hairs of the eyelids after plucking them in good health, if they make holes in the skin, or cause inflammation, if it does not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the forceps, and the nail is broken, I will tell you the cure for this afterwards.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And he should not try to straighten all the broken limbs at once.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not possible to put the nails in until after several years or seven, or according to the patient's strength; and here is the way the ancient emplausters were used to restore breaks, dislocations, and twists: and that you take flour that is made from the flour of mills, and knead it with a lot of beer, and make this dough, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the emplauster restoring breaks in other positions, and even in women and children, because it is not too hard or too weak.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	1. Another way to mend fractures and dislocations and twists: take barley, linen, oil, arabian gum, and mugate, in the ratio of 20 parts; mix and add rosemary, in the ratio of 5 parts; and make a powder, and mix with animal urine; if the complexion of the face is hot, use this plaster as it is of good composition and restores broken bones well, and is beneficial to many men.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	1. Another way to treat twists: take mugate and vismalve, in the ratio of 20 parts; mix and add rosemary, in the ratio of 79 parts; acacia, in the amount of 6 parts; arsenic, in the amount of 1 part; and cook well, and administer with hot or animal urine.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	1. Another way to mark joints and bones is to use the legs and their roots, and soothe the pain that follows, and the breakage: take fresh leaves, and grind them into oil and cooked fat, and place on the leg.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	2. These plasters do not repair anything, but they are useful for soothing abscesses and properly addressing bone pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	3. Another plaster to repair broken bones: take dried fig leaves and earth oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	4. Another plaster to repair the bone fracture and to help heal the abscess: take dried fig leaves and earth oak leaves, grind them together, and make a plaster.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	The root of viscloth, chamomile, violet flowers, flour of violets, and each part; and grind, and mix with wine, and wash your members, and apply with fresh coriander water or with water, and use.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to plaster more forcefully than the first, when an abscess is coming out of the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take the roots of viscloth, and the linseed meal, balm, honey, and without soap, and violet and chamomile flowers, of each part; grind, and marinate with salt water or sweet water, or with wine according to the chill of the member and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras states that no material is used to set a broken bone for restoration, and nothing else, and he says it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	It appears that Galien suggests that when setting a broken bone for restoration, one should use dry things like cheese, mirrory aloes, incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to illustrate the value of a wound and pain is to use raw meat, such as beef, or the feet of an ostrich, and vinegar, and the bricks, and in making the plaster and applying it to the limb.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then the pain subsides a little later, and one must take care that the patient does not feel any pain in their joint, nor any swelling or inflammation; if it does not subside by hand pressure, then if pain comes to the joint, or pricking, itching, or tenderness, if you hurry, and lift it, and now apply the plaster; take a light cloth, wet with seawater, dip in cold water, and lift the limb until the prickling stops, and soothe the pain; then let the limb rest for an hour, then put on a dry cloth, moisten it with cold or rose oil, and put on a bandage, as long as you are sure not to have an aposteme; let the inflammation in the limb subside, and soothe the pain, then resume the application of the plaster, a little subtle, and a little emplaster, and do not strain it too much; gradually as it becomes healthy.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	If you see that the wound is bleeding, swollen, painful, and inflamed, and you have the skill to plaster and bandage, if it recurs, as you did initially.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	If you do not see any sign of improvement within three days or four, or seven, and never more than twenty days, as you have seen, the fracture sets in, and the bone approaches the joint; therefore, the restraint is more stricter, and the flesh grows larger, as I have said before; if you see the leg becoming drier than it should be, you should bathe it with warm water every time you clean it, at least once a day, and keep a small piece of cloth wet; through this treatment, you will cut off the nourishment to the bone, and stop the pain that the flesh causes: this is good, and if it is done correctly, and I do not know anything else, I can only say that it is uncomfortable and must be done straightly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of various kinds of wounding
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many kinds of wounds are, and diverse shapes; for there are wounds made by the thrust of a spear, and which pierce the bone entirely, as if it were wood; and therefore this kind of wound is called "piercing.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	The spear pierces the bone by different senses of the point, and is called this kind of wound "absolute"; and it is the wound of these two great or small ones.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if it is made by a thrust that is embedded, or cut, or by the edge of a pierce, or by the point after a pierce, or by other such means.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	If there is a persistent wound, which approaches the skin that is exposed to the bone, or it is under the bone, and this is the injury or large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	If the wound is repaired in the bone as subtle as a thorn, and it is a small cut, and for this it is called this wound "capillary"; and if the wound is made by injuring a pierce, or by tearing, or by something seeming, and it enters the piece of the bone, and it is the same as the heated one when they were heating the cauldrons; if it enters the pierced hole.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And there are more cases where the bones are moist, like that of a child; and they occur in all these ways of fracture that are made lighter than these; and I will speak about it in his language.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let's examine all the ways of fractures by the methods used, and by the corrupted char that is used.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The apparent appearance is known by the fact that when one discovers the bone, and rubs it with a cloth, if the dark fracture is not wide open.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of the fracture, keep a close eye on the patient's condition, and if you see no serious complications, such as vomiting, confusion, apathy, muscle relaxation, fever, and redness, and other symptoms that cannot be cured, seek medical attention.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	If you do not see an unexpected accident, and you expect a cure to begin.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	When the bone comes first to you, and it is in your hand, if it is necessary to cut the bone before the fortieth day, then you must.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	If it is in this way, if you have cut the bone before the ninth day, then the wound that we have mentioned will be corrupted and the accident will come.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	If the bone fracture comes near the hollow that covers the knee, then it is necessary to cut the divided part if you want to: and you must cut the knee of the patient's wound in all the ways you can think of, and cut the plague more severe than you can think of, and the bone comes out to reveal the plague or the aposteme, if it helps that comes, and you fill the leg with oiled powdered silk; and let the plague rest as long as the aposteme is calmed and secured from decorrement of sanc; then start cutting the bone, and it is done according to twelve ways of cauterization: one way if you cut at the narrowest part before, and that is the form.
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then, a larger piece is cut than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method is if you have many different sizes of pieces, some narrow and others wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron; and you perform them lightly, so you do not cut the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and dense, it comes to pass that you perforate it too much, otherwise, if you make pieces with sharp edges, they must not go beyond the end of the bone, and there should be a margin or a circle that does not let the edge go beyond the bone; and you must have more pieces, if each one fits in its socket of the bone's thickness, if you have sharp edges for your test; and this is the form of the three methods of cutting:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality to perceive the broken bone is that you put wet cloth on the bone, and turn it around as much as you can until you feel the bone is perceived; then put the cloth on another part a little later, and then do everything else, then cut the incisions in the bone that is between the holes, and do it as subtly as you can, and lightly, as we have said, as you trace the bone with your hand, or with any of the nails, pincers; and make sure you do not touch the skull or the face.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have perceived and cut the bone, if the wound covers the other instrument that seems like an incision, but it should be more thin and subtle than the other incision; and if it does not cover any small bones, nor any scales, if the light bones are gently in the nails, then cure the wound with tents and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of opening is if it is done by the Galiens' method, which is safer; and the force is very great, and this is their saying.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to remove a part of the bone, where the fracture is open and bleeding. Once you have removed this part, measure from the edge of this incisional lenticular loop, of which the shape is:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut too much, and the part that is cut is towards the bone; then with a small scalpel, if you lightly touch the entire bone, and be careful of the cloth that is loose; if it is near the bone, if it is light, because it affects the bone uncomfortably, and causes pain.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	When the fracture of the bone does not pierce through the skin, and the bone is only covered by soft tissues, and it has small pieces, if they cover that roughness, and smooth the scales with a subtle rasping tool that you must have several quantities of, to adapt each limb to its use according to the type and position of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you shave in front of a coarse rasping tool, and then switch to a softer one, and continue doing this as much as it is necessary.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In every other hair cutting and subtle fracture, you must adapt according to its direction; and this is something that cannot be undone by the one who has studied in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	1. If the dislocation is discovered, it comes to light that you must preheat the linen according to the size of the wound, and apply olive oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled linen, and apply olive oil and olive oil, and place it over the first linen; and do this more gently so as not to burn the syfac, then administer through other linens, and do not strain it too much, and leave it for one or two days, until the aposteme is pacified, then remove it, and apply medicines such as roots of lis, flour of times, powder of incense, and aristolochum, and similar things; and from these things make powder, and place it on the wound, and apply further medicines without mordication; and when the wound is clean, do not leave the ointment or let the bow assemble under the skin, for if the bow assembles under the skin, it causes great harm to the patient, as it comes into contact with the flesh and causes great pain; for if something mordant is placed on the syfac, it causes great harm to the patient.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	If no accidents come to the patient, if no one doubts, as we have said, if there is any doubt in sense.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if darkness only comes forth by medicine that we have put in place, which has some virtue, then you must use a part of honey, and three parts of rose oil and one part of glue, and pour it on the face; then the cure will be done in the ways of cures that we cover, as long as it is healthy.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Wise ones, no time have ever broken the two parts of the nose, or only one, for they are bones; and this is cartilaginous, and does not break, unless it is bent or twisted, and then it becomes healthy.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	When one of the two parts is broken, if you cut off your small finger or thumb, and place the break evenly at the end of your index finger, and in the pocket as long as it does not deviate from its natural shape; and do this lightly, and make sure that the patient does not feel pain through your touch.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	If the break is in the middle of the nail and cannot be reached by the thumb, then you must place it evenly at the tip of a large pocket.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	If the break is in the other part, then you can repeat the process and restore the first joint if possible; otherwise, after the ninth or tenth day, when the inflammation has subsided, cut off the tip of the nail and take linen strips to cover the broken part, if the break is in a different place.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	If you cut another part, it will bleed; and if the wounds are large, they fill the cavities with pus.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And no restaurer will say that one must smooth the wounds with a blade, and each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It seems to me that this is well, but they must be smoothed in the making of oven ash and bone powder; then leave the wound, until the bone is hard and the cartilage becomes firm.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And no time is it cutting sheep's wings in the flesh of wounds, and if it is soft and draped around, and holds the bandage, and blows the salves among; or do as you have seen.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if the swelling comes to the eye while you are working, if it is made of wool or cotton that has been greased with oil of rosemary, or in a pot of vinegar.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the swelling does not come to the eye, if it is made of plaster made from flour and cinnamon powder, and melted with lamb's wax, then put it in light splints, and do not tie the knot too tightly; and if the eye cut is small, and it is cut into thin pieces, if the stitches are comfortable for this, then sew it up, and treat the wounds carefully, and soothing, as long as there is no pain. And if there is no wound on the eyelid, if the eyelid is treated with poultices of herbs, and bandages are applied as needed, until it is healthy.
de la routure de la mandibule	Of the dislocation of the lower jaw
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the lower jaw is dislocated, there is no wound, and the fracture is slight only, and not in two pieces, but rather a thin crack, which can be felt, if one knows how to do it lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It is necessary, if the fracture is in the right side of the jaw, to place your index finger in the mouth of the patient; and if the fracture is in the left side of the jaw, then place your index finger in the right hand and gently feel the break, and inform the other hand of its width.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the fracture of the lower jaw is described as a second degree, then it comes that you administer extension of two parts, as long as it is even.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if the teeth move, or fracture, then take a gold, silver, or silk thread, and stitch it into the broken lower jaw, and then place one double fold of cloth on it; and place a well-made rope or a piece of leather long and wide according to the jaw, and tie it to the mouth that you use, and command the patient to rest, and give light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	And if you see that the figure changes, if the jaw is not aligned, and then return to the point where it was; and apply plaster with a lot of flour or wheat flour, after you have cooled down the cerete; and apply light plaster on it, and let it dry, and the disposition of the patient does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times it becomes healthy in three weeks.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if the wound becomes inflamed, then we have said many times what to do about it.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and multiple wounds, a small piece of bone may be dislodged from the bone; if the osseous structure is subtle, it can be easily repaired.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is narrow, then widen it according to your needs.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the pieces of bone, and there is no need for them, if the wound is wide, and place them in removable dressings as needed, until it is healthy.
de la forcele	Of the force
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.
