The force breaks more often in front of the shoulder, towards the elbow, and the fracture is described in three ways: it is broken and separated in two, and it has pieces, and it is the lighter one to restore; or it is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	And the incision is when the fracture has pain, that you have two assistants, if one ties the shoulder that feels the force of the break; and the other extends your collar towards the part; then put the fracture in your two hands, so that it forms as it should, and there should be no appearance or discomfort.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have further experience, if you stretch the shoulder of the patient, place a round stone or a piece of cloth or linen on the shoulder, and make it as large as needed; and hold and gently apply the stone to your hand so that you can even out the fracture, just as you should.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you do not treat the head of the force with care, because it comes in front, and the patient may fall on his face or head, and place the shoulder outside the eye socket, and support the shoulder with your hand until the bone of the shoulder is lifted.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then address the fracture to your two parts, and if you can dislodge the fragments, then you must sell them; and take out the lighter pieces, and if the part cannot be joined by any overhang, if it is on one of the incisions you have made; but you must remove the force of this instrument to warn the face:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit. Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If only the small splints are broken, it is best to extend them lightly and make them even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	And if it is the large splint, it should be strained more firmly; and extend it over the thumb, and raise the pouch of the hand higher than the others, and the fingers should be lower than the others, and the maltreat should be at its own side, and the thumb raised above, so that the maltreat does not suffer any labor; then extend the other parts of the arm to the opposite side or to the elbow, and some other parts to the other hand.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	And then he places the head in its place, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	And if it breaks into pieces, he places each in its place, and if there are no loose pieces that point to the bone, and you cannot restore it to its place, then as we have said before, set the bone and the head.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the break there is a wound, I have spoken to the single cauterizer; if he takes care of it.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of restoration, there are pustules that ooze, if he makes a gauze pad from rose oil and wax candle, which is neither too hard nor too soft, and he dries it subtly as long as the pustules ooze, until they are calmed.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	Then take the knife, and put the powder of the mill with a lot of urine on it, then make the holes, and let the bristle be larger than the others; and see if it has six bristles or arms in other positions: whether it is in one of the bones, or in two; and pull it more under the bristle than anywhere else, and less by moving away, as I said at the beginning of this chapter; and let the hairs that are under the bristle be moist and slippery, and not too hard or sharp; and let the thread, which is taken out, be of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And reward the member and the limb after some years.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if any accidents come to the member, such as itching that comes to the member, if you wet the member with hot water until the itching is calmed, and let the member rest in its place.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then the inflammation resumes, and if the limb is smoothed and the bones are revealed, and it seems like something, if it is removed.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if the swelling is not coming to the member because it is too swollen, because there are no poultices that can relieve it, and let it rest for some time until the swelling decreases and then extract it.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	If these things do not come to the patient, if he does not loosen the dressing for 20 years.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	If the dislocation is not reduced, then the patient can move his hands to his collarbone, and it should be even, and he should be able to move and sway, and sleep on his back; and one should hope that this reduction is restored in 300 or 350 years, or by chance in 20 years, depending on the compositions and complexions of the virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the wrist fracture
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	Wishes that on the back of the hand and in the two wrists there are few fractures, and only painful swelling many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	When the palm of the hand is broken or crushed, if the patient feels pain, and then straightens it naturally in front of him; then places his hand on the extended toe, extends the broken bones, and places the toes evenly in the joints, as long as they are well-joined; then applies plaster and stitches, if necessary, then puts an elephant's leg according to the quantity of the foot; and it is wrapped in a drape of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	If the fracture is in the heel of the foot, near the sole of the plant, then make a gauze ball, and instruct the patient to tie it around their broken heel; then stretch a long gauze, and it should be as large as the sole of the hand, and stretch it, if possible.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	If the fracture is at the neck, then if you place a splint on it and another one in the plant, if the hand is over and straight, then the bone totally enters the hand, and it is held between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	If the fracture does not come from either of us, if it is tight, then if you straighten it, as it should; and hold it with the plant, and if you see that you need to put a splint on the right side to raise the fracture, and do not move; and if the fracture is in other bones, such as the index or one of the others, if it is tight, and the hand lies on the healthy finger that comes after; or you tie them all in one hand, as much as you can, or you put a splint on it, as I have said; and pay attention to the restoration and the position of the abscess, and whatever comes, as I have said.
de la cuixe brisie	Of the broken limb
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bone of the limb is often broken, and it can be seen when it turns forward and backward; the restoration if it lies in the bones of the fracture, and the other does not.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient groans when it hurts, then extends each member of its limb evenly; and this is when the fracture is separated from the bone.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is close to the root of the limb, then some of the bones are turned away from the point of impact, and the others are broken at the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And when it has been drawn to the bone, and then let loose the ligaments of the bone, and the extension is equal; then place the thumb on the bone even with your two hands, according to its natural figure, and then place the splint, and the bandage, they do not move.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if it has been strained, and if you let it rest, then return to your care and yours; the bandage is made in this way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	It is necessary that you wrap the ankle with a bandage doubled in half or three times, and remove any excess, then bend the leg until the heel reaches the root of the nail, and place one end of the thread between the calf and the leg, loosening the knee joint of the leg; then bend and wrap the leg and the calf with the bandage, then put on the brace and ankle strap, and put one end of the leather between the leg and the calf to make the lacing even, then start tying three or four turns on the brace; and as more threads you use, less the leg is tightened; then take out the two ends of the thread that you have tied between the leg and the calf, and with the three or four stays that are still on, go back to the ankle where the thread was tied, until you see the skin; the lacing, if it does not move from its place, then leave it as is, then let it be, then it will not tighten or swell anymore.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	If it happens, if it is not healed, and addresses what comes, as we have said many times; and if it has pieces of bone that prick, if it can be, then it can; and if it cannot, then it can be cut and drained, and the cure as we have said, as long as it is healthy.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And never is broken the cheekbone when it is set in its place, as we have said in the shoulder and arm; however, in the restoration that is made, it does not clash with the patient's pain.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And you should know that the cheekbone is restored in L years, or less than that, or more, according to the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	Of the right knee joint
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	It is said that in the right knee joint there is little breaking, but it often swells.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, if it is not much more than a fracture, or a puncture, and comes to all the wounds, and feels pain, and that feels okay.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is when you put back what has been dislocated as much as possible, until it is assembled as much as possible; then place the splint, and if you have a round staple, you can; then tighten all the adjustments that we have said for other fractures, such as apoplexy and other similar ones; if you put back to each accident what it comes to, as soon as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	Of the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	It is said that in the leg there are two bones, of which one is called by right not "mustelz", and the other is called "foscile"; and they all break in the same way as in the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as in the arm correctly, and the limbs are all mended. And if the two bones are broken together, then turn the leg around from all sides.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the small bones are broken, then turn forward.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bones are broken, then feel great pain and see that it is well; then turn around.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	Therefore, it is necessary to extend and place it evenly, and tie the threads evenly; but it should be noted that if the break is unsightly, and there are more pieces, then the extension should be smaller and lighter; and the thread according to your strength.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have completed your work, if you take two strips of wool that are twisted around the leg on both sides, and are long enough to reach from the knee to the ankle, then wrap them around the leg and tie them tightly, and at this point do not allow the leg to deviate to the right or left, and it is well; and no one has maintained the length of the leg, and it was made of wool, and he puts it on the leg to prevent movement, and it is properly made in the break or wound; and shake each leg every day to see if there is any swelling or other accident; if the cure is such that it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	Of the break of the bones so large
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no breaking of bones, but the large bones break never, and you must be careful not to break them in more positions.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	And if the large bones are broken and you see these bones sliding over each other, if you put your hand on the ground, it is like flying, and then put your foot on the leg that was injured, and lift the leg so that the bones return to their original position; then press gently until they become firm in their place; then put the splint and stitch, and make a small table for the large bone at the shoulder plains, then draw it towards the shoulder, and when you have covered the wound with bandages and other things that you know, then.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	When three or four days have passed, if the bone is not healed, you will find the bones unevenly broken, dislocated.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	If there are any of the two fractures remaining, if they are repaired, as we have said, then on the other one put a splint according to the length of the bone; and make it wider at the end, then make the socket that I mentioned thinner; and if there are two or three, or more, fractures, if you put one on each according to its quantity, enveloped in one layer of linen, and draw out the socket from the point of the bone; and let it be situated at the top of the chest, so that it covers the belly of the socket.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	It is necessary that you do not neglect the other things that I have said for other injuries, as we have said; and treat each accident as it comes up.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the fracture of the bone of the point
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the woman's bone is broken, if it is set in place, then it leans towards the side of the shoulder, and is held by the arm; then fill the nature of the wound with lint, and put it in as much as it can hold; then bend the woman, and gently raise the shoulder a little at a time, until the cotton comes to the entrance of the nature, and returns with the lint; and when she sees pus, if the cotton holds it, and when she has seen it, put on a bucket of blood, and tie a catheter to the urethra, and blow all the blood into the nature; then form the catheter in the nature, as the blood is emptied from the bucket: the nature will restore the fracture; then fill it with cotton, and leave it for several days until it is sound.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	When the bone of the elbow is broken, or of the woman, if it is restored as we have said in the elbow of the arm; and these breaks are not well concealed that those who study and use it, and read my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break signifies in more ways than one the right way of restoration: understand the question.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the meantime, when it is broken, take an ostrich's gape and bite the verge; then wrap around drapes, and leave it three times or more outside, and it will be healthy immediately.
de brisure avec plaie	Of a fracture with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is necessary for the one who has a fracture with wound, even if it is large, as the bone of the shoulder or elbow or appearance, that he be healthy now, if the wounds that we have said testify to it.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the healthy wound is, if the vitrol is not coming out, then continue to restore the fracture at the same hour, or the next day, if you are not able to come.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if you are not able to come the next day, leave the restoration until the next day, as long as you are calm and do not touch it again on the third or fourth day, because you will cause bad luck.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	If the bone is broken, it is separated at the point discovered, and if you want to put it back in place gently with your hands, at a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extension is not easy to put back in place with your hands, if the clamp has this instrument which is of iron, which has seven or eight turns, and the width is according to the size of the wound; and for this it is necessary to pierce three or four times, according to how much there is to do in each compression of the fracture; and so it should be firm and a little thick, so that it does not slip at the compression of the member in your hand, and so on the front, and thick ahead, in this way:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "bandage", because it aims that the edges of the head be placed on the top of the bone; and the bite once, as often as it rises, and be even with the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is not obvious, and the strings cannot well grasp the bone, then it comes that you cover the top of the bone with the string as much as it has power.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring the bone back, as we have said, if you cover it with an instrument that is suitable for this, or sharp and thin, then use this which is made of rough and small particles.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	When the bone is reset, and the patient feels great pain afterwards, it indicates that there is something wrong with its natural state.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If you stretch it as much as it can be in its place, then wrap it with a piece of black vinyl gloves, and properly do it; and do not put anything on the wound or elsewhere, except oil, so that it does not cause fever and corruption; then apply ointments after resetting the bone, and leave the wound exposed, and cover it thoroughly according to the size of the wound, and take good care that the wound is not stretched with the fracture; and many times it has happened that the patient has died or corroded, and has caused other wounds; and the stitching will be softer and more moist than the others.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	When the wound is large or severe, and you doubt that it will heal, as we have said, and you feel pain in the leg, but cannot move the limb; then encircle the leg, around the wound, tie tightly with cords, and support it.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	When you see after the first or second day that the wound is healing, and if all that you have placed on it is beneficial for healing wounds, and if the ointment is effective and similar to what you have used.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	It is necessary that you stretch the limb twice a day, in the morning and evening, as long as it is painful and healthy.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	It is necessary that the limbs are straightened in a way that the bow can be easily moved.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	If they persist, and the bow cannot be held back, but moves forward, it is necessary that you try to hold the wound with a tent, and all these pieces that cause the pain should be realigned.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	If an abscess comes to the limb, or in any other way of corruption, if you must cure it, according to what is said in this chapter before.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	If the bone is broken and exposed through the limb, as if it were the bone of the thigh or shoulder, and other similar bones of the large limbs, if not treated immediately, because many times it comes to death but leaves it until it pusses; by chance, heal after 20 or 30 years, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	The first sentence to translate is: "des brus qui viennent sour la souffrance
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	We come often after the healing of the fracture, and at the same time when it is near to the joint, and it is strange to see the limb in such a position; and by chance it cannot make the limb its own shape.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	If the wound is fresh: if you apply medicines such as aloes, incense, and myrrh, and sarcrolle, and others, if you choose none of these things or all together, and mix them with warm ointment or with a large amount of urine or with honey; and put them on the wound in spoons, and draw it well, and do not let it drip from your hands; and then draw it out, and continue another one as long as the sutures are intact; or you draw out a piece of plaster well made; because the property of the plaster is that it holds all the flaps of the members; and when the suture is converted into firmness also like a piercing, and it is bound with the cloth, and the surplus is removed; or you let it be to any rasping, as long as it is intact, and the cure as long as it is healthy.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	A weak limb that is after the cast
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the bone fracture is restored, and weakens after the weak limbs and subtly, if it comes from causes: whether one is because it was cut too tight, and not as it should have been; or because it had too many screws, and could not come to the member; or due to excessive swelling; or due to too large movements, not in its time; or because there is little blood in its chest, and is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient bite on the mouthpiece, and tighten the chest as much as possible without multiplying in it; then give him a bath, and relax him; then put poultice on the limb, if it attracts the great contraction, and the swelling often becomes acute, as the contraction approaches the member; and then return to its natural figure.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	A dislocated limb after the healing process.
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limb is swollen after rehabilitation, and the bones are broken open, and the shape of the dislocated limb is distorted, it does not return to its natural state: if one does not believe those who say that the bone must be broken completely at first, and many others have done this in our land; and these fractures cause great pain, and by chance the death occurs; however, if the wounds and tortures are fresh, and if they can be washed with hot water, or herbs softening are cooked, as cold compresses, and roots, and honey, and similar things; and I apply a softening ointment, as well made as dyaquilon, and take the greasy part of vismalve, and cook it with lard or oil of sage, and apply; or take fat figs and roast them with hemp seed, and similar medicines that dry the sweat.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	There is no instance of the nodation being tightened continuously and long with wet hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	And let there be movement in the limb every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the twisting is awakened and becomes painful, like an incision, and there is need for the ostetor to be strong, then it is necessary to cut deeply and lightly so as not to reach the bone; and it should be studied in the treatment.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	This begins the book of dislocations.
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to none, if it comes now to bring sense to the target.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if we delay, if we read it, and by chance reset it on the shoulder; for it does not come to move the eye as it is inflamed: many times brought pain and other pains; always, when this happens, if I make the patient healthier, then I let it be, until the abscess is closed and calmed; then raise the limb with hot water and oil, then reset it gently, and cure each member as I have cured it in its shoulder.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	I have ordered the surgeons for the dislocations of the shoulder bones.
des mandibules	for the mandibles
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	There are times when the mandibles are dislocated, and the dislocations of both sides are in two ways: either they are a little bone from their teeth, and become smooth; or they are completely dislocated, and hang down towards the cheek, and close the mouth, and cannot hold back saliva from the mouth, and wrap the tongue with the speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, it returns through the more various positions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	When it is complete and accomplished, if you reset it firmly and without force, and in such a way that the surgeon marks the patient's head with the tool, and cuts one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the mandible that covers the mouth, if the other two hands are deformed, to make them equal; and commands the patient to smooth his jawbones and move them from all parts.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And the surgeon makes them equal, as they should be in their place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And if the patient is reset, it should be done gently, just as the jawbones are assembled, using hot and oily ointments until they are lightly reset; do not force the patient to be reset, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	When they are properly realigned, and the patient's mouth feels quite relaxed, then place soft cloths on both sides of the mouth, made of oil of rosemary and wax, and gently tie them with ribbons; let the patient sleep on his back, and his head between two pillows, so that he does not move to the right or left, nor force himself to breathe, but chew light meat, as long as the pain is steadfast and does not affect the jaw; then take what he sees lightly, and do not try to open his mouth with his teeth and drink, as long as the jaw is well soothed and healthy.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	1. And if the two jaws cannot be set in place at once, and are not converted to their proper form, then if fevers and chills come on, and by chance the abdomen becomes distended, and by chance vomiting of clear bile occurs.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	2. And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times died those who came upon it in nine years.
de la forcelle	3. of the force.
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	4. The force cannot be dislocated due to the cost of continuing the work and the pain, and it is always dislocated once in the defense, and it is felt by everyone.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	The patient should lie on their back if they have pain in their shoulder and extend their arms; then press the shoulder joint against your palm, and it will return; then use the splint and bandage, and pull it; and the head that is towards the elbow cannot be reduced; however, if it cannot be reduced at all, and if it cannot be reduced once, then as we have said, lie on your back, and use the splint and bandage, and command the shoulder to rest until it is healthy; and then, when the head of the shoulder is dislocated, bring it back to its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	Of the shoulder dislocation
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	There are three ways in which the shoulder is dislocated: either it is dislocated at the part of the shoulder socket; or it is dislocated at the part of the deltoid muscle; or it is dislocated at the part of the humerus, and this happens rarely; or it does not dislocate at all from the shoulder, and neither does it dislocate from the nerves; and more often it dislocates forward towards the socket, and especially for those who have little strength, because they fall very hard; for those who have enough strength, they fall on their sides, and return to their sides.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And by chance, it happens to some men that they are struck or injured, and the spine of an abscess is broken, and take care that it is not dislocated by this.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	It is therefore necessary that you try it, as long as you are certain; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	And it is known that dislocations occur when moved towards the shoulder, and there is a difference between the diseased and healthy shoulder; you will find this difference manifestly between them; you will find at the top of the shoulder a hollow, and at the bottom of the shoulder the top of the shoulder, as if it were some ones; and he cannot bring his hand to her nipple, nor move any movements; and thus, if it is dislocated above, if it is not hidden, because you see it manifestly at the bottom; and this way of dislocation is not easy to return, when it is new, or if it is painful to the patient.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	The manner is that the minister gently places his hand on the shoulder of the patient, then puts his fingers at the joint, and gently strengthens it at the top of the arm; the minister then extends his hand and places it above, and if it comes quickly.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said in our hands a few hours later, and the patient is bathed in hot water; and the patient is gently relaxed and soothed, as a decoction of aloe and fenugreek and honey in hot water, and is soothed; then the patient is placed on his back, and a pillow is placed under his head, neither too soft nor too hard, then the patient's foot is placed on the pillow, and the shoulder muscle is gently relieved by the hand of the physician, and other physicians trace the shoulder muscle, so that it does not move; this shoulder now returns, and if you see that the ramorner follows this manner: and it is that you make present to the head which is greater than the shoulder; and it is turned towards the cost, and bend the shoulder away from the shoulder of the physician, and gently raise the shoulder above, so that the shoulder hangs in the arm; and other physicians trace the hand of the physician upwards towards the belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	If the patient is too light, if there is nothing heavy for them to bear with it, then the dislocation returns now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	If it is not in this way: and then take the bandage of two arms of great and four of wide, which can enter through the anus at front of the seat, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie the head on the pillow, that it may not be hurt by the maid, then place the other arm on the pillow; extend your arm over the long bone, and hold the shoulder of the hand with the other hand, and the elbow of the arm at the wrist, then put the arm in a hook of a large glove, and extend the hands on the other side, and let the chest hang down from another part: the joint now fits together.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.	And when it is in place, as it should be, if you happen to put the glove on the other side, then put a thread of wool even, then sprinkle powdered cinnamon with incense and almond oil all over the shoulder and the back, then pull the glove off the shoulder, turn the linen on the thread, and bind the hand on its own, and let the hands remain still.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he drinks little at first, as the limbs are comforted, for it heals faster; and then he drinks more after the days or weeks, and moves it; and if it is tight and does not soften, it is healthy.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint is tight due to moisture that came, or for another reason, then it is necessary that you administer cauterizations at three intervals, as it is placed before or in the chapter of cauterizations.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and after seven weeks, the joint does not hold, and cannot lift the arm forward, then it is necessary that you suspect that the nerve at the top of the shoulder is compressed or extended or softened; and suspect that the joint will never become loose in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The first line of the translation is: "The dislocation that is towards the toe, and the knees, or the hip, if it is made by force, and stretching of hands, and it is treated at another time; and it is cured as soon as it is healthy.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And after the cure comes pain in the limb, and then movement, if the patient uses cold water many times, as long as the pain is alleviated, and it returns to its original state.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the costly dislocation
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	It is said that the expensive joint is dislocated and re-dislocated many times, and it becomes dislocated from all sides, and even in front and behind, and the dislocation is not well set, because it can be seen and felt; and it becomes dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the male member with the female, if it appears open.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the union is weak, and cannot grip the arm, nor touch the shoulder with anything.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary to reset it always with the aid of the hand and leg, for if it is not reset with the aid of the hand and leg, it would be difficult to return; and by chance it cannot be returned at all, even when it is in its place; rather than other dislocations, and it is more painful, and by chance it comes to death.

Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the sign is that if the ankle is lax, and before reaching the part where it is dislocated: the fingers are light, and it should be gently extended by the hands when it is only loose.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is completely dislocated, if you manage to sit the patient right, and hold the ankle with your leg; then take the knee of the patient in your left hand, and then in the right, and stretch it up, and pull it gently but firmly on the knee; and do this twice, as we have said, by bending and pulling the knee, if it returns, that is good; if not, if it does not return, continue the treatment, for it will return; and if it cannot return, then hold the patient's shoulder with your hand on the ground, and firmly close the heel between the thighs, and tie it securely with a cloth or bandage, so that the ankle does not slip; then mark the position of the heel with your hand, and other hands extend the knee to the patient's hands or the lien; then extend them equally, and the knees will be held between the ankles to hold the ankle when it is extended; then place the dislocation in your hands, and mark the healthy leg at the opposite end, and the dislocation will return suddenly.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	When the dislocation occurs, if it is treated with plaster and bandages, and the limb is formed, and the patient lies down on the leg, and wraps the nerves that are under the ankle joint, so that the ligaments do not become too tight; then it is left alone for II or III days, and if the ligaments relax, then it is untied; then it is tied again at the end of the third or fourth day, and the patient is allowed to walk on it for IV days; and if it does not improve by this time, it is not a serious injury.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess forms, it comes; then it is necessary to open it, if as we have said, it is healthy.
des dois	Of two, one
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When both are dislocated, if they can be extended well in the work, it is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in no doubt or pain, then it is a light thing. Then make the patient lie on the affected side or on the other, and place your foot on what is open from these joints, and press with your foot on this until it returns; and when it is equalized, and there is no opening, then place the sole of your foot on the head of the dislocation, and form a table, and hold it for three days, and then let go; and then make the patient rest, as long as they are in pain.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	Of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and it is seen to be restored, often the patient dies: if you are not presumptuous in the cure, whether you are skilled in the art and have not used it long, or whether you are merciful and pitiful and slow, do not be presumptuous; and begin with calming measures at the onset of the wound, and leave the patient in God's hand, if you see no hope of health; and when you see hope, then immediately set the limb to the legs, unless the wound is swollen and bleeding; and when the limb is at the leg, if it is swollen and bruised, then apply calming measures and treat the wound, as required by simple diseases; and if there is a break with the dislocation, and the bones are broken, then follow what we have said in simple diseases, and do not enter into the way of despair, according to what we have said, for this is good according to your Creator, and for the wisdom of your heart.
